# Changelog

## Unreleased

### Added

- **A daemon restart is now transparent to a connected agent — strict-mode read-tracking and the pinned workspace survive it.** `plumb serve` already kept the client connected across a `plumb daemon` restart and replayed the `initialize` handshake, but all daemon-side per-connection state was in-memory and lost: in strict mode the first `edit_file` after a restart was refused with "has not been read in this daemon session" until the file was re-read, and a client that reports no roots (e.g. Claude Desktop) came back unpinned. `plumb serve` now generates a stable per-process **proxy session ID** (`crypto/rand` UUIDv4), injects it into the captured `initialize` frame's `params._meta["dev.plumbkit/proxy-session-id"]` (alongside the existing allow-dirs, via a single combined injector), and replays it on every reconnect. The daemon persists read-tracking (path → mtime + content SHA, scoped by `(proxy session, workspace)`) and the pinned workspace to a new `session_state.db` (in the data dir, beside `stats.db`; a dedicated store, **not** the drop-on-overflow stats writer), keyed by that ID. On reconnect the fresh daemon recognises the continuation and rehydrates: a strict-mode edit of an unchanged file read before the restart now passes, and an unpinned reconnect re-pins itself. **Safe by construction** — a rehydrated read still flows through `checkStrictRead`'s on-disk `os.Stat`+mtime comparison, so it can only satisfy a byte-identical file, never bypass a dirty-file check; workspace-scoping means a re-pin to a different project never resurrects the old project's reads; in-flight **writes** are still never auto-replayed. Controlled by `[session].persist_state` (default on; env `PLUMB_PERSIST_SESSION_STATE`) and `persist_state_ttl_minutes` (config-only, default 24h; `0` disables pruning), the latter reclaiming state left by a serve proxy that died without reconnecting, independent of `eviction_ttl_minutes`. Guarded by the `internal/sessionstate` store tests (round-trip incl. nanosecond mtime fidelity, per-session isolation, workspace-scoping, TTL prune), `ReadTracker` sink/`Hydrate` tests, `mcp.TestProxySessionFromParams`, the serve-side `TestInjectInitMeta_*`/`TestNewProxySessionIDFormat` tests, and the `internal/cli` `TestPersist_*` restart-survival/isolation/repin/pin-rehydration/disabled tests.

### Fixed

- **The dashboard's lifetime "Token Efficiency" block now shows the capability-vs-efficiency split instead of a permanently-full bar.** Both block-grids in the Dashboard Token Efficiency panel rendered `tokenSavingsBar`'s progress-toward-1.5M-tokens fill: the left grid against current-daemon savings (meaningful, it varies), but the right grid against the all-time lifetime total — which is virtually always far above the 1.5 M target, so it saturated to 100% bright after the first busy session and conveyed nothing (it looked identical for every heavy user). The right grid now renders the honest capability/efficiency composition it already captions (`tokenSavingsSplitRow`): every column is lit, apportioned by each axis's share of the lifetime total (a non-zero axis always shows at least one column; zero total renders dim), capability in the success colour and efficiency in the accent colour, with the `cap`/`eff` caption words colour-matched as a legend. The left grid, the compact header meter, and `tokenSavingsBar` itself are unchanged. Guarded by `TestSplitGroups` (apportioning, slivers, clamping, sum-to-groups) and `TestTokenSavingsSplitRow` (column count, per-axis colour counts, dim empty row).
- **Topology DB `busy_timeout` and `foreign_keys` now apply to every pooled connection, so `ON DELETE CASCADE` actually fires.** `openDB` opened the SQLite database on a bare path and set `PRAGMA busy_timeout`/`foreign_keys` via `db.Exec` — but those are PER-CONNECTION pragmas, and `database/sql` pools connections (the background indexer's writes run concurrently with read-tool queries on the shared handle). Only the one connection that happened to serve the `Exec` had foreign keys enabled; every other pooled connection ran with `foreign_keys = OFF`. Edge cleanup relies entirely on cascade (`deleteFileNodes`/prune delete only `topology_nodes`, never `topology_edges`), so a delete that landed on an FK-off connection silently left the file's edges behind — orphan `topology_edges` accumulated on every re-index/prune, and `busy_timeout = 0` on those connections turned recoverable writer contention into an immediate `database is locked`. The three pragmas now travel in the DSN (`_pragma=busy_timeout(5000)&_pragma=foreign_keys(1)&_pragma=journal_mode(WAL)`), which the driver applies on every new connection — matching how `internal/stats` already opens its database. Guarded by `TestOpenDB_PragmasApplyToEveryPooledConnection` (forces four concurrent pooled connections and asserts `foreign_keys=1`/`busy_timeout=5000` on each).
- **Semantic edits (`replace_symbol_body`/`insert_before`/`insert_after`/`safe_delete_symbol`/`rename_symbol`) now take the per-path write lock and write through a unique temp file, closing a lost-update / torn-write race.** `applyTextEditsToFile` read the file, applied the edits, and wrote `<path>.tmp` then renamed — with no `lockPath`, unlike `write_file`/`edit_file`. Because the daemon dispatches tool calls concurrently across connections, a `replace_symbol_body` racing an `edit_file` (or two symbol edits) on the same file could each read the same pre-edit content and silently overwrite the other's result, breaking the documented "per-path locks across all write tools" guarantee. Worse, the temp name was a fixed `<path>.tmp`, so two concurrent writers to one file wrote and renamed the *same* temp — corrupting or truncating it. The apply path now acquires the per-path lock and writes through `safeWrite` (uniquely-named temp + atomic rename, symlink-aware), with the lock taken/released per file so a multi-file `rename_symbol` never holds two locks at once (no lock-ordering deadlock). Guarded by `TestApplyTextEditsToFile_ConcurrentNoLostUpdate` (8 concurrent prepends must all survive; runs under `-race`).
- **`find_replace` no longer reads or writes through an in-tree symlink that points outside the workspace, and now warns when the `max_files` cap truncates the result.** (1) Every other write tool boundary-checks each resolved target path, but `find_replace` checked only the root argument — a directory walk that encountered a symlink to an external file would `safeWrite` *through* it (the resolver follows the link), silently mutating a file outside the pinned workspace and defeating the by-construction PathPolicy write boundary. The per-file worker now `Lstat`s each candidate and, for a symlink, runs the symlink-resolving boundary check (only a symlink can escape a walked in-boundary root, so regular files pay nothing), skipping any whose target lies outside the workspace — closing both the write escape and the dry-run preview's read of an external target. (2) When more matching files existed than `max_files`, the response reported `N file(s) changed` with no hint that the cap had silently dropped the rest; it now appends a `⚠ reached max_files=N — additional matching file(s) were NOT modified` warning, and the candidate list is sorted so the budget *prefers* the lowest-path files (this only biases the selection — the parallel workers race on the budget counter, so the truncated set is not guaranteed identical between a preview and the apply). Guarded by `TestFindReplace_SkipsSymlinkEscapingWorkspace` and `TestFindReplace_WarnsOnMaxFilesTruncation`.
- **The web UI's `GET /api/settings` no longer leaks the configured `semantics.api_key` in its response.** The settings model serialised every registry field's resolved value verbatim, and `semantics.api_key` is a registered string field — so the literal embedding-provider key was echoed into the JSON response body (landing in browser memory/devtools), even though the endpoint is loopback+token gated and the MCP `agent_config` path deliberately excludes it. The config field registry gains a `Secret` flag; `semantics.api_key` is marked secret, and the web settings surface now redacts secret fields to a fixed mask sentinel (`••••••••` when set, empty when unset) instead of the literal value. Because the settings are editable (`POST /api/settings`), the write path also treats an incoming value equal to the mask as an unchanged no-op, so a blind form re-submit can never round-trip the mask into the stored config. The TUI's local settings display is unaffected (it does not serialise to a client). Guarded by `TestSettings_RedactsSemanticsAPIKey` and `TestSettingsSet_RedactedSentinelIsNoOp`.
- **An untrusted project `.plumb/config.toml` can no longer widen the filesystem-access allowlist or redirect the semantics embedding endpoint/credentials.** A cloned hostile repo shipping `[workspace] extra_roots = ["/"]` previously gained read-WRITE access outside the pinned workspace the instant a session attached — no confirmation — defeating the "a write outside the workspace is refused by construction" invariant; and `[semantics] provider/base_url/api_key_env` turned a routine `topology_search` into an SSRF + environment-secret-exfiltration primitive (the resolver runs `os.Getenv` on the attacker-named variable and the client POSTs it as a bearer token to the attacker-named URL). `LoadProject` already forced `agent_config_writes`/`[web]`/`[ui]` back to the trusted global base for exactly this "a cloned repo ships it" threat model; it now also forces `[semantics]` and `[workspace] extra_roots`/`read_roots` back to base, closing the filesystem-boundary escape and the semantics SSRF/exfil vector while leaving benign per-project overrides (e.g. `edits.rate_limit_per_minute`) intact. These roots are global-only — set them in global config — consistent with the `agent_config` tool already treating them as un-writable, and the TUI Settings now shows `extra_roots`/`read_roots` only in the Global scope (a workspace-scope override would never take effect). Guarded by `TestLoadProject_ForcesUntrustedSecurityFieldsToBase`.
- **`git`-tool network-tier hardening: protected-branch force-push enforcement and ad-hoc-URL refusal across `push`/`fetch`/`pull`.** (1) `checkPushProtection` only treated `-f`/`--force` as a force push, so `git push origin +main` (git's `+`-prefixed refspec force form) bypassed the protected-branch guard; a `+`-prefixed positional refspec now also counts as a force. (2) The protected-branch match is lexical, so a force push that targets the current branch *without naming an explicit safe destination* — `git push origin +HEAD`, a bare `git push -f origin` (push.default), or `git push -f -o ci.skip origin` (a value-taking push option that shifts naïve positional parsing, so the remote was misread and the force allowed) — must be caught without resolving git's symbolic HEAD. The guard now refuses a force push, when any branch is protected, **unless it names an explicit destination refspec whose target branch is neither protected nor `HEAD`** (safe-bias, robust to arg parsing: the remote is identified with push flag-value arity awareness — `-o`/`--push-option`/`--repo`/`--receive-pack`/`--exec` consume the following arg — and a force with no provably-safe destination is *rejected*, not allowed). (3) The ad-hoc-URL/remote-helper refusal — which blocks the `git fetch ext::sh -c <cmd>` RCE vector — was applied only to `push` and matched only `ext::`; it now covers **every** network subcommand and any generic `<transport>::` helper form. All opt-in (require `allow_push` + `confirm`). Guarded by `TestCheckPushProtection` (force `+main`/`+feature:main`/`+HEAD`/bare-`-f`/`-o ci.skip origin`/`+main:feature`, generic `::` helper, plus the allowed `+feature`/`+HEAD:feature`) and `TestCheckPushProtection_NetworkSubcommandURLRefusal`.
- **The stats and session-state SQLite databases now actually apply `busy_timeout` and WAL.** `internal/stats` and `internal/sessionstate` opened their databases with the mattn-style `?_busy_timeout=5000&_journal_mode=WAL` DSN params — which the **modernc** driver this project uses *silently ignores* (verified: that DSN yields `busy_timeout=0`, `journal_mode=delete`). So both ran with no busy timeout and in rollback-journal mode rather than WAL, defeating WAL's concurrent-reader benefit (the stats read-only handle vs the writer) and turning any lock contention into an immediate `database is locked` instead of a 5s wait. Both now use the `_pragma=busy_timeout(...)&_pragma=journal_mode(WAL)` form the driver honours — the same fix #122 applied to topology (whose note mistakenly cited stats as already correct). Guarded by `stats.TestOpen_AppliesBusyTimeoutAndWAL` and `sessionstate.TestOpenAt_AppliesBusyTimeoutAndWAL`.
- **`config.Save` no longer bakes an active `PLUMB_*` environment override into `config.toml`.** `Save` loaded the config via `Load`, which applies the env overlay, then re-encoded the whole struct — so changing one global setting in the TUI (e.g. the log level) while, say, `PLUMB_WRITE_RATE_LIMIT` was set silently persisted that transient env value into the file as if the user had chosen it, where it then outlived the env var. `Save` now loads via `loadForSave` (compiled defaults + the on-disk file only, **no** env overlay), so a full-struct save can never write an environment override back into the file. (Single-key writes already had the sparse, env-free `SetGlobalValue`/`SaveTheme` path; this closes the whole-struct path that the other global Settings rows use.) Guarded by `TestSave_DoesNotBakeEnvOverride`.
- **The semantics embedding clients now bound the response body they read, so a misbehaving or hostile endpoint cannot OOM the daemon.** `openAICompatible.Embed` and `cohere.Embed` did `io.ReadAll(resp.Body)` with no size cap; the `http.Client` bounds time, not bytes, so an endpoint could stream an arbitrarily large body within the timeout and force the shared daemon to allocate it all into one slice (remotely triggerable when, before the companion fix, a project `[semantics] base_url` could point the client at an attacker URL). Both now read through a shared `readCapped` (`io.LimitReader`, 16 MiB cap) and treat an over-limit body as an error, so `topology_search` falls back to its FTS5 baseline rather than buffering an unbounded response. Guarded by `TestReadCapped`.
- **LSP supervisor: the OnStart-failure restart path no longer leaks two pipe FDs per attempt.** On an `OnStart` handshake failure the supervisor killed the process and called `proc.Process.Wait()` (`os.Process.Wait`), which does not close the `exec.Cmd`'s stdin/stdout parent pipe ends or join its IO goroutines — so a server that repeatedly fails its cold-start (a misconfigured rust-analyzer/jdtls) leaked two FDs per backoff attempt until GC. It now calls `proc.Wait()` (`exec.Cmd.Wait`), matching the normal-exit path. (`lsp-3`)
- **`git` tool: removed the unreachable `-c`/`-C` tokens from the `branch` classifier.** `classifyBranch` listed `-c`/`-C` (branch copy) as write-tier, but those short flags are rejected by the global-flag denylist (they collide with git's `-c`/`-C` config-injection flags) before classification ever runs, so the tokens were dead code implying a path that does not work. Branch copy is reached via the long `--copy` form, which is unaffected. (`toolsmisc-3`)
- **Episodic session summaries no longer count a FAILED mutation as a modification.** `buildEpisodicDetail` tallied every `edit_file`/`write_file`/`transaction_apply`/applied-`find_replace` call into `WriteN`/Touched/SourcePaths regardless of whether it succeeded, so a session whose write was rejected (rate-limited, dirty-file, boundary violation) was summarised as having modified files it never changed. Failed mutations are now excluded from the write tally and the touched/source-path lists (reads are still counted). Guarded by `TestBuildEpisodicDetail_ExcludesFailedWrite`. (`cli-1`)
- **`plumb stop` no longer risks signalling an unrelated process.** The pgrep fallback matched any process whose argv merely contained the substring `plumb daemon` (e.g. `vim plumb daemon.go`). Each candidate is now verified via `ps` to be a real `plumb daemon` (executable basename `plumb`, first arg `daemon`) before it is signalled. (`cli-3`)
- **The `[quality]` post-write analysis (golangci-lint findings appended to write responses) actually runs now — it was dead on arrival.** `buildWriteDeps` captured the quality runner eagerly: `if r := s.view().qualityRunner; r != nil { qualityReport = r.Report }`. But `buildWriteDeps` runs during tool registration (`handleConn` → `registerAllTools`), **before** the client handshake attaches the workspace and creates the runner (`startQualityRunner` at attach) — so the runner was always nil at capture, `WriteDeps.QualityReport` stayed permanently nil, and the whole feature silently never fired despite a green build (its unit tests exercise the `Runner` directly, never the wiring). The identical eager-capture-nil hazard was already fixed one line below for topology (`topologyNotify` resolves the store per-write) but missed for quality. `qualityReport` is now the same lazy closure, resolving `s.view().qualityRunner` on each write. Guarded by `TestBuildWriteDeps_QualityReportIsLazy`.
- **The web UI rejects a project-settings write to a non-workspace path, and no longer rejects every write when opened via `http://localhost`.** Two `internal/web` fixes: **(web-2)** `POST /api/settings` at a project scope passed `req.Scope` straight to `SetProjectValue`, so an arbitrary scope would drop a `.plumb/config.toml` at any path on disk; the scope is now validated against the currently-attached workspaces (`isActiveWorkspace`) and an unknown scope is a 400. **(web-3)** the CSRF same-origin guard compared the request Origin/Host against the bound `127.0.0.1:<port>` by exact string, so opening the UI via `http://localhost:<port>` (or `[::1]`) made every state-changing request fail as cross-origin; it now accepts any loopback host (127.0.0.1 / localhost / ::1) on the bound port while still rejecting a genuine foreign origin or a wrong port. Guarded by `TestSettingsSet_RejectsUnknownWorkspaceScope` and `TestSameOrigin_AcceptsLoopbackEquivalents`.
- **`GET /api/settings` masks credentials embedded in a URL-valued setting (e.g. `semantics.base_url`).** A `base_url` such as `http://user:pass@host` is user-typed config, not a dedicated secret, so it is intentionally not marked `Secret` (the user wants to see the endpoint) — but its embedded userinfo would otherwise be echoed verbatim into the settings response. The web settings surface now redacts the userinfo of any URL-valued field (rendering `http://redacted@host/v1`) while keeping the rest of the URL visible; non-URL and credential-free values are untouched. Guarded by `TestRedactURLUserinfo`.
- **A second connection attaching to a workspace can no longer roll back a live `transaction_apply` running on it from another connection.** `txlog.Scan` (orphan-transaction recovery) ran on every workspace attach/re-pin and unconditionally rolled back *every* `.plumb/tx-log/*` directory it found — with no way to tell a crashed-daemon orphan from a transaction that is in flight right now. Because the daemon is shared across connections, if connection A was mid-transaction (its tx-log dir on disk, files being written under per-path locks) when connection B attached the same workspace, B's `Scan` reverted A's already-written files to their pre-write snapshots and deleted A's log — silent partial corruption, with A still returning success. `Scan` now takes the daemon's start time as a cutoff and skips any tx-log directory whose manifest `StartedAt` is at or after it. To make that cutoff reliable, `writeManifest` is now **atomic** (unique temp + `rename`, fsync'd) — a `Record` during a live multi-file transaction rewrites the manifest on every step, and a concurrent `Scan` `os.ReadFile`-ing a half-written manifest would `Unmarshal`-fail, miss the `StartedAt≥cutoff` guard, and treat the live txn as a recoverable orphan; the atomic write guarantees a reader always sees a complete manifest (old or new), so the cutoff is never bypassed for a live transaction. A directory with an unreadable/absent `StartedAt` (a crash before the first manifest write, or a corrupt previous-run orphan) is still treated as a recoverable orphan. Guarded by `TestScan_SkipsCurrentRunButRollsBackOrphan` and `TestWriteManifest_AtomicUnderConcurrentScan` (a `-race` test running `Scan` concurrently with in-flight `Record`s).
- **A stalled language-server write no longer wedges every later LSP call, server notifications are delivered in wire order, and a cancelled call always reaches the server as `$/cancelRequest`.** Three JSON-RPC transport (`internal/lsp/jsonrpc`) concurrency fixes: **(lsp-1)** `Call` wrote the request synchronously while holding the write lock, so if the server stopped draining its stdin pipe (saturated/wedged, OS buffer full) the write blocked forever holding the lock — and because acquiring the lock *precedes* the ctx-aware response wait, the `[lsp_query]` deadline could not rescue it: every subsequent call on that connection hung. All writes now go through `sendCtx`, which performs the raw write in a goroutine and returns early on ctx-cancel or connection-close, and runs a stall watchdog: a write that blocks past `writeStallTimeout` (lowered to 15 s, kept distinctly below the default 30 s `[lsp_query]` deadline so a wedged write is torn down *before* the request times out rather than racing it) means a wedged server, so the connection is closed — unblocking every pending call with a clear error and letting the pool tear it down — instead of leaking the held lock. **(lsp-2)** server notifications were each dispatched in a fresh goroutine, so back-to-back `publishDiagnostics` for the same URI (the empty-then-real set gopls/rust-analyzer emit during indexing) could be reordered and leave the stale empty set winning, and a notification flood spawned unbounded goroutines; they now flow through a single in-order delivery goroutine fed by a bounded queue. **(lsp-4)** the cancel path had a CI-only deadlock: `Call` sent the request through `sendCtx(ctx, …)`, and when the write completed and `ctx` was cancelled in the same instant the watchdog `select` could pick `ctx.Done()` over the just-finished write and return `ctx.Err()` *before* the response-wait `select` ran — so `Call` returned without ever emitting `$/cancelRequest`, and a peer awaiting that frame blocked forever (only under scheduling load, so it deadlocked the cancel test under full-suite `-race` yet passed in isolation; reproduced locally with `GOMAXPROCS=1` and `-race -count`). `Call` now writes the request with `context.Background()` so cancellation flows solely through the response-wait `select`, which always runs after a successful send and emits `$/cancelRequest`; a ctx-already-cancelled pre-check avoids putting a doomed request on the wire. Guarded by `TestConn_WriteStallClosesConn`, `TestConn_NotificationsDeliveredInOrder`, and `TestConn_ContextCancel_AlwaysSendsCancelRequest_UnderLoad` (which pins `GOMAXPROCS=1` and fails on iteration 0 against the pre-fix code); all run under `-race`, and the existing `TestConn_Notify_ContextCancelUnblocks` still passes.
- **Topology read-only status handle now applies `busy_timeout` — the third instance of the modernc DSN bug (after #122/#133).** `StatusForWorkspace` (backing `topology_status` and the CLI status read while the daemon holds the writer) opened the index read-only with the mattn-style `?mode=ro&_busy_timeout=2000` DSN, which the modernc SQLite driver silently ignores, so the handle ran with `busy_timeout=0` — turning recoverable writer contention into an immediate `database is locked`. Switched to the `_pragma=busy_timeout(2000)` form. Guarded by `TestStatusForWorkspace_BusyTimeoutApplied`.
- **Web read endpoints now validate the `?workspace=` param against the active workspaces (read-side counterpart to the settings-write guard).** `/api/topology`, `/api/memory`, and `/api/memory/{name}` passed the raw `workspace` query value straight to `topology.StatusForWorkspace`/`memory.List`/`memory.Read` via `resolveWorkspace`, so a loopback+token-authenticated caller could read any on-disk path's `.plumb/` index or memories by naming it. `resolveWorkspace` now rejects an explicit workspace that is not a currently-attached session (the same `isActiveWorkspace` check the settings-write path uses), and the handlers return 400. Guarded by `TestReadEndpoints_RejectUnknownWorkspace`.
### Docs

- **Website and `AGENTS.md` trued up to the shipped code.** `site/index.html`: the adapter table and the LSP/"two engines" captions now show TypeScript/JS and Zig as **validated** (not experimental — both pass the real-binary integration tests since the `publishDiagnostics` capability fix); the Clients section advertises **thirteen** setup targets and adds the **Antigravity Desktop** chip; the seven tool-group badges now sum to the headline **55** (Read ×7→×8 for `file_status`, Edit ×12→×13 for `undo_edit`); and the footer version placeholder is bumped to v0.9.23. `AGENTS.md` (and its `CLAUDE.md`/`GEMINI.md` symlinks): the "Memory bounds" default soft heap limit is corrected from 4 GiB to the **1 GiB** the code actually applies (`defaultDaemonMemLimit`). Found by the autonomous review (`website-1/2/3/4/5`, `cli-2`).

## 0.9.23 (2026-06-29)

First tagged release. Automated cross-platform binaries — macOS (Intel + Apple Silicon) and Linux (Intel + ARM) — plus a Homebrew tap now ship from the release pipeline on every `v*` tag.

### Added

- **`edit_file` gains an anchor-bounded edit mode: replace the span between two unique anchors instead of an exact `old_string`.** As an alternative to the `edits` array, a call may pass `start_anchor` + `end_anchor` (two unique substrings/lines) and a `new_string` that replaces the span they bound; `include_anchors=false` (default) rewrites only the text *between* the anchors and keeps them as stable boundaries, `include_anchors=true` replaces the whole inclusive span. The two request shapes are mutually exclusive — `validateMode` rejects supplying both, or neither. Each anchor must match **exactly once** and `end_anchor` must occur after (and not overlap) `start_anchor`, with the same uniqueness/not-found errors as the `old_string` matcher; matching mirrors `str_replace` exactly — CRLF-tolerant and forgiving of a pasted display-only read_file gutter (`<n>\t`, multi-line consecutive prefixes), surfacing the same advisory note when a gutter is stripped. The mode lowers the anchors into a single synthetic `str_replace` edit (the full inclusive span, which carries both unique anchors and is therefore itself unique) and flows through the **same** write path as `edits` — per-path lock, `expected_mtime`/`expected_sha` guards, retry loop, LSP notify, cache invalidation, diff output, and write-rate budget — so only the span computation is new. Ideal for rewriting a block whose interior changes but whose boundary lines are stable. Guarded by `TestEditFileAnchor_*` (between/inclusive/empty-delete happy paths, not-found/ambiguous/end-before-start/overlap/both-modes/neither failures, gutter-aware, CRLF, and an existing-mode regression) and `TestBuildAnchorEdit_SpanIsUnique`.
- **The TUI Settings screen now exposes the `[memory]` Advanced Memory Engine knobs as editable rows.** The eight scalar/bool fields of `[memory]` (`enabled`, `generated_summaries`, `inject_hints`, `hint_budget_bytes`, `episodic_budget_bytes`, `max_hints`, `idle_summary_minutes`, `generated_memory_keep`) were settable only by hand-editing config TOML — every other config section already had Settings rows. They now appear under a new **Memory** group (toggles for the three bools, number rows for the five ints), wired through the same scope-aware persistence (global config or a workspace's `.plumb/config.toml`), reload-tier marker (next-session), and registry-stamped help as the existing rows. Backed by new entries in the config field registry (`internal/config/fields_registry.go`), so `plumb config show` and the agent-config validator see them too; `TestSettingsRegistryDrift` keeps the registry and the rows in lock-step. `intField`/`toggleLabel` were split (mirroring the existing `boolField`/`boolFieldMore`) to stay under the gocyclo-15 contract.
- **Self-heal recoverable tool errors instead of bouncing them back (data-driven from the most common live failures).** Three targeted recoveries, each completing the request (or giving a one-step fix) with a warning rather than a blind-retry round-trip: **(1) `edit_file` version-guard hint** — a stale `expected_mtime`/`expected_sha` is still **rejected** (auto-applying would clobber a concurrent change — optimistic concurrency is deliberate and the multi-session contract enforces it), but for an all-anchor-based batch the rejection now names `reconcile: true` as the one-call escape hatch for the single-agent edit→format→edit loop. **(2) `git switch -c/-C`** is accepted by rewriting to `--create`/`--force-create` before the global-flag denylist — git's short create flags collide with the denylisted `-c`/`-C` config-injection vectors, so a legitimate `git switch -c <branch>` was refused; the rewrite is a pure synonym scoped to `switch` only (a non-switch `-c` stays denied). **(3) Misplaced-parameter relocation** in the dispatch guard — a DECLARED parameter put at the wrong structural level is moved to where the schema declares it: a top-level param sent inside an `edits[]` item is **hoisted** up (`expected_mtime` in an edit), and scattered top-level edit keys with no `edits` array are **wrapped** into one (`{file_path, old_string, new_string}` → `edits:[{…}]`). It only ever touches a key validation would otherwise hard-reject, so it can never alter an already-valid call, and it relocates exact names only (a genuinely unknown key still rejects). The published schema drops array-of-object params from `required` so a to-be-wrapped call reaches the daemon. Guarded by new `argguard`/`argschema`/`argrelocate`, `edit_file`, and real-git `switch` tests.
- **`rename_symbol` now appends a per-file unified diff to its response, gated by `[edits].show_write_diff` — closing the last write tool that returned only a name list.** PR #70 brought unified diffs to the symbol-edit tools and `transaction_apply`; `rename_symbol` was left reporting only "Renamed to … across N file(s)" with the changed paths, so a caller still had to re-read to see what an applied (or previewed) rename actually did. The tool now reconstructs each affected file's before/after by applying the server's per-URI `TextEdit`s to a copy of the file's current on-disk bytes — computed *before* the edits land, so the same code renders both the dry-run preview and the applied change — and renders a unified diff via the shared `unifiedDiff` helper. Volume is bounded: diffs are capped at 20 files with an "and N more file(s)" summary beyond that, and each diff inherits the existing 80-line per-file cap. The diff is best-effort presentation (a file that can't be read or reconstructed is silently skipped, never failing the rename), and `show_write_diff = false` restores the previous output exactly. The structural-fallback path is unchanged — it surfaces `find_replace`'s own match output, since its line-granular text edits aren't reconstructed here. Guarded by `TestRenameSymbol_AppliedShowsDiff`, `TestRenameSymbol_DryRunShowsDiff`, `TestRenameSymbol_ShowDiffGateOff`, and `TestRenameSymbol_MultiFileDiffTruncation`.
- **New `file_status` read tool — a content-free "did this file change under me?" probe.** For each input path it reports `git_dirty` (uncommitted vs git HEAD/index, untracked counts as dirty), `changed_since_plumb_wrote` (the on-disk mtime advanced since plumb last wrote it this session — a peer or external process edited it), `last_writer` (`plumb` = plumb wrote it last this session and it is unchanged; `external` = plumb wrote it but it has since changed; `unknown` = plumb has not written it this session), plus `mtime` and `size`. It reuses the components the write tools already maintain — the per-connection `WriteTracker` for the last-writer/recorded-mtime signal, the same `git status --porcelain` dirty check the write dirty-guard uses, and `os.Stat` — and adds no new infrastructure. Pure read tool: it never locks, writes, or notifies the LSP, missing files are reported rather than erroring, and it deliberately does **not** satisfy strict mode's read-before-edit requirement (a status probe is not a content read). Lets an agent confirm a cached view is still current before a blind re-read, and decide whether to refresh. Hidden under the lean profile (a read-only commodity, still callable by name). Guarded by `TestFileStatus_*`.
- **A session can now carry an optional human-readable `purpose` tag, so concurrent sessions on one workspace are tellable apart at a glance.** `session_start` accepts a `purpose` argument (letters, digits, and `-`; max 32 characters — an invalid value is rejected with a clear error, never silently dropped). The tag is persisted on the session record (`internal/session`), stamped on the session's stats rows (a new nullable `purpose` column on `tool_calls`, stats schema v12→v13, added via the existing idempotent ADD COLUMN migration so an old database upgrades cleanly and a fresh one carries the column), and surfaced wherever sessions are shown: the TUI session list (an unobtrusive ` · <purpose>` suffix), `daemon_info` (a `purpose:` line when set), and `workspace_sessions` (a ` (purpose: …)` marker on each active session). Everything is nil/empty-safe — an untagged session renders exactly as before. Guarded by `NormalisePurpose`, `SetPurpose`, `session_start` purpose-validation, `daemon_info`, the TUI `sessionPurposeTag`, and stats migration/round-trip tests. (Implemented against the current incremental-migration machinery in `internal/stats/db.go`; a separate open PR reworks that file, so a merge-time conflict there is expected and is the reviewer's to resolve.)
- **`plumb serve --allow-dir` grants extra read-write roots to a connection at launch, transported per-connection and surviving the resilient-proxy handshake replay.** Previously the only way to widen a session's write boundary beyond the detected workspace was project config (`[workspace] extra_roots` / `read_roots`, shipped in 0.8.29); there was no client-side, connection-scoped grant. `plumb serve` now accepts a repeatable `--allow-dir <path>` flag and reads `PLUMB_ALLOWED_DIRS` (OS-list-separated) — each entry `$VAR`-expanded and made absolute in the serve process, then folded into the captured `initialize` frame's `params._meta["dev.plumbkit/allow-dirs"]`. Because the resilient proxy captures and **replays** that exact frame on every reconnect, the grant travels with the handshake for free — a reconnected daemon re-applies it with no separate control message. The daemon adds them to the connection's `PathPolicy` as **read-write** roots, **additive** to the detected workspace and config `extra_roots` (never replacing the baseline), and `NewPathPolicy` canonicalises each (symlink-/firmlink-aware) so an allow-dir cannot be used to escape via a symlink. The grant is strictly per-connection — it lives only in that session's snapshot and is preserved across a workspace re-pin — so connection A's allow-dir never leaks into connection B. An empty list (no flag, no env) transports nothing and is byte-for-byte identical to today; the legacy byte-pump proxy (`--no-reconnect` / `PLUMB_PROXY_RECONNECT=0`) does not inject and warns if `--allow-dir` is passed. Guarded by `TestAllowDir_PerConnectionIsolation`, `TestAllowDir_PreservedAcrossRepin`, the `TestInjectAllowDirs_*` / `TestResolveAllowDirs*` proxy tests, and `mcp.TestAllowDirsFromParams`.
- **`get_definition` by name now falls back to the topology index when the language server is unavailable, so a cold/warming server no longer blocks navigation.** The LSP→topology degradation that already backs `find_symbol`/`workspace_symbols`/`list_symbols` now extends to `get_definition`'s `symbol_name` path: on any LSP error (the still-warming server is the common case) it resolves the name against the tree-sitter index and returns the declaration site, annotated `[topology fallback — … located by symbol name, declaration line not cursor offset. source=topology, mode=indexed-approximate]`. It is deliberately scoped: the fallback fires only on a hard LSP **error**, never on an authoritative "no symbol named…" answer (so a working server's negative result is never masked); the **raw-position** form of `get_definition` has no name to resolve and still surfaces the error; and `find_references`, the call/type hierarchies, and `rename_symbol` keep no fallback — they need a precise position or a whole-workspace reference graph the index does not hold. A dotted `ReceiverType.MethodName` retries on its final segment. Guarded by `TestGetDefinition_TopologyFallbackByName`, `TestGetDefinition_PositionPathNoFallback`, and `TestGetDefinition_NoFallbackOnAuthoritativeMiss`.
- **LSP cold-start is now observable, so a still-warming language server no longer reads as a silent multi-minute stall.** A heavy server (rust-analyzer running `cargo metadata` + sysroot load, a large gopls module, jdtls) can take minutes to finish its handshake on first attach; until it does, every routed semantic call returned a bare `LSP server not yet ready` (or, with the query timeout raised/disabled, blocked outright). Each `poolEntry` now records `startedAt` (set on first start and on each wake from hibernation), and the routing proxy exposes a resolution-only `WarmupStatus(uri)` (it never starts a server). The not-ready errors now fold in elapsed warm-up time and name the tools that answer immediately — `LSP server still warming for <root> (4s elapsed) — retry shortly (topology_search / find_symbol / file_outline answer now)` — and `session_start`'s recommended-first-step softens "LSP is available" into a warm-up advisory that steers the agent to the tree-sitter index meanwhile (it pre-empts the ready line, so an attached-but-cold server is never reported as ready). Guarded by `TestWarmupFor`, `TestWarmingErr`, `TestRoundWarmElapsed`, and the `session_start` warming-advisory tests.
- **Tolerant tool arguments: a high-confidence single-character typo in a parameter name is now auto-corrected instead of rejected, and the curated alias table is broadened.** The dispatch-path guard already rewrote known aliases (`query`→`pattern`, `filepath`→`file_path`, …) and warned; it now adds a tightly-gated second pass that promotes a near-miss to an auto-rewrite when the typed key matches a declared parameter at edit distance 1, the match is **unique** (no tie), the key is ≥4 runes (so a distance-1 match isn't coincidental), the target is currently unset, and the target is **not safety-critical** (`confirm`, `use_regex`, `replace_all`, `allow_dir`, `dirty_ok`, `overwrite_changed`, `reconcile`, `expected_mtime`/`expected_sha`, `subcommand`, `force` are never edit-distance-guessed — only exact aliases reach them). Anything looser stays the existing "unknown parameter … did you mean?" rejection, and the correction surfaces as a `corrected likely typo "namex" to "name"` warning, never a silent reshape. The curated table also gains `text`/`contents`/`body`→`content`, `start`→`start_line`, `end`→`end_line`, `msg`/`commitmessage`→`message`, `repository`→`repo`, and `subcmd`→`subcommand` (the new `content` target also drops `content` from the published `required` set, so a `write_file({text})` survives client-side schema validation). Guarded by new `argguard`/`argschema` cases (auto-correct, distance-2 reject-with-suggestion, safety-critical guard, short-key guard, ambiguous-tie reject).
- **`find_replace` now appends a per-file unified diff to its response, matching the write and symbol-edit tools.** PR #70 wired `[edits].show_write_diff` into `write_file`/`edit_file`/`transaction_apply` and the symbol-edit tools but deferred `find_replace`, so the one tool that can touch dozens of files at once still reported only a `path (count)` summary — forcing a follow-up `read_file`/`file_diff` to see what actually changed in a preview. `find_replace` now reuses the same `unifiedDiff` helper and the same `show_write_diff` gate (resolved via `WriteDeps.showWriteDiff()`), rendering a diff in **both** dry-run preview and applied modes. The volume is bounded: diffs are rendered for the first 20 changed files (`maxFindReplaceDiffFiles`) with a `+N more file(s)` summary beyond that, each file's pre-replacement content is captured only within the existing 200 KiB diff cap (oversized files are replaced but their inline diff is skipped), and each per-file diff keeps the shared 80-line hunk cap. When `show_write_diff` is off the output is byte-identical to before. Guarded by preview-present, applied-present, gate-off-suppresses, and multi-file-truncation tests.

### Fixed

- **`topology_affected` dropped all but one co-located test ([#87](https://github.com/plumbkit/plumb/issues/87)).** `TestsInDirs` (the co-located-tests recall booster) selected the test nodes but omitted `n.id` from its query and scan, so every returned `Node` had `ID == 0`. The caller dedups co-located tests via `g.seen[n.ID]` — a shared `map[int64]bool` — so all co-located tests collapsed onto key `0`: only the **first** test in a seeded directory was ever emitted (and a test that was both graph-reached and co-located appeared twice). For a changed directory with more than one test function — the common case — the headline "which tests to run" answer silently under-reported. Fixed by selecting and scanning `n.id` so co-located nodes carry their real IDs; the existing id-keyed dedup then works. Guarded by `TestTopologyAffected_MultipleColocatedTests` (three tests across two sibling files must all surface — fails against the old query). The secondary SQL-pushdown optimisation noted in the issue is intentionally left out.
- **URI↔path conversion is consolidated into Windows-safe `paths` helpers, replacing two divergent helpers and 60+ inline strip sites ([#67](https://github.com/plumbkit/plumb/issues/67)).** Path→URI conversion had a Windows-safe `protocol.FileURI` *and* a naive `toFileURI` (`"file://" + s`, which mangles drive-lettered Windows paths), while URI→path was hand-inlined as `strings.TrimPrefix(x, "file://")` at 62 sites across 29 files — none of which strip the leading slash from the `file:///C:/…` form. Both directions now route through one pair in the low-level `internal/paths` package: `paths.PathToURI` (lifting the correct `FileURI` logic) and the new `paths.URIToPath` (the Windows-safe inverse, a behaviour-preserving no-op on Unix). `protocol.FileURI` and the tools' `toFileURI`/`toFileURIAnchored` now delegate to them (the latter keeping its empty/relative/anchoring policy). A genuine cross-platform correctness fix plus a single choke point for any future change; behaviour on the supported platforms is unchanged.
- **Auto-mode now serves the *full* tool set to Claude Code, which otherwise could not reach lean-hidden tools at all.** The lean profile hides ~33 commodity tools from `tools/list` on the promise they stay *callable by name* via `tools/call` — but that escape hatch holds only for a client that can invoke a tool it was never advertised. Claude Code builds its tool list (and its ToolSearch deferred-tool list) solely from `tools/list`, so a hidden tool has no schema to load and is genuinely unreachable, not merely undisplayed: calling `search_in_files` returned "No matching deferred tools found", forcing the native-grep fallback the always-plumb rule forbids. `internal/clientcaps` gains a `SchemaDiscoveryOnly` capability (set on `claude-code`), and `autoProfile` returns `full` for any client carrying it. Codex and Gemini are left unflagged (still lean) until their invocation behaviour is likewise verified; an explicit `[tools] profile` or per-client override still wins. Guarded by `TestSchemaDiscoveryOnly` and the updated `TestResolveToolProfile`.
- **The reconnect note no longer tells an autonomous agent to "start a new client session" — an action it cannot take.** On a daemon/proxy version mismatch the one-shot reconnect note appended "this serve proxy is still ‹v› — start a new client session to refresh it". The resilient proxy already reconnects transparently and keeps tools registered, so the mismatch is harmless; the note now reports the two versions and suggests restarting `plumb serve` at the user's convenience instead of prescribing the impossible. `TestReconnectNoteText` updated to assert the new wording and the absence of the old.

### Changed

- **`tools/list` no longer applies `ToolFilter` (and reads each tool's name/description/schema) while holding the shared registry lock, keeping a lightweight liveness probe responsive under load ([#15](https://github.com/plumbkit/plumb/issues/15)).** `handleToolsList` held `s.mu` (read mode) across the whole response build — the per-tool name/description/schema reads *and* the `ToolFilter` call, which may resolve a client profile of unbounded cost. Holding the shared registry lock across that work needlessly serialised it against `Register` and every other `s.mu` reader, widening the window in which a queued `ping`/`daemon_info` liveness probe could stall behind a slow `tools/list`. The handler now snapshots the registry under `s.mu` into a local slice via the new `snapshotTools` helper — the lock covers only the cheap map reads — then releases the lock before applying `ToolFilter` and marshalling the response. Behaviour and wire format are identical (insertion order, hidden≠unregistered, schema fallback); only the lock's hold time changes. Guarded by `TestToolsList_FilterRunsWithoutHoldingLock` (a concurrent `Register` must complete while a parked `ToolFilter` runs — it deadlocks against the old lock-held-across-filter code), run under `-race`.
- **`session.Touch` no longer takes the directory-wide exclusive flock on every tool call ([#85](https://github.com/plumbkit/plumb/issues/85)).** `Touch` runs on the synchronous response path of every completed tool call but only sets one file's mtime (`os.Chtimes`); wrapping it in `withSessionDirLock` (`syscall.LOCK_EX` on the shared `.sessions.lock`) made every tool call across every session and process serialise on one global lock — and queue behind `List`'s long read-parse-stat scan, which shares that lock (TUI refresh, web UI, eviction reaper, `workspace_sessions`). `Touch` is now lock-free. It is race-free because it does no read-modify-write: `writeSessionFileAtomic`'s temp+rename guarantees `Chtimes` only ever observes a whole inode, so the worst case is a lost mtime bump (re-applied by the next tool call) or a transient `ENOENT` mid-rename — both harmless, and the error was already discarded. `FindEnded` already reads lock-free against the same writers. Added `TestTouch_ConcurrentWithWriters_NoCorruption` (race-tested).
- **Dropped the redundant `d.mu` lock from the stats episodic read methods ([#89](https://github.com/plumbkit/plumb/issues/89)).** `LatestEpisodic` and `ToolCallsForSession` took `d.mu` for pure reads while every reader in `db_query.go` does not — a misleading inconsistency. The lock guards only the writer's transaction/checkpoint critical sections; reads are already serialised by `database/sql` + `SetMaxOpenConns(1)` (the basis the 13 unlocked `db_query.go` readers rely on), and in production these two run on the separate `SharedReadOnly` handle (a different `*DB`, a different mutex), so the lock never prevented contention to begin with. Removed it from the two read methods only (the write-path `recordEpisodic` lock is untouched). Added `TestEpisodic_ConcurrentReadDuringWrite` (race-tested).
- **`SplitIdentifier` is now a single pass over the identifier instead of four allocating passes ([#86](https://github.com/plumbkit/plumb/issues/86)).** The shared FTS tokeniser (run once per symbol during a full resync of both the topology and memory FTS indexes) built its result through `strings.NewReplacer(...).Replace`, `[]rune`, an unhinted `strings.Builder`, and a final `strings.Join(strings.Fields(...))` to collapse and trim. Separator handling now folds into the boundary walk — separators and Unicode whitespace mark a lazily-emitted single space (never leading or trailing), the builder is capacity-hinted, and the `Replacer`/`Fields`/`Join` passes are gone. Output is byte-identical (an exhaustive `TestSplitIdentifier_MatchesReference` checks the new pass against the retained old implementation over every string up to length four across lower/upper-acronym/digit/separator/whitespace runes, plus realistic and multi-byte cases). On a representative identifier this cuts 11 allocations/792 B to 1 allocation/48 B and roughly halves the time. Supersedes #66 (the `NewReplacer`-hoist), which is no longer needed.
- **`plumb config show`/`print` no longer import the Bubble Tea TUI package for styling — an unwanted layering dependency.** `internal/cli/config.go` pulled in `internal/tui` purely to borrow a theme→chroma-style mapping (for `config print`'s TOML highlighting) and a handful of foreground styles for `config show`'s status glyphs and tables. Both now route through the render-neutral `internal/theme` palette catalogue (no lipgloss, no bubbletea): `config print` reads the chroma style via `theme.Get(name).ChromaStyle` (the palettes already mirror the TUI's chroma names exactly), and the status/table styles are rebuilt from `theme.Default` in a small `configstyle.go` helper. `config show` always rendered with plumb's default Plumb theme anyway — it never assigns `tui.ActiveTheme` — so the output is byte-for-byte unchanged; the redundant `tui.RebuildStyles()` call (already performed by the root command's `PersistentPreRun`) is dropped. `config.go` no longer imports `internal/tui`. Guarded by `TestConfigShowStyles_MatchTUIPlumb` (palette↔TUI Plumb colour + key-width parity) and `TestConfigPrintChroma_ParityWithTUI` (chroma-style parity across every theme), which fail on a future palette drift. Pure refactor; no behaviour change.

### Docs

- **The Topology guide's extractor list no longer claims `.ts`/`.tsx`/`.jsx` (and Swift) use the gotreesitter/regex path — it now matches the wasmts routing the code actually wires.** `docs/topology.md`'s "How it works" section still described the pre-migration arrangement: TypeScript (`.ts`) on the pure-Go gotreesitter runtime, TSX/JSX (`.tsx`/`.jsx`) "only" on a fast regex scanner, and Swift listed alongside the gotreesitter languages. In reality `buildExtractors` (`internal/cli/topology_pool.go`) routes `typescript` → `wasmts.NewTypeScript()`, `tsx` (owning both `.tsx` and `.jsx`) → `wasmts.NewTSX()`, and `swift` → `wasmts.NewSwift()` — all the canonical tree-sitter grammars compiled to WASM and run via wazero — with the legacy `internal/topology/extractors/typescript` regex scanner retained only as a wasm-init-failure fallback. The guide now says exactly that, consistent with the already-correct summary higher in the same file and with AGENTS.md. Documentation only; the `wasmts` and `langsupport` tests that validate the routing are unchanged and passing.

## 0.9.22 (unreleased)

Public website launch refresh: the modern landing page is now the published site, with refreshed logo-derived favicons and social preview assets. Plus review-pass fixes to the 0.9.17/0.9.18 write-tool, detection, proxy, and Linux-testing work.

### Fixed

- **The macOS daemon RSS reported peak memory (`Maxrss`), not the documented current sample — it now sources current RSS ([#62](https://github.com/plumbkit/plumb/issues/62)).** On macOS `readProcessMetrics` set `RSSBytes` from `Getrusage(RUSAGE_SELF).Maxrss`, which is *peak* RSS since process start: monotonic, never reclaimed after a GC or `FreeOSMemory`. That value flowed into `DaemonMetrics.RSSBytes`, which the TUI daemon widget and web UI render as the **current** RSS — overstating live memory, never reflecting idle-reclaim, and contradicting the documented contract that the RSS row is a current sample. `readProcessMetrics` now sources RSS from the same `ps -o rss=` path already used for child processes (which reports current RSS) for its own pid too, keeping CPU time from `Getrusage`. Darwin-only correctness fix; the cross-platform `processMetrics`/`DaemonMetrics` shape is unchanged.
- **The topology resync no longer re-parses every unchanged file before the staleness check discards it ([#58](https://github.com/plumbkit/plumb/issues/58)).** `processUpsert` read, hashed, **and** ran the expensive tree-sitter/AST parse (`extractPath` → `safeExtract`) *before* calling `isStale` — so on an up-to-date tree (the startup resync, the periodic fallback, and `resync_on_attach`) every file was fully parsed only for `isStale` to return false and the freshly-extracted nodes/edges to be thrown away: N parses for zero index changes. The read-then-parse is now split — `readAndHash` resolves the extractor, reads the file, and hashes its content (the content hash genuinely needs the read, to catch a backup-restore that resets mtime but changes content), and only once `isStale` confirms a changed mtime or hash does `extractFile` run `safeExtract` and `persistFile` land the result. All prior semantics are preserved exactly: the backup-restore hash detection, the no-extractor case (recorded with empty hash and zero symbols), the `skipOversizedGrammar` recorded-with-hash-zero-symbols case, and `recordFileError` on a read or extract failure; `Store.ExtractFile` (the symbol-edit fallback that always re-parses current content) is rewired through the same two helpers. Guarded by `TestIndexer_ProcessUpsert_SkipsParseWhenUnchanged` (a counting extractor proves the first index parses once, an unchanged resync parses zero more, and a content+mtime change re-parses).
- **Memory `Reindex` read every unchanged file twice ([#61](https://github.com/plumbkit/plumb/issues/61)).** `(*Index).Reindex` called `List`, which already reads each memory's bytes and computes its content sha256, then for *every* memory re-opened, re-read, re-stat'd, and re-hashed the file via `recordFromFile` before checking whether anything had drifted — so a steady-state reindex over unchanged files paid a second full read plus hash per memory for nothing. Reindex now consults the sha256 `List` already produced: it pre-loads the stored `name → content_sha` anchors in one query, and only re-reads (and upserts) a memory whose content drifted or that is absent from the index. The new/changed/removed paths are unchanged. Guarded by a regression test that counts file re-reads through a `readRecord` seam and asserts a steady-state reindex re-reads nothing while a changed file is still reindexed.
- **The TUI re-read the selected memory's body from disk on every render frame while the Memory section was open ([#59](https://github.com/plumbkit/plumb/issues/59)).** `currentMemoryBody` cached the body into `m.memoryBodyCache`, but the only path that reached it was the render chain (`render → renderMainBody → renderMemoryPanels → renderMemoryBody → memoryRightLines`), which runs on a throwaway value copy of the model — so the cache write was discarded and `memory.ReadBody` (file open + read + frontmatter split) ran on every keypress, mouse move, and 2-second poll. The cache populate now happens off the render path in a pointer-receiver step (`populateMemoryBody`, called from `refreshMemories` and from `Model.Update` on the model that is actually returned), and the render chain reads the already-populated cache read-only. Existing navigation handlers clear the cache, so one populating read after each invalidation suffices; the body still displays and updates on selection change. The same change also stops a latent re-read for genuinely empty-bodied memories (the cache hit no longer required a non-empty body).
- **The `plumb web` dashboard aggregated the stats DB twice per request and its log tail dropped recent lines ([#64](https://github.com/plumbkit/plumb/issues/64)).** Two independent defects on default request paths in `internal/web`. (1) `handleDashboard` ran `Summary(Filter{})` — a full-table aggregation over the stats DB — **twice** per request: once inside the top-tools helper and again inside the savings-breakdown helper, on the landing view served on every dashboard load and every SSE refresh. The two helpers now consume a single precomputed `[]stats.ToolStat` slice from one `Summary` call, halving the stats-DB scan per request for no change in output. (2) The log-tail SSE handler seeks ~8 KiB before EOF and drops the partial leading line so the client sees recent context immediately, but it dropped that partial line on a **throwaway** `bufio.NewReader(f)`; that reader's buffer fill pulled ~4 KiB off the descriptor and was then discarded, so the freshly built follow reader started ~4 KiB further in and silently skipped the recent lines the seek was meant to surface. The handler now drops the partial line on the **same** reader it then follows with, so the full tail window reaches the client. Both fixes are regression-tested (the log-tail test fails against the old throwaway-reader code).
- **The topology indexer's per-file FTS cleanup is now a single set-based delete instead of one DELETE per symbol, cutting M FTS5 round-trips to one on the hot write path ([#65](https://github.com/plumbkit/plumb/issues/65)).** `deleteFileNodes` runs on every upsert — every `edit_file`/`write_file`, every watcher-triggered re-index of a changed file, and per stale file in prune/delete — and it SELECTed every node id for the file into a slice, then looped issuing `DELETE FROM topology_fts WHERE rowid = ?` once per node. A file with M symbols therefore cost M separate DELETE statements against the FTS5 virtual table. Because `topology_fts` is rowid-keyed on the very `topology_nodes.id` assigned in `insertNodes` (the per-row loop used the node id as the FTS rowid), the loop is exactly equivalent to one `DELETE FROM topology_fts WHERE rowid IN (SELECT id FROM topology_nodes WHERE file_id = ?)`, which is what the function now issues before the existing node delete — dropping the intermediate id slice and its SELECT-into-slice loop. Guarded by `TestIndexer_ReindexDropsStaleFTS` (a symbol renamed away in a re-index must no longer match an FTS search afterwards, and the FTS row count must equal the node row count). This addresses the set-based FTS-delete half of #65; the resync-cancellation half is fixed in the companion entry below.
- **A topology resync with pacing disabled could not be cancelled, blocking daemon shutdown ([#65](https://github.com/plumbkit/plumb/issues/65)).** `processResync`'s `filepath.Walk` callback only observed `idx.done`/`ctx.Done()` inside `pace()`, and `pace` returns immediately without any cancellation check when pacing is disabled (`resync_batch <= 0 || resync_pause_ms <= 0` — both documented, config-validated values). With pacing off, an in-progress resync ran to completion regardless of `Stop()`; since `Stop()` does `close(done)` then `wg.Wait()`, daemon shutdown (and `Store.Close`) blocked for the entire walk of a large workspace. The walk callback now does an unconditional, non-blocking `select` on `idx.done`/`ctx.Done()` at its top, aborting promptly via `errResyncAborted` (which already skips the prune so a partial walk cannot delete live files) whether or not pacing is configured. This completes #65 — the set-based FTS delete (part 1) shipped in the same release. Guarded by `TestProcessResync_PacingDisabled_AbortsOnDone` and `TestProcessResync_PacingDisabled_AbortsOnContextCancel` (a pacing-disabled resync indexes zero files once `done`/`ctx` is signalled).
- **The write rate limiter over-counted the shared parent budget for an operation it then refused locally, over-throttling sibling connections ([#63](https://github.com/plumbkit/plumb/issues/63)).** `RateLimiter.Allow` evaluates the local window, releases the local lock, then calls `parent.Allow()` on the shared per-client budget — which **records** a slot when it returns true — before re-acquiring the local lock to re-verify the window. If the local window advanced or a concurrent sibling filled it in that gap, `Allow` returned false: the operation was refused, but the parent slot was already consumed and there was no path to return it. Under contention across connections from the same `(client, workspace)`, the shared budget therefore drifted upward, throttling siblings more aggressively than the true combined write rate, and the method's "nothing is recorded" guarantee was violated for the parent. `Allow` is now a thin orchestrator over `checkLocalAndParent` (local window then parent, lock released between) and `recordLocal` (re-verify + append); when the re-verify refuses *after* the parent recorded, a new compensating `release()` hands the parent slot back, so the shared budget reflects exactly the operations that were allowed. The duplicated window-pruning is factored into `pruneLocked`. Guarded by `TestRateLimiter_ParentNotOverCountedOnLocalRefuse` (64 siblings race a child of limit 1 sharing a generous parent; exactly one op is admitted and the parent count must equal that one — the test fails against the un-released code, recording many parent slots for one allowed op) and `TestRateLimiter_release`; run under `-race`. No change to the single-threaded behaviour the existing parent tests assert.
- **The golangci-lint quality analyser was silently dead against golangci-lint v2 — it now uses the v2 output flag and surfaces a failed invocation ([#57](https://github.com/plumbkit/plumb/issues/57)).** The analyser invoked `golangci-lint run --out-format=json`, but `--out-format` was removed in golangci-lint v2 (the project pins v2.12.2): the binary errors with `unknown flag: --out-format` and writes nothing to stdout. Because `_ = cmd.Run()` discarded the exit error and the code then treated empty stdout as "no issues", **every** post-write lint pass returned zero findings in production, and a broken invocation was indistinguishable from a clean file. Three fixes: (1) the flag is now the v2 spelling `--output.json.path=stdout` (verified to emit `{"Issues":[…]}` on stdout with v2.12.2); (2) `parseOutput` decodes only the **leading** JSON value via a `json.Decoder` — golangci-lint appends a human-readable run summary (`N issues:` …) after the JSON on stdout when issues are present, which `json.Unmarshal` would reject as trailing data (so the naive flag swap alone would still drop every finding whenever issues exist); (3) since a successful v2 run always writes a JSON document to stdout even with zero issues, empty stdout now reliably means the linter failed to run, so the analyser `slog.Warn`s with a bounded stderr tail instead of silently reporting clean. The write still succeeds regardless (a lint failure never breaks a write). Guarded by a new `//go:build integration` `TestIntegration_RealBinary` that drives the real binary on a file with a known govet issue and asserts at least one finding comes back — the regression the prior unit-only tests (which fed `parseOutput` hardcoded JSON) could not catch.
- **Post-merge cleanup of the dependency-reads + lean-profile work: removed the two `#nosec` suppressions and reconciled the tool-priority rule with the lean profile.** (1) `internal/cli/dep_roots.go` no longer carries any `#nosec` — gosec's G703 (path-traversal-via-taint) false positives on the read-only existence stats are cleared by laundering the `os.Getenv` reads (`CARGO_HOME`, `GRADLE_USER_HOME`, `JAVA_HOME`, `VIRTUAL_ENV`) through small getter functions that return the path, the same idiom `goEnvRoots` already uses (gosec does not propagate taint through a function return). The repo keeps **zero** linter suppressions, and the JVM resolver's home handling is tidied in the same pass. (2) AGENTS.md's CRITICAL tool-priority rule now carves out the lean profile: the read-only commodity search/list/find tools are intentionally hidden there, so native equivalents are expected, while writes/edits, symbol operations, `git`, and `run_task` stay always-plumb. No behaviour change.

- **A mid-session tool-profile change now actually takes effect: the server advertises the `tools.listChanged` capability and emits `notifications/tools/list_changed` when a config reload changes a connection's resolved profile.** Client-aware tool profiles (`[tools] profile`) bind the `ToolFilter` once and the server never re-lists, so a per-project `[tools]` override loaded at attach — or a hot-reloaded `profile = "full"` — was invisible until a brand-new connection (a documented limitation). The fix wires a server→client notification path: a new `mcp.NotifyFn` (a no-id JSON-RPC notification guarded by the same `wrMu` as every other socket write) is handed to `OnInit` alongside the existing `RequestFn`; the initialize response now advertises `capabilities.tools.listChanged = true`. Per connection, plumb **seeds** the last-advertised profile at `OnInit` (so the seed matches what the client first listed and no spurious notification fires at startup) and, at the end of `applyProjectConfig` (the single funnel for attach / re-pin / hot-reload), compares the freshly-resolved profile against the seed — on a genuine change it updates the seed and sends `notifications/tools/list_changed`. The check runs after `applyProjectConfig`'s own `mutate` has returned, so it never re-enters the mutation lane (no deadlock). The resilient proxy already forwards any server-initiated frame to the client unchanged, so no proxy change was needed: a client that honours the notification re-lists and picks up the new profile mid-session; a client that lists only once simply ignores it. Guarded by `TestServer_Initialize_AdvertisesToolsListChanged`, `TestServer_NotifyFromOnInit` (a real net.Pipe round-trip asserting the notification frame carries a method and no id), and `TestMaybeNotifyToolProfileChange_{FiresOnChange,NoFireWhenUnchanged,NoNotifierIsNoOp}`.
- **The write tools now document the sole-agent `expected_mtime` fast path and the atomic-write guarantee on a transport failure — two recurring sources of agent uncertainty.** (1) Agents doing a burst of sequential `edit_file`s repeatedly rediscovered that threading the freshly-returned `mtime` into the next edit is self-defeating (each edit returns a *new* mtime) and that the exactly-once `old_string` match is itself sufficient safety — so `edit_file`'s description and `docs/tools.md` now bless “omit `expected_mtime`, trust exact-once” as the fast path for a sole agent, reserving `expected_mtime`/`expected_sha` for when a concurrent writer may touch the file. (2) When a `write_file`/`edit_file` call died mid-flight with `Connection closed`, the agent had no way to know whether the write had landed and dropped to a shell `ls` to check; `write_file`/`edit_file` descriptions and `docs/tools.md` now state the guarantee the code already provides — the atomic temp+rename means the file is either fully written or untouched, never partial, so a re-read (not an assumption of corruption) resolves it. Documentation only; no behaviour change.
- **`run_task` is now in the lean tool profile, so recognised CLI clients (Claude Code, Codex, Gemini CLI) discover the build/test runner instead of silently shelling out.** The lean profile hides commodity tools that have a safe native equivalent — but `run_task` has none: it is the trust-gated, no-shell, bounded `[tasks.<lang>]` build/test/lint/verify runner whose only alternative is a raw shell `go test`/`zig build`, exactly the fallback plumb exists to replace. Because the lean profile is served precisely to recognised CLI agents, hiding `run_task` from `tools/list` made it invisible to the very clients meant to use it — so they ran builds and tests in the shell, outside plumb's view (a recurring agent-feedback observation: “verification lived in Bash; plumb saw the edits, not the evidence”). Moving it into `LeanTools` (`internal/tools/profile.go`) keeps the lean `tools/list` payload under its <50% budget (`TestLeanProfileBudget`: lean is ~46% of full). The lockstep guards (`TestLeanToolSet_MatchesLeanTools`, `TestToolProfileClassification`, `TestFullToolSet_Count`) and the AGENTS.md lean-set description are updated in step.
- **A prolonged daemon outage (notably a version upgrade) no longer kills the in-session client — `plumb serve` rides it out instead of exiting.** The resilient proxy reconnected to a fresh daemon transparently, but only for `defaultMaxReconnects` (10) fast attempts; on exhaustion it returned a fatal “daemon unreachable” error, which propagated out of `run()` and **exited the `plumb serve` process**. That closes the client's stdio, so the host (e.g. Claude Code) emits its own `-32000: Connection closed` and **de-registers every `mcp__plumb__*` tool for the rest of the session** — a hard outage needing a full host restart. This is reachable during a routine daemon upgrade: while the human's freshly-built daemon is starting, the proxy's own reconnect dials fail (or its spawned daemon loses the singleton `flock` race and exits on `EWOULDBLOCK`), and the ~30–40 s upgrade window can burn the whole 10-attempt budget. An agent reported exactly this. The fix makes reconnect **non-fatal**: once the bounded fast phase is exhausted, the proxy fails the in-flight requests **once** (so the client gets a retryable `-32000` instead of hanging for the whole outage) and then keeps retrying in the background at the capped backoff **indefinitely**, until a daemon returns or the client closes stdin / the context is cancelled. A daemon restart/upgrade is now a brief pause, not a session-ending outage — the next tool call succeeds against the recovered daemon. The synthesised retry error is also reworded to state a write's outcome is **unconfirmed** (re-read before retrying), and the reconnect note now gives actionable guidance (re-read before editing, or `dirty_ok:true` for a file you wrote earlier this session, since the fresh daemon rebuilt the per-connection read/write tracking). Version skew remains purely informational (no version is ever treated as fatal). Guarded by the rewritten `TestProxySurvivesProlongedOutageThenRecovers` (in-flight request gets the retryable error, `run()` stays alive through the outage, the next call succeeds once a daemon is provided, and closing stdin shuts down cleanly), with the existing crash-recovery / no-auto-replay / hang-kill proxy tests still passing `-race`.

- **The topology indexer now drains its parse-arena pool after the queue goes idle, so a daemon left at rest no longer holds hundreds of MB of pooled tree-sitter arenas.** gotreesitter's full-parse node arenas are recycled through a **package-global, strong-reference free-list** (`fullArenaPool`, `maxSize = 4`) — not a `sync.Pool`, so a pooled arena survives GC until explicitly drained (`tsg.DrainArenaPools()`). Plumb only drained it in two places: at the end of a full resync, and after a coalesced **burst** of `>= 64` files in one queue cycle (`shouldReclaimAfterBurst`). But with the live file watcher running, the periodic resync is **suppressed** (`store.go` sets `resyncMins = 0`), and the normal edit loop is a *trickle* — each `edit_file`/`write_file` re-indexes one file in its own cycle, which never trips the 64-file burst gate. So the high-water-mark arena from the largest file parsed sat pooled indefinitely on an otherwise idle daemon. Measured on a real workspace: a daemon at **681 MB RSS / 211 MB live heap** (stable across a forced GC with the indexer goroutines parked) had **72% of its live heap (~156 MB) in gotreesitter markdown arenas** under the indexer; reproducing the daemon's *actual* markdown set (files within the 256 KiB per-grammar parse cap — `langsupport.MaxParseBytes`, applied by `skipOversizedGrammar` before parsing) retained **~67 MB pool-held** across the corpus, **all of which `DrainArenaPools()` reclaimed** — proving the residue was pool-retained, **not a leak**. The 156 MB live snapshot is consistent with a single high-water arena left by a moderately-large markdown file re-indexed via a trickle (the pool keeps one arena up to its 128 MB eviction ceiling). The fix adds a **debounced idle-reclaim timer** to the indexer's background worker: a queue cycle that did not already reclaim (not a burst, not a resync) arms a `defaultIdleReclaim` (30 s) timer; once the queue stays quiet for that window the worker drains the arena pools and hands the freed pages back to the OS. Each new cycle resets the timer, so an active edit loop never pays a per-edit stop-the-world GC, the burst gate still reclaims a large burst immediately, and an idle daemon settles back to its lean resident set within ~30 s. All three reclaim paths now funnel through one injectable `reclaimFn` (`drainArenas`), and a successful resync (not merely its intent) is what credits the reclaim, so a failed walk/prune leaves the idle backstop armed rather than cancelling it. Guarded by `TestIndexer_IdleReclaim_TrickleDrainsArenaPool` (a single-file edit must reclaim once the queue goes quiet), `TestIndexer_IdleReclaim_DisabledByZero` (`idleReclaim = 0` turns the idle drain off and a trickle reclaims only via the timer, never per-cycle), `TestRunQueueCycle_ReclaimedReturn` (the bool contract: trickle false, burst true, resync true only on success, **failed resync false**), and `TestIndexer_BurstReclaim_CancelsPendingIdleDrain` (a burst following a trickle cancels the pending idle drain). **Follow-up not in this change:** the 256 KiB grammar cap bounds *which* files parse but not the transient spike — a 129 KB markdown file still balloons to ~250 MB mid-parse — so a per-parse arena budget (gotreesitter exposes `budgetBytes`) or a tighter markup cap would bound the peak; tracked separately.
- **The TUI dashboard no longer re-runs whole-table stats aggregations on every 2 s poll — a CPU-usage regression that scaled with `stats.db` size.** Each dashboard poll recomputed the lifetime-, uptime- and project-scoped widgets from scratch — `SavingsAxes` scans every row, and `Summary` sorts every call's `duration_ms` for its p95 — so as `stats.db` grew to tens of thousands of rows the 2 s poll began spiking a core to 40%+. The regression rode in with the two-axis token-efficiency widgets (this release), which added the per-poll `SavingsAxes` full scan to `refreshDashboard`. Three fixes: (1) the lifetime/uptime/project aggregates now recompute only on the existing 30 s bucket cadence (and the first poll), keeping the hot poll path off the full table — these figures barely move between 2 s ticks; (2) `Summary` folds `SUM(tokens_saved)` into its single `GROUP BY` instead of issuing one `tokensSavedFor` query per distinct tool (an N+1 that ran ~50 extra queries per call); (3) a new composite index `idx_tc_tool_dur (tool, duration_ms)` lets the p95 query scan a covering index already in tool/duration order, removing its temp-b-tree sort (measured ~27 ms → ~7 ms on a 22k-row database). The index is created by the idempotent base-schema DDL on the next daemon open, exactly like the other `tool_calls` indexes (no `user_version` bump). Guarded by the extended `TestOpenCreatesCurrentGlobalSchema` (asserts every `idx_tc_*` index, including the new one) and the existing `TestSavingsCountsStoredExcludesLegacy` (covers `Summary`'s folded `tokens_saved`).
- **The TUI "Token Efficiency" widget caption is one line again, and no longer shows a `total` that reads as a duplicate of `efficiency`.** The two-axis work (this release) added a second caption line — `capability ~X · efficiency ~Y` — beneath the existing `uptime … / total …` line, and because the lifetime `total` is defined as `capability + efficiency` (`AxisTotals.Total`), whenever one axis dominates (e.g. capability ~166 vs efficiency ~19235k) the `total` and `efficiency` figures rounded to the same `k` value and looked duplicated. The widget now drops the standalone `total` and renders a single caption — `uptime <savings> (<window>)` on the left and the honest split `cap ~<capability> · eff ~<efficiency> (<lifetime>)` on the right — so the breakdown is preserved without the redundant headline or the extra row. The lifetime total still drives the right-hand block-grid fill; only the text changed. The right caption is longer than the old `total …`, so the label gap is now clamped to keep the line within the box's inner width at narrow terminals (`dashBox` does not widen for an over-long line). Guarded by the updated `TestDashTokensWidgetUsesLargeTwoColumnLayout` (asserts the single `cap ~… · eff ~…` caption and the absence of a second axis line).
- **Tidied a `strings.Builder` write in `safe_delete_symbol`'s REFUSED branch — no behaviour change ([#71](https://github.com/plumbkit/plumb/pull/71)).** The external-reference loop built each line with `sb.WriteString(l + "\n")`, allocating a throwaway string per reference just to append a newline; since the builder is already a buffer it now writes the line and the newline byte separately (`WriteString(l)` + `WriteByte('\n')`), emitting identical output. Clears the `writestring` linter nit noticed while [#70](https://github.com/plumbkit/plumb/pull/70) was fresh.

### Added

- **The semantic symbol-edit tools and `transaction_apply` now append a unified diff to their response, so the agent can show the user exactly what changed.** Until now only `edit_file`/`write_file`/`undo_edit` rendered a diff; the four semantic edits (`replace_symbol_body`, `insert_before_symbol`, `insert_after_symbol`, `safe_delete_symbol`) returned only a one-line "Replaced symbol X in …" — and in `dry_run`, a bare line/char range — while `transaction_apply` reported a per-file line-count summary with no diff. All five now emit the same unified-diff block as the file-write tools, gated by the existing `[edits].show_write_diff` toggle (default on; `PLUMB_SHOW_WRITE_DIFF=0` to suppress). For the symbol tools the diff is rendered in **both** `dry_run` preview (the high-value case — the agent shows the change before applying, file untouched) and applied mode; `transaction_apply` lists each file with its own diff. The in-memory edit-application logic is factored out of `applyTextEditsToFile` into a pure `applyTextEdits(data, edits)` so the symbol tools can compute the post-edit content for the diff without a second read/apply, and the diff is **best-effort presentation** — a read or apply error degrades to no diff, never a failed edit. `delete_file` additionally now reports the line + byte count it removed (bytes only for a binary or oversized file), read before deletion. Guarded by `TestReplaceSymbolBody_DiffInPreviewAndApplied`, `TestReplaceSymbolBody_ShowWriteDiffOffSuppressesDiff`, `TestSafeDeleteSymbol_DiffOnApply`, `TestApplyTextEdits_PureMatchesFileWrite`, `TestTransaction_DiffGatedByShowWriteDiff`, and `TestDeleteFile_Summary{ReportsLinesAndBytes,BinaryFallsBackToBytes}`.
- **`allow_dependency_reads` is now multi-language: a Zig/Rust/Python/Swift/Kotlin/Java session can read its toolchain stdlib + dependency cache read-only, not just Go.** Until now the dependency-read grant was hardcoded to Go (`GOMODCACHE`/`GOROOT`), so in every other compiled language half the real questions — the ones that live in the language's own stdlib outside the workspace root — forced a shell `grep` fallback (the #1 agent-feedback item).
