The single Go-only gate is replaced by a **per-language resolver registry** (`internal/cli/dep_roots.go`, `depResolvers` keyed by the `[lsp.<lang>]` id): **Go** (`go env GOMODCACHE`/`GOROOT`), **Zig** (`zig env` → `lib_dir` + `global_cache_dir`; its output is ZON, parsed by the pure, unit-tested `parseZigEnv`), **Rust** (`rustc --print sysroot` → the rust-src `library` tree when the component is installed, plus `${CARGO_HOME:-~/.cargo}/registry/src`), **Python** (the active interpreter — venv's `python` when `VIRTUAL_ENV` is set, else `python3`/`python` on PATH — introspected via `sysconfig` for stdlib + site-packages), **Swift** (`xcrun --show-sdk-path`; nil off macOS), and **JVM** (kotlin/java: `${GRADLE_USER_HOME:-~/.gradle}/caches/modules-2`, `~/.m2/repository`, and `$JAVA_HOME`). TypeScript is intentionally absent — its `node_modules` already lives inside the workspace. Each resolver shells out under a bounded 5 s context, degrades to **nil** when its toolchain binary is absent, and only adds directories that actually exist; every root is `AccessRead`, so writes there stay refused by `PathPolicy` construction. Roots are still resolved **off the attach mutation lane** by `warmDepRoots` so attach never blocks on a toolchain shell-out. A new `depRootsLang` field records the language the cached roots were resolved for, and `buildPathPolicy` admits them only while the session stays on that language — so a cross-language re-pin cannot leak the prior toolchain's roots until `warmDepRoots` recomputes for the new language. Guarded by `TestParseZigEnv` (realistic ZON blob, empty/malformed, partial), `TestBuildPathPolicy_DepRootsGatedByLanguage` (the cross-language guard — roots resolved for "go" are unreadable while the session is "python", readable once the recorded language matches, never writable), the retained `TestBuildPathPolicy_GoDependencyReads`, and a per-resolver test for each language that skips when the toolchain (or a component like rust-src) is absent and otherwise asserts ≥1 existing read-only root with the expected label and never `AccessReadWrite`.
- **New `plumb web` command serves an opt-in, loopback-only web UI with full TUI parity.** Plumb's only human-facing surface was the Bubble Tea TUI, reachable only from a terminal. `plumb web` adds a modern, embedded single-page app — Dashboard, Sessions, Memory, Logs, and the scope-aware Settings editor with theme picker — served by the daemon over `127.0.0.1` only, behind a per-start 256-bit token. The HTTP server is hosted **inside** the daemon process (so it reads the same live pools/stores as the tools, fresher than the TUI's direct DB reads) and is **never bound until asked**: `plumb web` ensures the daemon is up, sends `web-start` over the control socket, and opens the browser at the returned tokened URL. Security model: loopback bind only, constant-time token check (query param on first load, then an `HttpOnly`/`SameSite=Strict` cookie), and an `Origin`/`Host` CSRF check on the two write paths (config + theme). The API reuses plumb's existing read paths (`internal/stats`, `internal/monitor`, `internal/session`, `internal/topology`, `internal/memory`) and pushes live updates over Server-Sent Events (stdlib `net/http`, no new web-framework or WebSocket dependency). The frontend is a Svelte 5 + Vite + Tailwind SPA with ECharts + uPlot charts, `go:embed`'d into the binary so the single-binary distribution is preserved; the web palette is driven by CSS variables fed from `/api/theme`, so it tracks the selected plumb theme. New config `[web] port` (default 8870, global-only); the theme palette is extracted into a UI-agnostic `internal/theme` package consumed by both the TUI and the web UI. Guarded by `internal/web` handler/auth tests (loopback guard, token + CSRF enforcement, SPA fallback, theme/settings/dashboard endpoints, bind-loopback round-trip) and `internal/cli` control-socket tests for `web-start`/`web-status`/`web-stop`.
- **Parameter aliases now survive client-side schema validation, so a tool call under a near-miss parameter name runs instead of failing — and the alias table is much broader.** plumb already rewrote alias parameter names to canonical ones inside the daemon (`internal/mcp/argalias.go`), but the rewrite never ran for the most common failure: a host that validates `tools/call` arguments against the advertised `inputSchema` *before transmitting* (Claude Code does, via a Zod schema) rejected `search_in_files({query, …})` with `-32602 … "pattern" is Required` — the call never reached the daemon, so the alias layer was dead on arrival. (Confirmed empirically against the stats DB: these were host-side `required`-check rejections, distinct from the server-side "did you mean" rejections that *did* reach the daemon.) The fix is a new **`publishSchema`** transform (`internal/mcp/argschema.go`) applied only at the `tools/list` publish seam: for the top level and recursively through nested object / array-of-object schemas (`edits[]`, `operations[]`) it (1) drops every **alias-target** field (any name in the union of the alias table's values — `pattern`, `query`, `name`, `file_path`, `path`, `paths`, `root`, `from`, `to`, `replacement`, `workspace`, …) from `required`, and (2) relaxes `additionalProperties` to `true`, so a pre-validating host forwards the alias-bearing call. The daemon keeps validating against the **original strict schema** (`parseShape` is unchanged), so the real contract — full `required` set, unknown-parameter "did you mean" — is still enforced server-side with plumb's good error messages, and the alias rewrite still fires (the rewrite sees alias keys as *unknown*, which is what triggers it). `publishSchema` is pure and **fail-open** (a non-object/unparseable schema is returned byte-for-byte) and the published schema is precomputed once per tool at registration. The **alias table is also substantially expanded**, driven by the parameter names agents actually send (mined from the stats DB): `pattern`↔`query` reciprocal; `name`/`symbol`→`symbol_name`/`query`; `path`→`root` (list_files) and `root`→`path`; `is_regex`→`use_regex`; `file_paths`→`paths`; `find`/`replace`→`pattern`/`replacement`; `file_pattern`→`glob`; `source`/`destination`→`from`/`to`; `workspace_path`/`workspacePath`→`workspace`. Every entry is gated by the existing **eligibility rule** (applied only when the canonical is a real, unset parameter of *that* tool), so one alias serves differently-shaped tools and never misfires; deliberately excluded are semantic flips (`include`≠`exclude`, `apply`≠`dry_run`) and any safety-critical guess (no `git` subcommand/`confirm`/`files` inference). Guarded by `TestPublishSchema_*` (drops aliased required, keeps non-alias required, recurses into array items, fail-open, preserves property order), `TestAliasTargetSet_CoversCanonicals`, and `TestResolveArgs_ExpandedAliases`.
- **`get_definition` and `find_references` now steer agents toward `symbol_name` over a hand-computed `line`/`character`.** These two tools carry the highest genuine failure rates in the stats DB (17–35%), almost all from bad positions — gopls "no identifier found", "column is beyond end of line", or an off-by-one from 0-based confusion — when the agent computed a cursor position by hand. Both already accept a `symbol_name` alternative that plumb resolves against the file's symbols; their schema descriptions now mark it the PREFERRED path and say why (it avoids those position errors). Combined with the new `symbol`/`name`→`symbol_name` aliases (above), the natural `{uri, symbol: "Foo"}` call now resolves cleanly. (`call_hierarchy`/`type_hierarchy`/`explain_symbol` are position-only and unchanged.)
- **`rename_symbol` now returns actionable guidance when the language server can't compute a rename, plus an opt-in structural fallback ([#40](https://github.com/plumbkit/plumb/issues/40)).** When the LSP `Rename` errored or returned an empty edit set, the tool surfaced the raw error (or a bare "empty edit set" line) — common with sourcekit-lsp before the build graph resolves — leaving the agent to guess the fallback and waste a turn. It now appends a recovery hint that names the likely cause (build graph not resolved) and the concrete next steps (retry after a build; `find_references` + `edit_file`; `find_replace` on the resolved identifier). The hint resolves the actual identifier at the cursor by reading the file (`identifierAt`), so the suggestion is concrete. **Opt-in structural fallback:** passing `structural_fallback:true` makes a failed LSP rename fall through to a best-effort, identifier-boundary text rename via the existing `find_replace` engine — a word-boundary (`\bOld\b`) regex replace across same-extension files under the workspace, honouring `dry_run` (default true). It is loudly labelled **not scope-aware** (a same-named identifier in another scope is also matched), so a same-name collision elsewhere is the agent's to review — but it unblocks Swift/sourcekit-lsp renames that the LSP cannot do at all. The default path (LSP up, no flag) is byte-for-byte unchanged. Guarded by `TestRenameSymbol_LSPError_ActionableHint`, `TestRenameSymbol_LSPError_SuggestsStructuralWhenWired`, `TestRenameSymbol_StructuralFallback_{DryRun,Applies,OnEmptyEditSet}` (the apply test asserts the word boundary leaves `FooBar` untouched when renaming `Foo`), and `TestIdentifierAt`.
- **New `undo_edit` tool safely reverts plumb's most recent write to a file ([#39](https://github.com/plumbkit/plumb/issues/39)).** Until now the only way to revert a bad edit was `git checkout`/`git restore` via the `git` tool, which sits at the destructive tier and reverts the **whole file** — discarding any *other* uncommitted changes in it (a real data-loss footgun); the `txlog` WAL only rolls back a `transaction_apply` that fails mid-flight, not a write that already completed. `undo_edit` closes the gap: `edit_file` and `write_file` now snapshot each successful write into a per-session `UndoStore` (the content before the write + a hash of what plumb wrote), and `undo_edit({file_path})` restores **only** plumb's own change — deleting the file if that write created it. It **refuses by default** when the file has changed since plumb wrote it (an external or peer edit, detected by hashing the current content against the recorded post-write hash), so it never silently clobbers someone else's work; `force:true` overrides. Single-level per path (a fresh write re-arms it), per session, and cleared on a workspace re-pin. Memory is bounded — pre-write content over 1 MiB is not snapshotted, and the store keeps at most 64 paths (oldest evicted). `undo_edit` is in the lean tool profile (a mutation tool with no safe native fallback). Guarded by `TestUndoEdit_*` (restore an edit, remove a created file, restore an overwrite, nothing-to-undo, refuse-on-external-change + force override, nil-store) and `TestUndoStore_*` (record/take/peek/reset, oldest-eviction cap, nil-safety).
- **`edit_file` now appends a closest-match diff when an `old_string` is not found, so a near-miss is fixed without a full re-read ([#38](https://github.com/plumbkit/plumb/issues/38)).** A failed match is the most common write-tool retry cause: an agent guesses the wrong indentation, or carries a one-token typo, and the existing not-found error said only "not found" plus the read-state tier (file changed since read vs unchanged-so-snippet-wrong) — leaving a slow `read_file` → `edit_file` loop to discover the truth. `notFoundError` now receives the current file content and, when a sufficiently similar region exists, appends a bounded, labelled unified diff (`"-"` = your `old_string`, `"+"` = the actual file content) pointing at it — a *suggestion only*, never an applied edit, so the exactly-once contract still governs any real write. Candidate regions are found whitespace-first (each non-blank old line aligned against content lines with the same trimmed text — the dominant indentation-drift case) with a character-similarity (Sørensen–Dice bigram) fallback that rescues the single-line-typo case where no line is trimmed-equal; windows are scored by a whitespace- and typo-tolerant per-line similarity over the longer length, gated at 0.5 so an unrelated snippet stays silent and does not drown out the existing guidance. Cost is bounded (candidate cap; the diff reuses the package's existing Myers/`renderUnifiedDiff` machinery, capped at 80 lines). CRLF normalisation and line-number-gutter detection already handled their cases and are unchanged. Guarded by `TestClosestMatchDiff` (indentation drift, single-token drift, unrelated/empty/below-threshold silence, nearest-of-several anchors), `TestClosestCandidateStarts`(`_Capped`), `TestLineWindowSimilarity`, and the end-to-end `TestEditFile_NotFound_AppendsClosestMatchDiff`.
- **Char-precise byte/column and doc-comment spans on topology nodes, so symbol-edit tools can retire the line-scan doc-comment heuristic when an exact span is available.** Every `topology.Node` now carries a byte-precise declaration span — `StartByte`/`EndByte` (0-based byte offsets) and `StartCol`/`EndCol` (0-based byte columns) gated behind a `HasBytes` presence flag (byte 0 is a legitimate offset, so a zero is never the "absent" sentinel) — plus an optional doc-comment byte span (`DocStartByte`/`DocEndByte`, present only when `DocEndByte > DocStartByte`; `HasDocSpan()` reports it). The data was already computed by the extractors and discarded. **All three extractor families now populate the declaration span:** the Go AST extractor (from `token.FileSet` offsets/columns, doc span from the `*ast.CommentGroup`), the gotreesitter extractors (Python, JavaScript, Rust, Kotlin, Java, Swift, Zig + the config/IaC/markup grammars), and the wasmts TS/TSX/Swift walks (byte offsets from the grammar, columns derived from the line map — the wasm bundles export no point/prev-sibling functions). **Doc spans** are populated for the C-style/leading-comment languages with a reliable preceding-comment node (Go, Rust, Java, Kotlin, JavaScript, Zig, and gotreesitter Swift via `docSpanBefore`); config/markup grammars and the wasmts TS/Swift walks carry the declaration span only (a wasm rebuild would be needed for their leading comments). `StartLine`/`EndLine` are unchanged, so every line-based caller is unaffected. **topology.db schema upgrade:** the index had no version system, and `CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS` never alters a pre-existing table, so an `INSERT` naming the new columns would fail on an old database. A minimal `PRAGMA user_version` gate (`SchemaVersion = 1`) now drops and recreates the rebuildable topology tables when the on-disk version is older — the indexer repopulates them on the resync that runs at every attach — and stamps the current version (a fresh database stamps directly). **Consumer:** the symbol-edit topology fallback (`nodeToDocSymbol`) now emits a char-precise `protocol.Range` (real start/end columns) when a node carries a span, falling back to the line-granular 0→EOL range otherwise; and `include_doc_comment` on `insert_before_symbol`/`replace_symbol_body` prefers the node's precise doc-span start over the `docCommentStart` line-scan when topology resolves a node with a doc span (the line-scan stays the fallback for the LSP-only path and `safe_delete_symbol`). The LSP-up path is byte-for-byte unchanged. Guarded by `TestExtract_ByteSpanReconstructsDeclaration`/`TestExtract_ByteSpanMultibyte` (Go), `TestPython_ByteSpanReconstructsDeclaration`, `TestRust_ByteSpanAndDocSpan`, `TestTS_ByteSpanReconstructsDeclaration` (wasmts), `TestInsertNodes_SpanRoundTrip`, `TestOpenDB_FreshStampsVersionAndSpanColumns`/`TestOpenDB_OldVersionRecreatesSchema`, `TestNodeToDocSymbol_CharPreciseWhenSpansPresent`, `TestByteOffsetToPosition`, and `TestReplaceSymbolBody_Fallback_CharPreciseRange`/`TestReplaceSymbolBody_Fallback_IncludeDocComment_PreciseSpan`.
- **The `zls` (Zig) adapter is promoted from experimental to validated.** A real-binary retest (2026-06-17, zls 0.16) confirms it now passes **both** gated integration tests — `TestIntegration_DocumentSymbols` and `TestIntegration_DidChangeWatchedFiles`. The diagnostics round-trip began working once plumb advertised the `textDocument.publishDiagnostics` client capability (the same fix that validated typescript-language-server); the earlier "zls is pull-only so it never pushes" hypothesis was wrong. `doc.go`, the README language-tier matrix, and the AGENTS.md adapter table are updated. (kotlin-language-server was retested in the same pass and still fails `TestIntegration_DidChangeWatchedFiles` — it needs a real Gradle/Maven project, not a bare temp workspace — so it stays experimental.)
- **Git serialisation Parts 2 & 3: a graceful-shutdown drain and an attributable stale-lock reaper, so a `plumb restart` or crash mid-commit no longer strands `.git/index.lock`.** Completing the per-repo serialisation work (Part 1, above). **Part 2 (drain):** the instant daemon shutdown begins, `tools.BeginGitWriteDrain()` stops admitting *new* index/ref-mutating git ops (they fail fast with "daemon is shutting down; git writes are paused"), and an *in-flight* write's git child now runs under a **cancellation-decoupled, bounded context** (`context.WithoutCancel` + a 2-minute grace) so a shutdown or connection eviction mid-commit lets git finish and release the lock instead of SIGKILLing it. The accept loop additionally waits a short bounded `gitWriteDrainGrace` for a quick commit to finish before exit (the watchdog deadline absorbs it). Network-tier ops (push/fetch) stay request-cancellable — a hung auth prompt must remain interruptible. **Part 3 (reaper):** while a git child runs, plumb stamps an **owner sidecar** (`.git/plumb-index-owner.json`) with the *child's* pid + hostname; before the next op on that repo it reaps a stranded `.git/index.lock` **only** when the sidecar proves a dead, this-host, plumb-spawned owner — an external git (no sidecar), a live process (pid alive, including a decoupled child still finishing), or another machine (host differs) is always left untouched, preserving today's safe-by-default behaviour (the manual `indexLockHint` remains the fallback for an unattributable lock). The sidecar records the git *child* pid, not the daemon pid, precisely so a `plumb restart` (daemon dead, decoupled child alive) cannot false-reap a live commit's lock. Guarded by `TestReapStaleGitLock_{DeadOwnerReaped,LiveOwnerKept,NoSidecarKept,DifferentHostKept,NoLockNoop}`, `TestRecordAndClearGitLockOwner`, `TestBeginSerialisedGit_RefusedWhileDraining`, and `TestWaitGitWritesDrained_NoInflightReturnsTrue`.
- **`workspace_symbols` now fills empty-but-no-error results from the topology Map for tree-sitter languages, and zig prefers the structural outline.** Lazy language servers (zls, and the other on-demand indexers) only answer `workspace/symbol` for files they have already analysed, so a freshly-attached session legitimately returns `[]` for a symbol that exists — previously printing "No symbols found" even though `file_outline` showed it via the Map. When the LSP answers empty *with no error*, the tool now supplements from the topology index for tree-sitter-backed languages (annotated `topology fill … source=topology, mode=indexed-approximate`); native-AST languages (Go via gopls, which indexes eagerly) are deliberately excluded so an authoritative empty answer is never supplanted by approximate matches. The fill runs in the tool layer, so both the single-server path and the multi-language monorepo fan-out benefit. Separately, `zig` now carries `PreferStructuralOutline` (joining markdown/html), so `file_outline`/`list_symbols`/`find_symbol` use the instant, version-robust Map instead of waiting on a cold zls. Guarded by `TestWorkspaceSymbols_TreeSitterFillOnEmptyLSP` and `TestWorkspaceSymbols_NoFillForNativeAST`.
- **Pull-diagnostics consumption path (toward validating zls / kotlin on the LSP 3.17 pull model).** Builds on the existing pull protocol types and the TypeScript adapter's `Diagnostic()`: the `diagnostics` tool now has a **pull fallback** — when a single-file query finds the push cache empty for an untracked file and the language server advertised `diagnosticProvider`, it issues `textDocument/diagnostic` directly (folding in any `relatedDocuments`, labelled `source=lsp-pull`) instead of only opening-and-waiting for a `publishDiagnostics` that a pull-only server never sends. The **zls** adapter gains `SupportsPullDiagnostics()` + `Diagnostic()` (mirroring the TypeScript adapter), so a pull-first zls is ready. Guarded by `TestDiagnostics_PullFallback_{Reports,Clean,RelatedDocuments}`, `TestDiagnostics_NoPullWhenUnsupported`, and the zls `TestAdapter_Diagnostic_Pull`/`TestAdapter_SupportsPullDiagnostics`. **Dormant pending real-binary validation:** the path is not yet routed through the live session proxy and the pull *client* capability is still not advertised (advertising it risks a dual-mode server such as gopls/pyright going pull-only — see the 0.9.20 TypeScript diagnostics fix), so no adapter is promoted here; that step needs a real zls/kotlin retest.
- **The pull-diagnostics path is now routed live through the session proxy (no longer dormant by construction).** The previous entry wired the `diagnostics` tool's pull fallback but left it dormant *live*: the tool type-asserts its LSP handle to a `pullDiagnoser` interface, and that handle is the per-connection `routingProxy`, which did not implement the interface — so the assertion failed at runtime and the pull path never fired regardless of server support. `routingProxy` now implements the pull surface (`SupportsPullDiagnostics` resolves the primary adapter; `Diagnostic` routes by URI to the owning per-file adapter and delegates), both nil/err-safe, so the assertion succeeds and the path is reachable for any installed server that advertises `diagnosticProvider`. The **gopls** adapter gains the pull methods too (mirroring zls), giving the live path a real, capability-gated backing. The path stays **purely additive** — the tool only reaches it for an untracked file the push stream never reported on, so normal pushed-diagnostics behaviour is byte-for-byte unchanged. The pull **client** capability remains deliberately un-advertised in `DefaultClientCapabilities` (advertising it risks a dual-mode server going pull-only and regressing the validated push path); with it un-advertised, an empirical retest confirms neither gopls nor zls (0.16) advertises `diagnosticProvider`, so the live path is dormant *in practice* until a pull-only server is in use, but it is no longer dormant *by construction*. kotlin promotion still needs a real Gradle/Maven project, not a bare temp workspace. Guarded by `TestRoutingProxy_SupportsPullDiagnostics_{Delegates,AdapterReportsFalse,NoPullSupport,NoPrimary}`, `TestRoutingProxy_Diagnostic_{RoutesByURI,UnsupportedAdapter}`, and the gated `TestIntegration_PullDiagnostics_LiveOrSkip` / `TestIntegration_PullAdditions_NoPushRegression` (the live pull assertion skips when no installed server advertises pull; the push-regression check passes against real gopls).
- **Client-aware tool profiles trim the `tools/list` payload for clients that already have native filesystem tools.** A new **`[tools]`** config section (`profile = auto|lean|full`, plus per-client overrides and `PLUMB_TOOLS_PROFILE`) controls which tools are advertised in `tools/list`. `auto` (default) resolves to **lean** for a recognised CLI agent that reads/searches files natively (Claude Code, Codex, Gemini CLI) and **full** for Claude Desktop and any unrecognised client. The lean profile advertises 19 of the 53 tools — cutting the measured `tools/list` payload from ~70 KiB to ~31 KiB (≈55% smaller) — while every hidden tool **stays callable by name** (`hidden ≠ unregistered`: `handleToolsList` filters, `handleToolsCall` does not, and the resilient proxy replays `initialize`, not `tools/list`). The lean set (`internal/tools/profile.go` `LeanTools`, the single source of truth) is governed by a **mutation-lane rule** — a read-only commodity tool may be hidden, but a mutation tool whose native fallback bypasses plumb's per-path locks / LSP notify / transaction WAL stays lean, as do `read_file`/`read_symbol` (the edit lane needs their mtime/sha headers). Under the lean profile `session_start` prints a one-line note with the hidden count and how to restore `full`, and its tool guidance no longer steers to a hidden tool. The filter resolves per `tools/list` off the client identity (known synchronously at `initialize`) and the per-connection `[tools]` snapshot. Guarded by `TestToolFilter_HidesFromListNotCall`, `TestResolveToolProfile`, `TestToolVisible_LeanHidesCommodityKeepsLean`, `TestToolProfileClassification`, `TestLeanProfileBudget`, `TestFullToolSet_Count`, `TestSessionStart_LeanProfileNote`, and the config plumbing tests (`TestDefaults_ToolsProfile`, `TestValidate_ToolsProfile_*`, `TestApplyEnv_ToolsProfile`, `TestApplyProjectConfig_SnapshotsTools`).
- **The `git` tool now serialises plumb's own index/ref-mutating operations per repository, turning `.git/index.lock` collisions into bounded waits.** The daemon is a singleton shared across connections, so two sessions sharing one worktree could run `git commit` concurrently and collide on `.git/index.lock` (git's exclusive per-index mutex) — the second op failing outright. A new per-repository lock (`internal/tools/git_repolock.go`, mirroring the `pathLocks` pattern with a background idle sweep registered in the daemon) wraps `runGit` for the write/destructive/network tiers only — read-tier ops (status/log/diff) are never serialised, so a query never queues behind a slow commit. The lock is keyed by the worktree's resolved top-level (`git rev-parse --show-toplevel`), so two linked worktrees committing different branches never serialise against each other. The wait is context-aware and bounded (`repoLockMaxWait`, default 2 m): a queued op whose caller context is cancelled, or that waits too long behind a wedged holder, fails fast with "another git operation is in progress on this repository" instead of hanging the connection. **Scope:** this serialises plumb's *own* git ops — an external git process (the user's shell, an IDE, CI) is invisible to the lock and can still collide. (A graceful-shutdown drain and an attributable stale-lock reaper land in a follow-up entry below.) Guarded by `TestLockRepo_SerialisesSameRepo`, `TestLockRepo_DistinctReposDoNotSerialise`, `TestLockRepo_ContextCancelledWhileWaiting`, `TestSweepRepoLocks_EvictsIdleKeepsHeld`, and the end-to-end `TestGit_ConcurrentCommitsSerialise` (six concurrent commits to one worktree all succeed, `-race` clean).
- **`plumb doctor` now validates each client's *registered binary*, and `plumb setup --all` repoints them all in one go.** The MCP-client check previously only asked "does the word `plumb` appear in this config?" — so a client still pointing at a moved or deleted plumb binary (after relocating or rebuilding the executable elsewhere) reported a clean ✓ while being completely broken. Doctor now extracts the launch command each client config registers for plumb (`setupTarget.extractFn`, format-aware across the JSON/TOML/YAML shapes and OpenCode's argv array and the standalone Antigravity file) and classifies it: a registered binary that **no longer exists** is a failure, one that exists but **differs** from the running executable (symlink-resolved) is a non-fatal warning (`!`), an exact match a clean pass — both carrying a `plumb setup <client>` fix hint. The new **`plumb setup --all`** is the bulk repair: it repoints every already-registered, installed client at the current binary and reports per-client status (`updated` / `already current` / `not installed — skipped` / `plumb not registered — skipped`), without ever adding plumb to a client that didn't already use it. Both drive the shared `allSetupClients()` table, now wired with an `extractFn` (and the originals' `intoFn`) for every client. Relatedly, `mergeServerEntry` now **merges** the canonical command/args onto an existing plumb entry instead of replacing it wholesale, so a re-register or `--all` repoint preserves user-added keys — most importantly Codex's per-tool `[mcp_servers.plumb.tools.*]` approval tables, which the old replace silently dropped. Guarded by `TestCommandString`, `TestRegisteredCommand`, `TestClassifyClientBinary`, `TestSameBinary`, `TestRefreshClient`, and `TestSetupCodexInto_PreservesPerToolTables`.

- **Per-language task commands + agent-writable config, on a new shared config-field registry.** Three interlocking additions. (1) **`[tasks.<lang>]`** stores five optional command slots per language — `build`/`lint`/`test`/`e2e`/`verify` — with shipped defaults (Go fully populated; a slot left empty over guessing an uninstalled tool). The new **`run_task`** MCP tool and the **`plumb build|lint|test|e2e|verify`** CLI execute the stored command as a **bare argv with no shell** (`config.ParseTaskCommand` rejects shell metacharacters; `RunArgv` caps output at 100 KiB/200 lines under a timeout, mirroring the git tool); `verify` is a build-then-test composite, and the only agent input reaching the argv is a shell-safe `{target}`. A project-supplied (`.plumb/config.toml`) command is gated behind a **per-workspace trust gate** — `plumb trust` records trust per workspace root in `config.DataDir()/trust.json` (never in the project, so a cloned repo cannot self-trust); defaults and global config always run. (2) The new **`agent_config`** MCP tool lets an agent read (`describe`) and, only when the user has enabled the new top-level **`agent_config_writes`** knob (default off, user-settable only), write (`set`) a small allowlist of project-config keys (the task slots + `log_level`, `ui.theme`, `ui.path_style`, `topology.exclude_patterns`, `quality.analysers`). The allowlist (`internal/config/fields_agent.go`) is the entire security model — every guardrail (git tiers, workspace roots, `edits.strict`/`rate_limit`, `semantics.api_key`, session eviction, `log_file`, `lsp.*`, **and `agent_config_writes` itself**) is never agent-writable, so the agent cannot escalate its own permission. A batch is validated against a candidate merged config and written in one atomic rewrite (a bad batch is a no-op), tagged `provenance=agent` in an auto-gitignored `.plumb/config.provenance.json` sidecar, surfaced by `plumb config show`, and revertible with the new `plumb config unset`. (3) Both are powered by a new **config-field registry** (`internal/config/fields.go`) — a single source of truth for each field's description, reload tier, type, and allowlist — that also replaces the ~50 hardcoded help strings and the local reload-tier table in the TUI Settings screen (guarded by `TestSettingsRegistryDrift`). Guarded across `internal/config`, `internal/tools`, `internal/cli`, and `internal/tui` (incl. `TestRegistry_DenyListNeverWritable`, `TestAgentApplyBatch_PartialInvalidRollsBack`, `TestTrustStore_NotWrittenIntoProject`, and the self-escalation tests).
- **`plumb setup antigravity` and `plumb setup antigravity-desktop` register plumb in Antigravity.** Google is deprecating Gemini CLI on 2026-06-18 in favour of Antigravity (a Go-based terminal agent in the Antigravity 2.0 platform); these add one-command setup targets. Antigravity reads MCP servers from a flat `{"mcpServers": {...}}` config — primarily the shared `~/.gemini/config/mcp_config.json`, which serves both the CLI and the IDE (verified against Antigravity's MCP docs and a live install) — so `plumb setup antigravity`/`antigravity-desktop` create-or-merge plumb into it, and into any per-surface `~/.gemini/{antigravity-cli,antigravity-ide,antigravity}/mcp_config.json` that already exists. A standalone `~/.gemini/antigravity-cli/mcp/plumb.json` is also written as a `plumb doctor` binary-anchor, but Antigravity regenerates those `mcp/` dirs from the shared config, so it is not the load-bearing write. **(Corrected 2026-06-17 — earlier 0.9.21 builds wrote *only* the standalone `mcp/plumb.json`, which Antigravity ignores, so plumb never appeared in Antigravity; the "per-server config files" assumption was wrong and unverified.)** Setup is non-destructive (sibling server files are preserved, an existing config is backed up first) and idempotent, via a dedicated `setupAntigravityInto` (split into `listPreservedAntigravityServers`/`isSameAntigravityConfig`/`syncAntigravityIdeConfig` to stay under the complexity gate). Both targets auto-enumerate in `plumb config show` and `plumb doctor`; `plumb setup gemini` is retained (enterprise accounts keep Gemini CLI past the deadline). Brings the supported-client count to **thirteen**. Guarded by `TestNewClientConfigPaths` and `TestSetupAntigravityInto_*` (fresh write, sibling preservation + backup, idempotency, desktop→ide mirroring).
- **Multi-language monorepo roots now detect and attach every nested language from the root.** A workspace whose `.plumb/` root carries no language marker of its own, with the languages living one level down (a Ghostty-style layout: `core/build.zig` + `app/Package.swift` under one root), previously resolved as `LanguageNone` — no LSP attached, the session showing `language: none` until a file was touched, and `workspace_symbols` failing for want of a primary. `Detect` only walks *up*, so it never saw the child markers. On a `LanguageNone` attach the daemon now additionally descends up to `[workspace] child_scan_depth` levels (default 2) for **strong** language root markers in subdirectories (new `discoverChildLanguages`/`electPrimary` in `pool_detect.go`; prunes dotdirs/`node_modules`/build outputs, stops at a matched root, never scans `$HOME`). Each discovered child language attaches its own server **rooted at its subdirectory** via the existing multi-LSP-per-root machinery (`core/`→zls, `app/`→sourcekit-lsp); one is elected the connection primary (go-first, then alphabetical) and the rest attach lazily on first file. All discovered languages show in the `session_start` identity line (`Language: Swift, Zig`) and `workspace_sessions`, and `workspace_symbols` **fans out** across every detected server (merge + dedup, warming a lazily-attached child on the first such query) instead of consulting the primary alone. Discovery runs only for a markerless root — a root with its own `go.mod` is untouched. New `[workspace] child_scan_depth` config knob (default 2; 0 disables). Guarded by `TestDiscoverChildLanguages_*`, `TestElectPrimary_Order`, and `TestWorkspaceSymbols_FanOut*`.
- **Two new TUI themes, `plumb` (dark) and `plumb-light`, derived from the project website's palette.** Lifted from `site/index.html`'s own colour tokens — a warm near-black/off-white background with the site's terracotta-amber accent and sage/forest green — so the dashboard matches the brand. `plumb` is now the **default** theme (was `nordico`). Both register in `tui.AvailableThemes` and appear in the Settings theme picker (the `plumb`/`plumb-light` pair classifies dark/light correctly via `isLightTheme`). Guarded by the existing `TestTheme_AllFieldsSet`, `TestIsLightTheme_Classification`, and `TestTheme_AllThemesRegistered` (extended).
- **`plumb config show --adapters` prints a focused language-server adapter table.** A new flag renders just the adapters — language, server binary, validation tier (first-class / validated / experimental), and live activation state (ready / install-gated / disabled) — instead of the full resolved config. Aliases: `--adapter`, `--lsp`, `--lsps`, `--integration`, `--integrations` (wired through a flag normalise func, so one flag answers to all spellings).
- **`topology_impact` now augments its inward section with cross-file callers resolved via the language server.** The Go topology extractor records call edges intra-file only (single-file extraction has no cross-file symbol table), so the "depended on by" section missed callers in other files/packages — a function called only from another package showed none. The tool now appends a `cross-file callers (source=lsp, N site(s))` block for a function/method/test centre, resolved through the language server (DocumentSymbol `SelectionRange` → references, self-file references filtered, deduped, sorted, capped at 25 with a remainder note). Best-effort: it stays topology-only when no server is wired or the lookup fails, so the fast path is unchanged. New `tools.NewLSPCrossFileCallers` + `TopologyImpact.WithCrossFileCallers`; guarded by `TestLSPCrossFileCallers_*` and `TestWriteCrossFileCallers_LabelAndCap`.
- **`plumb config show` now lists plumb's base directories.** A new "Directories" section surfaces the resolved config, data, state, **log**, and runtime/cache directories (with what each holds: `config.toml`, `sessions`/`stats.db`, regenerable state, `daemon.log`, and the socket/pid/locks/version) so the daemon log folder and stats database are discoverable without reading the source. Resolved via `internal/paths`, not created, so a not-yet-materialised directory shows as missing.
- **The `git` tool and `session_start` now understand nested submodules.** Working an agent in a superproject (e.g. plumb-ops, which mounts the public plumb source as a `./plumb` submodule) hit a silent footgun: a submodule is a separate repository, so a `git add`/`commit` run against the superproject can only record the submodule's commit pointer, never stage its file contents — and nothing told the agent the submodule existed. Three changes close the gap: (1) `session_start` adds a **"Submodules (nested git repositories)"** section listing each submodule and stating the repo-targeting rule, when the workspace has a `.gitmodules` (new `gitSubmodules` reads it via `git config`, so it reports even uninitialised submodules; `writeSessionSubmodules`); (2) `enhanceGitError` now rewrites git's cryptic `Pathspec '<p>' is in submodule '<name>'` failure into an actionable hint — re-run with `repo` pointing inside the submodule, then record the moved pointer with a separate add+commit in the superproject (new `submodulePathspecHint`/`firstQuoted`; the existing stale-`index.lock` rewrite is factored into `indexLockHint` unchanged); (3) the `git` tool's `repo` arg description documents targeting a submodule. The capability was always present — `findGitRoot` resolves a path inside a submodule to the submodule's own root via `git rev-parse --show-toplevel` — this surfaces it. Guarded by `TestEnhanceGitError_SubmodulePathspec`, `TestEnhanceGitError_IndexLockUnaffected`, `TestEnhanceGitError_Passthrough`, `TestFirstQuoted`, `TestGitSubmodules*`, and `TestWriteSessionSubmodules`.
- **Go workspace detection now recognises `go.work` as a root marker.** A directory with a `go.work` but no co-located `go.mod` — e.g. a parent that mounts a module from a subdirectory or git submodule via `use ./sub` — now resolves as Go and attaches gopls, instead of falling back to `LanguageNone`. `go.work` joins `go.mod` in the default `[lsp.go] root_markers` (`detectDiagnosticsLang` already honoured it). Guarded by `TestDefaults_GoRootMarkersIncludeGoWork` and `TestDetect_GoWorkResolvesGo`.
- **Pull-diagnostics groundwork for the TypeScript adapter (toward validating it on typescript-language-server ≥ 5.3).** typescript-language-server ≥ 5.3 does not push `textDocument/publishDiagnostics` for files outside its open-document set — it exposes diagnostics only through the LSP 3.17 *pull* model — which is why the adapter's gated `TestIntegration_DidChangeWatchedFiles` saw no diagnostics and the adapter stayed experimental ([#1](https://github.com/plumbkit/plumb/issues/1)). This lands the protocol and adapter layer for pull diagnostics: the `textDocument/diagnostic` method constant; the `DocumentDiagnosticParams`/`DocumentDiagnosticReport` (full + unchanged variants, with related-document diagnostics) and `DiagnosticOptions` types; a `diagnosticProvider` field on `ServerCapabilities` with `PullDiagnosticsEnabled()`; the `diagnostic` **client** capability (so a pull-only server advertises support); and on the adapter, `SupportsPullDiagnostics()` (records whether the server advertised the provider at initialize) plus `Diagnostic()` (issues the pull request). Guarded by `TestAdapter_Diagnostic_Pull`, `TestAdapter_SupportsPullDiagnostics`, `TestServerCapabilities_PullDiagnostics`, and `TestDocumentDiagnosticReport_Decode`. **Superseded — see the Fixed entry below:** validating against a real typescript-language-server 5.3.0 showed it does **not** implement pull diagnostics (the hypothesis was wrong); the actual fix was a missing `publishDiagnostics` client capability. The pull types/method survive as dormant infrastructure, but the `diagnostic` client capability is no longer advertised.

### Fixed

- **The TUI theme picker no longer bakes active `PLUMB_*` env overrides (or compiled defaults) into the global config file ([#2](https://github.com/plumbkit/plumb/issues/2)).** `SaveTheme` went through `Save`, which re-encodes the *entire resolved* `Config` — and the resolved config has environment variables overlaid by `Load`. So picking a theme while, say, `PLUMB_WRITE_RATE_LIMIT=5` was set wrote `rate_limit_per_minute = 5` into the file permanently, as if the user had set it; a minimal config was likewise expanded into a full dump of every field at its default. `SaveTheme` now does a **sparse** write of only the `ui.theme` key via the new `config.SetGlobalValue` (the global analogue of the project-config sparse writers): it reads the raw on-disk TOML — no defaults, no env overlay — sets the one key, and writes it back atomically, preserving every other key already present. An unparseable existing config still aborts the write rather than clobbering it. Guarded by `TestSaveTheme_DoesNotBakeEnvOverride` (the existing `TestSaveTheme_*` round-trip/preserve/refuse-broken tests still pass unchanged).
- **Tree-sitter `calls` edges resolved by name to an ambiguous target are now down-weighted and flagged, instead of asserting a confident edge to an arbitrary same-named callable ([#30](https://github.com/plumbkit/plumb/issues/30)).** The gotreesitter extractors are syntactic — they have no type information — so they resolve a call edge by callee **name** alone, and `funcIdx` keeps only one index per name. When more than one function/method in a file shares that name (e.g. two types each with their own `deinit`), a receiver-blind `recv.name()` match could mean any of them. Such an edge is now emitted at `Confidence: 0.5, Source: "heuristic-ambiguous"` rather than the usual `0.8/heuristic`, so `topology_explore`/`topology_impact`/`topology_affected` and the reconstructed `call_hierarchy` callees rank it honestly. A new shared `callableNameCounts` + `heuristicCallEdge` (in `treesitter/common.go`) centralise the decision; all eight name-keyed extractors (Zig, Python, Rust, Swift, Java, JavaScript, Kotlin, Bash) route their call-edge emission through it. `KindTest` names are excluded from the count, so a describe/it-style suite label (`describe('greet', …)`) never falsely marks a real same-named function ambiguous. Uniquely-named calls are unchanged (still `0.8`). Receiver-type-aware resolution (the full fix) and the canonical-grammar **wasmts** TS/TSX/Swift path remain out of scope here. Guarded by `TestZig_AmbiguousCallEdgeDownWeighted`; every existing `Test*_CallEdgeIntraFile` passes unchanged.
- **`plumb config show --workspace <dir>` now flags a path the daemon would refuse to attach, instead of printing a misleading ✓ ([#31](https://github.com/plumbkit/plumb/issues/31)).** For a directory with no `.plumb/` marker, no language root marker, and no `.git/` anywhere above it, `resolveCLIWorkspace` optimistically echoed the queried directory while the daemon resolves nothing ("cannot determine workspace root") and refuses to attach — so `config show` claimed a workspace for a path that will never attach. A new `resolveCLIWorkspaceDetailed` additionally reports whether the daemon would actually attach (false only for the marker-less, non-git case, and true when `[workspace].auto_attach` is enabled, since the daemon then synthesises a root). `config show` renders a warn marker (`!`) on the workspace row and prints an honest one-line note for a non-attachable path; the optimistic root is still shown, so the inspect-any-path use-case is preserved. Guarded by `TestResolveCLIWorkspaceDetailed_Attachability` (markerless → not attachable, +auto_attach → attachable, `.git/` → attachable); the existing `TestResolveCLIWorkspace_*` tests pass unchanged.
- **A path-limited `git commit` of a freshly-created (untracked) file now explains how to fix it instead of surfacing the raw `pathspec '…' did not match` error.** A path-limited commit (`git commit -m <msg> -- <files>`, the safe way to commit just your change in a shared worktree) only commits *already-tracked* paths, so naming a brand-new file git has never seen fails with git's cryptic `error: pathspec '<p>' did not match any file(s) known to git` — a real footgun reported from a live session, where the agent had to guess it needed to `git add` first. `enhanceGitError` now rewrites this into an actionable hint: the path is untracked, so stage it first with the git tool (`subcommand: "add"`, `files: [<p>]`), then commit. The new `untrackedPathspecHint` is a self-contained helper chained alongside the existing `submodulePathspecHint`/`indexLockHint` (the two pathspec failures use distinct markers — `did not match any file` vs `is in submodule` — so they never collide). Behaviour is unchanged; only the error message is friendlier. Guarded by `TestEnhanceGitError_UntrackedPathspec` and `TestEnhanceGitError_UntrackedNotSubmodule`.
- **A hibernated primary language server is now woken by URI-less LSP calls (`workspace_symbols`, the lifecycle methods), not just by URI-bearing ones.** `routingProxy.route()` already re-acquires (and so wakes) a hibernated entry via `acquireLang`, but `routingProxy.primaryClient()` returned "LSP server not yet ready" without re-acquiring — so once a pinned-but-idle primary was hibernated (the idle janitor after `idle_timeout`, or LRU eviction; Java is the only adapter that hibernates today), a `workspace_symbols` call silently fell through to topology-approximate results and never woke the JVM, and the error message implied a cold start that was not happening. `primaryClient` now takes a context and falls through to `acquireLang(ctx, primaryRoot, primaryLang, false)` to wake the entry, mirroring `route()`; a genuinely cold first start (no primary pinned yet) still returns the original error. Guarded by `TestRoutingProxy_PrimaryClientWakesHibernated`. ([#3](https://github.com/plumbkit/plumb/issues/3))
- **Security review pass on the agent-writable-config + task-runner feature.** A multi-agent review of the 0.9.20 `agent_config`/`run_task` work surfaced one consent gap and a tail of hardening items, all now fixed. (1) **`agent_config_writes` is now genuinely global-only.** It was documented as "user-settable only", but `LoadProject` merged it like any other field, so a project's `.plumb/config.toml` — which a cloned repo ships — could enable the agent-writable-config tool with no user opt-in. `LoadProject` now forces the global value to win regardless of the project file (the single chokepoint, so the daemon gate, `config show`, and the TUI all agree), and the TUI no longer offers the knob at workspace scope. The allowlist already blocked the agent from writing the key itself; this closes the project-config vector. Guarded by `TestLoadProject_AgentConfigWritesGlobalOnly`. (2) **`validateTasks` now checks the `verify` slot**, which is agent-writable but was skipped (its command is read via the struct field, not `Get`, which returns `""` for the composite) — so a shell-metacharacter string could be staged there unchecked. Guarded by `TestValidateTasks_ChecksVerifySlot`. (3) **`plumb trust` now prints the exact project-supplied task commands before recording trust**, so trusting a workspace is an informed decision (and re-running it after a command changes re-confirms the current set) rather than a blind grant. (4) The agent-config allowlist is now re-checked independently at the cli seam *and* inside `config.AgentApplyBatch` (genuine defence in depth, matching the doc comment). No exploitable path was found in the review — project task commands remain trust-gated and the trust store lives outside any workspace — these harden the consent model around it.
- **`plumb doctor` no longer misreports a hand-edited `~`/`$VAR` client launch path as a missing binary.** The registered-binary check `os.Stat`'d the raw path, so a config edited by hand to use `~/bin/plumb` or `$HOME/...` (plumb itself always writes an absolute path) was flagged as "registered binary missing". The doctor now expands a leading `~` and any environment variable before the existence check, for both the per-client and legacy-Antigravity scans. Guarded by `TestExpandRegisteredPath`.
- **`topology_routes` no longer false-matches UIKit/AppKit symbols as Vapor `configure` routes ([#5](https://github.com/plumbkit/plumb/issues/5)).** The `vapor.configure` pattern queried the bare substring `Application`, matched case-insensitively against a symbol's signature + name — so in a mixed Swift project it also flagged `UIApplication`, `ApplicationDelegate`, and `applicationDidFinishLaunching`, none of which are Vapor entry points. The query is tightened to `: Application`, requiring `Application` in a parameter-type position (the indexed signature stores `func configure(_ app: Application) throws`); this still matches both the unlabelled `configure(_:)` and labelled `configure(app:)` forms. FTS5 candidate selection is unchanged — `buildFTSQuery` still narrows on the `Application` token — and the tighter match happens in `isRouteCandidate`'s substring filter. Guarded by `TestTopologyRoutes_VaporConfigureCandidate` (the valid signature matches; the three UIKit symbols must not).
- **TypeScript diagnostics now work — the adapter is promoted to _validated_ ([#1](https://github.com/plumbkit/plumb/issues/1)).** `typescript-language-server` published **no** diagnostics for externally-changed files, so `diagnostics` and post-write checks were silent for TypeScript/JavaScript and the adapter stayed experimental. Validation against a real `typescript-language-server` 5.3.0 binary pinned the root cause: the server publishes nothing unless the client advertises the `textDocument.publishDiagnostics` capability — which plumb's `DefaultClientCapabilities` never did. (The "it uses pull diagnostics" hypothesis was disproven: `textDocument/diagnostic` returns `-32601` and the server advertises no `diagnosticProvider`.) Declaring `publishDiagnostics` makes the existing push pipeline carry TypeScript diagnostics; the gated `TestIntegration_DidChangeWatchedFiles` now passes (was a 45 s timeout). The same capability is shared by every adapter, so zls/kotlin likely benefit too (not yet retested). The pull-diagnostics client capability added in the groundwork above is **no longer advertised** — plumb consumes only push, and advertising pull could make a dual-mode server (gopls/pyright) go pull-only and stop pushing; the pull protocol types and adapter `Diagnostic()` method remain as dormant infrastructure. Guarded by `TestDefaultClientCapabilities_Diagnostics` plus the real-binary `TestIntegration_DidChangeWatchedFiles`/`TestIntegration_DocumentSymbols`.
- **`call_hierarchy` and `type_hierarchy` no longer come back empty from sourcekit-lsp (and other servers that use the `data` field).** The LSP `CallHierarchyItem`/`TypeHierarchyItem` carry an opaque `data` field that the spec requires the client to **preserve verbatim** from the `prepare` response into the follow-up `incomingCalls`/`outgoingCalls` (resp. `supertypes`/`subtypes`) request. plumb's structs omitted the field, so it was dropped on the unmarshal→remarshal round-trip and sourcekit-lsp returned no calls/types — even though the prepare step resolved the item and `find_references` at the same position found the call sites. Added `Data json.RawMessage` to both structs so it round-trips. Verified against the pauta Swift app: `call_hierarchy` on a method now lists its callers/callees and `type_hierarchy` supertypes lists the declared conformances. Guarded by `TestHierarchyItem_PreservesData`.
- **Swift `get_definition`/`find_references` by `symbol_name` now resolve nested members.** sourcekit-lsp names Swift members with their argument list in `documentSymbol` (`show()`, `load(from:)`), so an exact-string match against a plain query (`show`) failed — by-name lookup only ever resolved top-level Swift symbols (a class resolved, its methods did not), while Zig/Go worked because their member names carry no parens. `resolveSymbolsByName` now matches a symbol when the query equals either its full name or its base name (everything before the first `(`), for both the plain and dotted `Type.member` forms. Guarded by `TestResolveSymbolsByName_StripsArgList`; the Go-flat and nested-method cases still pass unchanged.
- **The semantic-edit tools (`replace_symbol_body`/`insert_before_symbol`/`insert_after_symbol`/`safe_delete_symbol`) now address a Swift member by plain `name_path` too — the by-name fix above reached only the read/query side.** Their addressing runs through `findSymbolByPath`/`findSymbolRecursive`, which still matched each path segment with an exact `==`, so `name_path: "PanelController/show"` did not match sourcekit-lsp's `show()` document-symbol name. Because the LSP now answers (the open-before-query fix), the resulting "symbol not found" was treated as an LSP miss and the edit silently fell back to the line-granular **topology** path — mislabelled `[topology fallback — LSP unavailable]` even though the server was healthy — or failed outright when topology was disabled. `findSymbolRecursive` now matches each segment with `symbolNameMatches` (the same base-name match the read/query side uses), so the edit resolves the precise LSP range directly. Verified against the pauta Swift app. Guarded by `TestFindSymbolByPath_StripsArgList`.
- **`call_hierarchy` now reconstructs a hierarchy when the language server provides none (e.g. zls for Zig), and no longer lists the same callee once per call site.** Two fixes to the same tool. (1) zls does not implement `textDocument/prepareCallHierarchy`, so `call_hierarchy` on a Zig symbol returned "No call hierarchy item found" at a position where `get_definition`/`explain_symbol` resolve fine. When the server resolves no item, the tool now reconstructs the hierarchy from the primitives the server *does* provide plus the topology call graph: **callers come from the server's own `find_references`**, each call site mapped to its enclosing symbol (so the result is named callers, and it catches callers the topology graph misses — e.g. calls inside a Zig `test "…" {}` block), and **callees come from the topology call graph** (`calls` edges, since references cannot answer "what does this call"). When the server has no references either, callers fall back to topology too. Annotated `reconstructed … approximate`. Verified against the pauta Zig core: `call_hierarchy` on `Engine.review` lists its callees (`laneOf`, `move`, `commit`, …) and its caller (the `review loop on disk` test block). (2) The LSP path deduplicated nothing, so sourcekit-lsp reporting a repeatedly-used property getter once per call site rendered `getter:panel` three times; callers/callees are now deduplicated by (name, uri, line). New `CallHierarchy.WithTopologyFallback`; guarded by `TestCallHierarchy_TopologyFallback`, `TestCallHierarchy_FallbackCallersFromReferences`, `TestCallHierarchy_TopologyFallbackDisabled`, and `TestCallHierarchy_DedupsOutgoing`.
- **`daemon_info` no longer reports `restart needed: yes` on a freshly-started daemon.** `RestartNeeded` compares the live config against a `cloneConfig` snapshot taken at startup, but `cloneConfig`/`cloneLSPConfig` copied slices with `append([]string(nil), x...)` — which returns `nil` for an empty-but-non-nil input. The compiled defaults use `Args: []string{}`, so the clone collapsed it to `nil`, the snapshot stopped being `reflect.DeepEqual` to the live config, and the restart flag latched `true` from the first second of every daemon (and never cleared, since no real change moved the generation). `cloneConfig`/`cloneLSPConfig` now use `slices.Clone`/`maps.Clone`, which preserve nil vs empty-non-nil exactly. Guarded by `TestCloneConfig_RoundTripsDefaults` and `TestRestartNeeded_FreshStoreIsFalse`.
- **Path-bearing tools now accept a workspace-relative path — a relative path no longer triggers a spurious `workspace boundary violation`.** A client that passed a relative path (e.g. `app/Sources/Foo.swift` rather than the absolute form) had it resolved by `filepath.Abs` against the **daemon's** working directory — and the daemon is a singleton that never `chdir`s to the workspace — so the resolved path landed outside the pinned workspace and every read/write/edit was refused as a boundary violation. Claude Code always sends absolute paths so it never tripped this; other clients that send relative paths hit it constantly and fell back to their native edit tools. Every path-bearing tool now resolves a relative argument against the connection's **pinned workspace root** before both the boundary check and the filesystem/LSP operation, via one shared seam: the package `resolvePath` (its prior `os.Getwd()` fallback — the same latent bug in `list_directory`/`list_files`/`find_files`/`search_in_files` — removed), a new `WriteDeps.resolvePath` for the write tools, and a new `toFileURIAnchored` for the uri-taking LSP tools (`get_definition`, `find_references`, `find_symbol`, `list_symbols`, `call_hierarchy`, `type_hierarchy`, `explain_symbol`, `file_outline`, `read_symbol`, `rename_symbol`, the four `*_symbol` edits, `diagnostics`). Absolute paths and `file://` URIs are unchanged; an unattached session leaves a relative path relative (so the boundary check still rejects it rather than touching a daemon-CWD file); and an escaping relative path (`../other`) still resolves and is correctly refused — the boundary check remains the safety net. Server-emitted URIs (rename's `WorkspaceEdit`, reference results) are left untouched. Tool schema descriptions now read "Absolute path, file:// URI, or workspace-relative path" (and `list_files` no longer claims it defaults to "the current working directory"). Guarded by `TestResolvePath`, `TestWriteDepsResolvePath`, `TestToFileURIAnchored`, `TestWriteFileResolvesRelativePath`, `TestWriteFileRelativeEscapeRejected`, `TestReadFileResolvesRelativePath`, and `TestEditFileResolvesRelativePath`.
- **`plumb setup antigravity` and `plumb doctor` now repoint and validate the *legacy flat* Antigravity configs, not just the new standalone files.** Antigravity reads MCP servers from more than the per-server `mcp/plumb.json` files setup writes: older builds and the shared Gemini config still consult flat `mcpServers`-wrapped `mcp_config.json` files under several `~/.gemini` subdirectories (`config/`, `antigravity-cli/`, `antigravity-ide/`, `antigravity/`). A plumb binary that moved or was rebuilt went stale in those files — and the standalone-only setup never touched them — so Antigravity kept launching a path that no longer existed (`fork/exec …/plumb: no such file or directory`) while `plumb doctor` reported a clean ✓ against the new files. Now `setupAntigravityInto` **creates or repoints** the plumb entry in every flat `mcp_config.json` Antigravity reads (the canonical `config/` one always; the per-surface dirs when they already exist; sibling servers preserved, existing files backed up), so `plumb setup antigravity` and `plumb setup --all` fix every location Antigravity reads; and `plumb doctor` adds an **"Antigravity (legacy)"** check that scans those files and reports a **missing** registered binary as a failure, a **mismatched-but-present** one as a warning, all-current as a clean pass (omitted entirely when no legacy file registers plumb). The `~/.gemini` base is derived from the standalone config path so the scan tracks wherever those files live. New `internal/cli/setup_antigravity.go`; guarded by `TestEnsureFlatAntigravityConfig_*` (creates-when-absent, repoint+preserve-siblings, idempotent), `TestEnsureAntigravityFlatConfigs_CreatesCanonicalAndExistingSurfaces`, `TestSetupAntigravityInto_RepointsLegacyConfigs`, `TestGeminiBaseFromStandalone`, and `TestCheckLegacyAntigravityConfigs`.
- **`get_definition` no longer errors on a server that returns a single `Location` object or `LocationLink`s.** `textDocument/definition` per the LSP spec returns `Location | Location[] | LocationLink[] | null`, but the Swift and Zig adapters decoded straight into `[]Location` — so zls's bare single-object `Location` response failed with `cannot unmarshal object into Go value of type []protocol.Location` (surfaced once the open-before-query fix below let zls actually answer). New `protocol.DecodeLocations` (`internal/lsp/protocol/locations.go`) normalises all four shapes to `[]Location` (array of `Location`, falling back to `LocationLink[]` when entries carry `targetUri`; single `Location`, else single `LocationLink`; a `LocationLink` collapses to its `targetSelectionRange`), and both adapters' `Definition` route through it. Verified against the pauta Zig monorepo: `get_definition` on a `.zig` identifier returns a real location. Guarded by `TestDecodeLocations` (six-shape matrix + malformed JSON) and `TestAdapter_Definition_SingleObject` in both adapters.
- **sourcekit-lsp (Swift) and zls (Zig) now serve per-document semantic queries — the whole LSP layer was dead for both.** Every position/document operation (`get_definition`, `find_references`, `call_hierarchy`/`type_hierarchy`, `explain_symbol` hover, `rename_symbol`, and push `diagnostics`) failed for Swift and Zig: sourcekit-lsp replied `-32001 "No language service for <uri> found"` and zls resolved nothing — while `workspace_sessions` advertised both as attached. Root cause: both servers serve those requests **only for documents opened via `textDocument/didOpen`** (like vscode-html-language-server), but the Swift and Zig adapters were modelled on gopls/pyright — which answer from disk without an open — and so issued `documentSymbol`/`definition`/etc. against never-opened files. plumb's external-edit model deliberately uses `didChangeWatchedFiles`, not the open-document lifecycle, so the file was never opened on the server. Both adapters now carry the html adapter's `ensureOpen`/`refreshOpen` pattern: a per-document query lazily `didOpen`s the file from disk (cached, one open per file) and a watched-file change `didClose`s the stale copy so the next query reopens it. Verified end-to-end against the pauta Swift+Zig monorepo: `find_references` returns real cross-file results for both languages and `diagnostics` resolves clean (was a 10s empty wait). Guarded by `TestAdapter_EnsureOpenBeforeQuery` and `TestAdapter_RefreshOpenReopensAfterWatchedChange` in both adapters. (zls does not implement `prepareCallHierarchy`; `call_hierarchy` for Zig now falls back to the topology call graph — see the entry above.)
- **The TUI no longer double-counts a monorepo language whose adapter is also listed (`swift, zig, zig`).** For a multi-language monorepo root the session's `DetectedLanguage` is already the deduped, comma-joined label (`swift, zig`), but `sessionLanguages` treated that whole string as a single primary entry and then *appended* each secondary adapter's language on top — so `zls` re-added `zig`, rendering `Languages: swift, zig, zig` in the Details pane and `SWIFT, ZIG  ZIG` badges in the list (the pauta repro). `sessionLanguages` now splits the joined primary label and dedups it against the adapter-derived languages. Guarded by an added `monorepo joined label not double-counted` case in `TestSessionLanguagesAndBadges`.
- **`make install-hooks` now works in a git submodule or worktree, not just a normal clone.** It hard-coded `.git/hooks/`, which is a directory only in a normal clone — in a submodule or linked worktree `.git` is a file (a gitdir pointer), so the `cp` failed with "Not a directory". It now resolves the hooks directory via `git rev-parse --git-path hooks` (which returns `.git/hooks` in a normal clone, so behaviour there is unchanged) and `mkdir -p`s it first.
- **`get_definition` and `find_references` by `symbol_name` now query the identifier, not the declaration keyword.** Both fed `DocumentSymbol.Range.Start` — the `func`/`type` keyword at column 0 — into the LSP position query instead of `SelectionRange.Start` (the identifier), so a real language server returned "no definition found" / "no identifier found" for essentially every Go top-level function or method looked up by name. The bug was masked because the unit-test mock returns a fixed location regardless of the queried position. Both now use `SelectionRange.Start`, matching the existing correct pattern in `symbol_edits.go`. The test mock records the queried position; guarded by `TestGetDefinition_ByName_UsesSelectionRange` and `TestFindReferences_ByName_UsesSelectionRange`.
- **plumb no longer lands its config/data in a throwaway temp directory when a shell session manager hijacks `XDG_*_HOME`.** Session managers such as `tsm` export `XDG_CONFIG_HOME` (and friends) pointing at a per-session temp dir, stashing the real value in a `TSM_ORIG_<var>` companion — so `internal/paths` (via `adrg/xdg`) resolved plumb's global config into a directory that vanishes with the session, making saved settings invisible. `internal/paths` now detects this (the live var resolves under a temp root *and* the `TSM_ORIG_<var>` companion is present — gating on the companion leaves legitimate temp-dir XDG usage in CI/tests untouched) and recovers the stashed original, falling back to the OS-native default when the original is also temp. The recovery is surfaced properly: a `WarnStyle` banner in `plumb config show` and a structured `slog.Warn` in the daemon log, exposed via the new `paths.RecoveredHijacks`. Guarded by `TestConfigDir_RecoversTSMHijack`, `TestConfigDir_HonoursTempXDGWithoutHijackSignal`, `TestConfigDir_HijackWithTempOriginFallsBackToDefault`, and `TestRecoveredHijacks_ReportsRecovery`.
- **`plumb serve` reconnect note no longer reports a stale daemon version after a modern→legacy daemon replacement.** `consumeInitializeResponse` adopted the replayed initialize response's `serverInfo.version` only when non-empty, so when a modern daemon (which reports a version) was replaced on reconnect by a legacy one (no `serverInfo`), the note kept reporting the dead modern daemon's version instead of falling back to the proxy's. It now adopts the new daemon's version unconditionally — including empty, which correctly triggers the proxy-version fallback. Guarded by `TestProxyReconnectNote_ModernThenLegacy`.
- **`edit_file` now computes its Myers edit script once per successful edit instead of twice.** `formatEditFileSuccess` ran `computeEditScript` over the same before/after content twice — once for the "lines changed" summary and again for the unified diff — so an edit with `show_write_diff` on (the default) paid the diff cost twice. The script is now computed once and shared by both via the new `summariseEditScript` and `renderUnifiedDiff` helpers; the public `summariseLineChanges`/`unifiedDiff` wrappers are unchanged for their other callers. Behaviour-preserving (covered by the existing `TestSummariseLineChanges*` and `edit_file` diff tests).
- **Workspace language detection's display path now stops at `$HOME`.** `detectAnyLanguageAt` — which fills the TUI's "detected language" label for a `LanguageNone` workspace — walked ancestors with no `$HOME` boundary, unlike the authoritative `Detect`/`detectLanguageAt` walks fixed in 0.9.17, so a stray `~/package.json` (or other home marker) could cosmetically mislabel a markerless workspace beneath `$HOME`. It now stops at `$HOME` like the other walks. Guarded by `TestDetectAnyLanguageAt_StopsAtHome`.

### Tests

- **Restored CI green: synced the self-test checklist with the new tools and de-flaked the stats timing guard.** The 0.9.19 `run_task`/`agent_config` tools were registered without a self-test checklist entry, so the `cmd/smoke` parity guard (`TestSmoke_ToolListParity`) failed on the live `tools/list`. Added a `selftestTasksConfig` coverage group (read-only Tier A: `agent_config describe` + a non-mutating `run_task`) so the canonical list matches the registry again. Separately, `TestStatsStore_RecordReturnsFast` timed the *first* `Record` — which lazily opens the stats DB and runs migrations synchronously — and that one-time cold-start cost could exceed the 200 ms budget on a loaded CI runner; it now warms the writer (`ensureWriter`) before the timed loop, so it measures only the async enqueue path it intends to guard.
- **Closed two coverage gaps in the 0.9.17 Settings fixes:** `TestClampSettingsValueW` exercises the value-column clamp (the layout-corruption fix), and `TestHandlePasteMsg_Routing` exercises the paste-routing priority (list editor, rename-modal precedence, drop-when-no-input). Both were previously only exercised indirectly.
- **The Swift `topology_routes` e2e now exercises the production extractor.** `TestTopologyRoutes_ArgumentParserEndToEnd` opened topology with the init-failure fallback `treesitter.NewSwift`; it now uses the production `wasmts.NewSwift` (canonical-grammar WASM) so it proves the real route path, not the fallback.
- **New guard against tool/language/client count drift across the docs and website.** `TestDocToolCountMatchesRegistry` (`internal/cli/doc_counts_test.go`) derives the tool count from the `srv.Register(tools.…)` calls in `conn_register.go` and asserts every place that restates it — `README.md`, `docs/tools.md`, `docs/architecture.md`, `docs/token-efficiency.md`, `docs/index.md`, and `site/index.html` (digit and prose forms) — matches, so adding or removing a tool without updating the prose now fails CI. `TestLanguageAndClientSourceCountsPinned` pins the `langsupport.All()` and `allSetupClients()` source counts, pointing at the editorial display strings (the site's "17 languages" folds the `.tsx` alias; "12 AI clients" collapses the two Antigravity entries) to revisit when either changes. Mirrors `TestServerJSONVersionMatchesVERSION`.

### Changed

- **`make docker-cleanroom` build context no longer ships local `.plumb/` state.** `.dockerignore` now excludes `.plumb` so the cleanroom builder's `COPY . .` does not send the workspace's generated topology/memory databases into the Docker build context.
- **The public website now uses the modern multi-agent launch page.** `site/index.html` has been replaced with the polished modern page, the temporary draft HTML files have been removed, and the page now ships with refreshed favicon and Open Graph assets generated from the plumb logo.
- **Website and docs now reflect the `run_task`/`agent_config` tools and the true 53-tool count.** The site's toolset section gains a seventh **“Tasks & config”** capability group (`run_task`, `agent_config`) and the structured-tool stat now reads 53 (was 50); the tools grid centres the trailing card so seven groups tile cleanly. The stale “51 tools” count is corrected to 53 across `docs/tools.md`, `README.md`, `docs/architecture.md`, `docs/index.md`, and `docs/token-efficiency.md` (the agent briefs already said 53).
- **Client-count and Antigravity setup paths corrected across the site and docs.** The website's "AI clients" stat now reads 12 (was 11), matching the page's own "Twelve agents" heading and chips. `docs/cli-reference.md` gains the `plumb setup antigravity-desktop` row and its `plumb setup antigravity` path is corrected to `~/.gemini/antigravity-cli/mcp/plumb.json` (was the stale `mcp_config.json`), so the reference matches `AntigravityConfigPath`/`AntigravityDesktopConfigPath`.

### Docs

- **`CONTRIBUTING.md` now walks an outside contributor through the fork + pull-request flow.** The guide assumed a maintainer cloning `plumbkit/plumb` directly; it now opens with the fork-first path (fork → clone your fork → add an `upstream` remote), shows the branch → `make verify` → push-to-fork → open-PR loop, and cross-links the existing `CODE_OF_CONDUCT.md`, `SECURITY.md` (report privately, not via a public issue), and the structured issue forms. It also documents the `main` branch-protection expectations — required CI matrix (`verify`/`race`/`integration` on Linux + macOS), one maintainer approval, up-to-date branch — and refreshes the `make verify` target list (`build test lint build-integration build-clients check-size`).
- **GitHub Discussions is enabled, and `CONTRIBUTING.md` now routes proposals there.** The “discuss large changes first” step points features, design ideas, open questions, and “would you accept a PR that…?” to [Discussions](https://github.com/plumbkit/plumb/discussions); issues are reserved for confirmed bugs and agreed, actionable work, keeping the tracker a to-do list rather than a forum. A short “Getting help” section points the same way.
- **A versioned road to 1.0 ([`docs/roadmap.md`](docs/roadmap.md)).** Rather than jump from 0.9 straight to 1.0, Plumb now ships a themed series of minor releases — **0.10 through 0.19, with 0.19.x the last 0.x** — before 1.0 lands as a deliberate stability commitment; native Windows support is an explicit post-1.0 (1.1) item, not a 1.0 gate. The new doc lays out the per-minor themes and rationale; the README `Roadmap` section is reframed to point at it.

## 0.9.18 (unreleased)

Swift's structural extraction moved off the pure-Go gotreesitter port onto the canonical grammar compiled to WASM, fixing the implicitly-unwrapped-optional collapse at the root, plus a dependency refresh.

### Fixed

- **Swift outline no longer collapses on an implicitly-unwrapped optional property (`var x: T!`) — fixed at the root by moving Swift onto the canonical grammar via WASM.** The pure-Go gotreesitter Swift grammar cannot parse an implicitly-unwrapped optional *type* — `var manager: Manager!`, `@IBOutlet var label: NSTextField!` — and emits an `ERROR` that cascades up the tree and collapses the *entire* enclosing `class`/`struct` declaration: the type, its properties, and its methods all vanished from `file_outline`/topology. Since `T!` is pervasive in AppKit/UIKit, real macOS/iOS files (e.g. the reported NoCaps `AppDelegate`) outlined as nothing but their `import`s. 0.9.17 shipped a byte-blanking workaround; this release replaces it with a root fix. Investigation proved the defect is in gotreesitter's parser-core lexer — its immediate-token vs external-token disambiguation in type position, where the IUO `!` is an `IMMEDIATE_TOKEN` resolved by the core lexer, not by the external `scanner.c` — and not in the grammar: the canonical alex-pinkus grammar defines `_possibly_implicitly_unwrapped_type` correctly, and the bug is undocumented upstream because gotreesitter is a niche port (the widely-used grammar handles `T!` fine); a v0.20.2 bump does not fix it (it only changes the error shape, and in fact breaks the 0.9.17 workaround). Swift now extracts via the **canonical `tree-sitter-swift` grammar (alex-pinkus 0.7.1) + its C external scanner compiled to WASM** (`swift.wasm`, driven by wazero, pure-Go at runtime) in the `wasmts` package — the same proven route TS/TSX took. The class, its members, and the `T!` *in method-parameter signatures* all survive (the latter a fidelity the byte-blanking workaround could not preserve). The canonical-grammar walk also extracts members the gotreesitter extractor dropped — initializers (`init`, including failable `init?`), `deinit`, `subscript`, operator functions (named by their operator token, e.g. `==`/`+`), and `typealias` — and was stress-tested clean (zero ERROR nodes) against realistic SwiftUI/Combine code (result builders, generics, `async`/`await`, actors, property wrappers, associated types). The `wasmts` runtime was generalised to host multiple grammars; the gotreesitter Swift extractor and its `recoverIUOBangs` workaround are retained only as the wasm init-failure fallback, with a tripwire test (`TestSwift_IUO_GotreesitterStillBroken`) and `todo.md` follow-ups to retire them (and to file an upstream gotreesitter fix/PR). Guarded by `TestSwift_KindsExtracted`, `TestSwift_ImplicitlyUnwrappedOptional`, `TestSwift_InitDeinitSubscript`, `TestSwift_Containment`, and `TestSwift_CallEdge` in the `wasmts` package. Regenerate the grammar bundle with `make swift-wasm` (needs Zig).

- **Xcode-app projects now detect as Swift (`*.xcodeproj`/`*.xcworkspace` root markers).** An Xcode app has no SwiftPM `Package.swift`, so workspace detection resolved it to `LanguageNone` — no primary Swift server attached and every semantic tool returned "not ready" (observed live: `NoCaps` showed `Language: none`). `[lsp.swift].root_markers` now also includes the globs `*.xcodeproj` and `*.xcworkspace`; the three marker-matching sites (`strongLangAt`, `weakLangAt`, `detectAnyLanguageAt`) gained glob support via a shared `markerPresent` helper (a `*` in a marker is `filepath.Glob`-matched, else exact `os.Stat`). A bare `.xcodeproj` now resolves as Swift and attaches sourcekit-lsp. (Note: sourcekit-lsp's cross-file index — `workspace_symbols`, `find_references`, `get_definition` — still needs build args an `.xcodeproj` doesn't supply without a build server; that Xcode/BSP integration is tracked separately. Structural tools — `file_outline`, topology — work fully.) Guarded by `TestDetect_XcodeProjMarker`, `TestDetect_XcodeProjFromSubdir`, `TestDetect_XcworkspaceMarker`.

### Changed

- **Dependencies refreshed to latest; gotreesitter deliberately held at v0.20.1.** `go get -u ./...` brought the direct/indirect tree to current (`modernc.org/sqlite` 1.52.0, `modernc.org/libc` 1.73.0, `golang.org/x/sys` 0.46.0, `golang.org/x/sync` 0.21.0, `github.com/dlclark/regexp2/v2` 2.2.1, `github.com/charmbracelet/ultraviolet`). `github.com/odvcencio/gotreesitter` is the one held-back pin: its v0.20.2 changes the Swift implicitly-unwrapped-optional error shape in a way that breaks the `recoverIUOBangs` fallback workaround for **no** offsetting gain (it does not fix the underlying `T!` collapse — see the Swift WASM entry above), so it stays at v0.20.1 until the gotreesitter Swift fallback is retired.

## 0.9.17 (unreleased)

The memory roadmap wave: `workspace_search` ranked discovery across code, docs, and memories, plus the topology ↔ memory join (CodeRef resolver, staleness surfacing, related-memory sections on the topology tools, once-per-session hint suppression).

### Fixed

- **The self-test tool-list parity guard no longer lags the tool registry.** `TestSmoke_ToolListParity` (`cmd/smoke`, `//go:build integration`) asserts every registered tool appears in the self-test checklist (`internal/mcp/selftest_prompt.go`), but three tools had drifted ahead of it: `workspace_search` (the new 51st tool), `structural_query`, and `workspace_sessions`. The checklist now lists them (`structural_query`/`workspace_search` under the topology group, `workspace_sessions` under the session group). The gap was invisible to `make verify` because the parity test is integration-gated; it surfaced via the new `make docker-integration` harness (and would have reddened the CI integration job on both ubuntu and macOS).
