- **`topology_status` now reports indexed languages (the `languages:` line was always blank).** The tool's description promises a `languages:` line and `FormatStatus` renders one from `Status.Languages` (a `SELECT DISTINCT language FROM topology_files`), but the indexer never wrote the `topology_files.language` column — its INSERT/UPDATE omitted it — so the column was always empty and the line never appeared. The indexer now threads each file's language (from the extractor's `Language()`) through `extractPath` → `persistFile` → `upsertFileRecord` and writes it on every upsert, so `topology_status` (and any consumer of `Status.Languages`) shows the real per-workspace language set. Existing indexes backfill the column as each file is next re-indexed (on change or a resync). Guarded by `TestIndexer_PopulatesLanguageInStatus`.

- **Workspace language detection no longer crosses `$HOME` — a Swift/Xcode project under home stopped misdetecting as TypeScript.** `detectLanguageAt` (and `Detect`'s main-loop language-marker check) walked up from the workspace to the filesystem root with no `$HOME` boundary, so a project with a `.plumb/` marker but no language root marker of its own (an Xcode app has no SwiftPM `Package.swift`) inherited the *first* enabled language marker found in any ancestor — including a stray global `~/package.json` (the file npm and many tools drop in `$HOME`), which is a `typescript` root marker. The result: an unambiguous Swift app reported `Language: TypeScript`. The `.git` fallback already had a `$HOME` identity guard (`sameDirAs`); the two language-marker walks now share it, so `$HOME` and anything above it are never consulted for the language and such a workspace resolves as `LanguageNone` instead. (The `.json` file count in the report was a red herring — a single `~/package.json` is the trigger; detection is marker-based, not file-vote-based.) Guarded by `TestDetect_StrayHomeMarkerDoesNotCaptureViaPlumb` and `TestDetect_StrayHomeMarkerRefusedViaAscent`.

- **The automatic concurrent-edit guard now confirms by content hash, catching peer writes that leave the mtime unchanged.** `changedSinceSessionRead` — the session-aware staleness guard that fires when a caller passes no explicit `expected_mtime`/`expected_sha` — compared only the on-disk mtime against the mtime recorded at read time, so a peer write that landed in the same mtime tick, or a tool that preserves mtime (`cp -p`, some formatters), changed the content invisibly and a blind `write_file` overwrite could silently clobber it. `ReadTracker` now records the content SHA-256 `read_file` already computes alongside the mtime, and the guard uses mtime as the cheap first signal (an advanced mtime is flagged with no hashing) then falls back to a SHA comparison only when the mtime did not advance — so the common write stays hash-free while the ambiguous case is caught. The explicit `expected_sha` path was already precise; this brings the automatic net to the same precision. Guarded by the new `TestChangedSinceSessionRead` (covering mtime-advanced, same-mtime-unchanged, mtime-preserved-content-changed, and the no-recorded-sha fallback). `ReadTracker.Record` gains a `sha` parameter; its three call sites (`read_file`, `read_symbol`, the post-write refresh) pass the hash they already have.

- **`edit_file`'s "lines changed" summary no longer over-reports on large files.** `summariseLineChanges` compared the before/after line arrays positionally (`bl[i]` vs `al[i]`), so a single small insertion near the top of a long file shifted every line below it by one index and flagged them all as changed — a one-paragraph insert into the 425 KB `CHANGELOG.md` reported `…(+312 more)`. It now walks the Myers edit script already produced for the unified diff (`computeEditScript` + `diffSplitLines` from `diff.go`), so a run of additions reports just the new-file lines it added and unrelated downstream lines are never flagged; line numbers now also match the unified-diff hunk headers in the same response (`diffSplitLines` drops the trailing-newline artefact the old `strings.Split` counted). The fix stays inside `summariseLineChanges`; its five call sites are unchanged. Guarded by the new `TestSummariseLineChanges` (with the insertion regression as the load-bearing case) and `TestSummariseLineChanges_MatchesDiffNumbering`.

- **TUI settings: long values can no longer corrupt the layout, the editor popups widen to fit, and every text input accepts paste.** A long path in `extra_roots`/`read_roots` widened the settings value column past the rows pane, so the fixed-width cell render wrapped the row and broke the borders; the value column is now clamped to the pane width and row values (and list continuation lines) are ellipsis-truncated to fit. The list/text editor popups, which hard-truncated entries at 32 columns, now size their field to the longest entry (or the live input), capped at a 4-cell margin from each screen edge — so the popup shows the full path the row elides. And pasting now works in every text input (settings list/text editors, rename-session modal, memory filter, log filter): Bubble Tea v2 delivers bracketed paste as a dedicated `PasteMsg` the update loop never routed, and the key handlers' printable-ASCII filter meant pasted text was silently dropped; a new `handlePasteMsg` routes sanitised single-line paste (newlines/tabs → spaces, control runes dropped, non-ASCII kept) to the active input, and a paste while browsing a list editor opens a new-entry input holding the pasted text. Guarded by `TestEditorFieldWidth`, `TestSanitisePaste`, and `TestListEditorPaste`.

- **The reconnect note now reports the daemon's version, not the proxy's — and says when the two differ.** Observed live during this release's upgrade: after `plumb restart`, a long-lived session's one-shot note said "daemon reconnected (now 0.9.16)" while the fresh daemon was 0.9.17 — `annotateReconnect` passed the serve proxy's own compiled `Version`, and a long-lived proxy always predates an upgraded daemon. The proxy now captures `result.serverInfo.version` from the daemon's initialize response (both the first-connect response and the post-reconnect replay, where it is the *new* daemon answering) and the note reports it; when daemon and proxy versions differ it adds "this serve proxy is still ‹v› — start a new client session to refresh it", the only in-band signal of proxy lag after an upgrade. A daemon whose initialize response carries no `serverInfo` falls back to the old wording. Guarded by `TestServerInfoVersion`, `TestReconnectNoteText`, the extended `TestProxyReconnectNote` (distinct mock daemon version; asserts the daemon's version, not the proxy's), and `TestProxyReconnectNote_LegacyDaemonShape`.

- **A tool call sent at the instant of daemon death can no longer hang the client forever (the proxy-test family's long-standing "flake" was this bug).** Track-after-write left a real race: the pump writes a request, the daemon dies, and the daemon pump's reconnect runs its outstanding-request sweep *before* the client pump records the request — the late-tracked entry then sat in `outstanding` with no daemon ever going to answer it and no synthesised error either, so the client (agent) hung until its own timeout. Raising the harness deadlines from 3 s to 10 s converted the "load flake" into a hard never-arrives failure (~1 in 4 `-count=5` family runs), proving it was never scheduling slowness. Fix: `outstanding` entries now carry the connection generation they were written under; the reconnect sweep runs *after* the generation bump and fails only entries from older generations (`failOutstandingBelow`), and `trackOutstanding` re-checks the generation after storing — whichever side deletes the entry synthesises the single `-32000` retry error, so exactly one response reaches the client in every interleaving. Ten consecutive `-count=5` family runs green; race-clean. Guarded by `TestTrackOutstanding_LateTrackAfterReconnect` (deterministic reproduction of the gap).

- **Memory-roadmap review pass: docs corpus can no longer be starved, dotted symbol references resolve, and a seen hint frees its slot.** Four findings from the independent review of the 0.9.17 wave. (1) *Docs starvation:* `workspace_search`'s code and docs corpora shared one ranked topology query budget, so in a code-heavy repo the top hits were all code and the docs corpus returned nothing; docs is now served by dedicated language-filtered queries (Markdown, HTML) with its own budget. (2) *Dotted references:* provenance `source_symbols` come from symbol-query args, which accept the dotted `ReceiverType.MethodName` form — but topology node names are bare and Go qualified names use `(*Recv).Method`, so `read_memory`'s stale-check falsely flagged dotted references as missing and symbol-aware hints/joins missed them. New `memory.SymbolBase` compares the base segment everywhere (stale-check retries it before flagging; `refMatch` and hint matching accept it). (3) *Hint slots:* the `max_hints` cap was applied before suppression filtering, so once the top-ranked memories had been hinted, unseen ones ranked below the cap could never surface for the rest of the session; suppression now runs before the cap. (4) The TUI memory detail panel now shows an `Origin` row for machine-written memories (the wave's own noted follow-up). Guarded by `TestWorkspaceSearch_DocsNotStarvedByCode`, `TestSymbolBase`, `TestMemoriesForRefs_DottedSourceSymbol`, the extended `TestStaleSymbolsNote`/`TestMatchingMemoryNames_SymbolRefs`, `TestUnseenHints_CapAfterSuppression`, and `TestMemoryDetailShowsOriginForGenerated`.

### Added

- **Tokens-saved metric rebuilt as a counterfactual, two-axis token-efficiency model.** The old single "tokens saved" number came from a hardcoded per-client `profiles[client][tool]` table recomputed on every read; the hot-path tools (`read_file`, `edit_file`, `git`) earned zero, roughly 80% of the lifetime figure was one legacy `diagnostics` artefact, and changing the table silently rewrote all history. It is replaced by `internal/clientcaps`, a stdlib-only client-capability registry (one struct literal per client, subsuming `normaliseClient`) plus a counterfactual scorer that values each call on two honest axes: **capability tokens** (work a client could not do natively; dominant for thin clients like Claude Desktop) and **efficiency tokens** (fewer tokens for the same result; dominant for capable CLI agents), using per-family, per-content-type tokeniser ratios in place of one global chars-per-token constant. Savings are scored once at write time in `connSession.onAfterTool` and stored with their model version (schema v8 to v12 adds `tokens_saved`, `savings_model_version`, `capability_tokens`, `efficiency_tokens`); `read_file`/`read_symbol` emit a `baseline=<bytes>` header so a ranged read is credited the context it avoided pulling into the window. `plumb stats`, `session_start`, and the TUI ("Token Efficiency") now show both axes plus the active model version, never "tokens saved". The legacy recompute path and the `profiles`/`normaliseClient`/`HasSavingsModel`/`charsPerToken` machinery are deleted: totals are a trivial `SUM` of stored, versioned rows, and pre-redesign rows (`savings_model_version = 0`) are excluded rather than dishonestly rescored. Separately, `release.yml` now jq-stamps `server.json` from the release tag and publishes to the MCP registry via GitHub OIDC.

- **`session_start` gains an optional `language` arg to force the primary when detection can't infer it.** Some projects have a language plumb supports but no root marker that names it — the canonical case is an Xcode app: `.swift` sources, but the build is driven by an `.xcodeproj`, not a SwiftPM `Package.swift`, so detection resolves `LanguageNone` and `workspace_symbols` / the call-and-type hierarchies (which consult the *primary* server) have nothing to attach to. Passing `language: "swift"` (the `[lsp.<lang>]` key) now re-pins the current workspace — or pins alongside an explicit `workspace` — to that server as the primary and shows it in the identity line, even though no marker named it. The override is gated on the language being active (installed + enabled via the automatic-enablement work below); an unknown, uninstalled, or disabled value is ignored and normal detection applies, so a typo or an absent server never breaks the bootstrap. Threaded through `repinWorkspace(folder, langOverride)` and `attachOrRepinTo` (whose same-root no-op now also re-acquires on a primary-language change); `pool.hasActiveLanguage` validates the override; the displayed label prefers the attached primary (`labelForLSPKey`) over marker detection. Guarded by `TestSessionStart_LanguageOverride`, `TestRepinWorkspace_IgnoresInactiveLanguageOverride`, and `TestHasActiveLanguage`. AGENTS.md § Workspace detection and the tool's own description document it.

- **Automatic LSP enablement (install → on) + strong/weak root markers.** Two changes to how plumb decides which language servers run and how it identifies a project's language, motivated by a Swift/Xcode project under `$HOME` misdetecting as TypeScript. **(1) Automatic enablement.** Every `[lsp.<lang>]` now defaults to `enabled = true`; the *effective* state is that intent gated on the server binary actually being installed (`exec.LookPath`, cross-platform — honours `PATHEXT` on Windows, plain PATH on macOS/Linux), resolved by the new `lspActive` helper. Install `rust-analyzer` and Rust activates for every Cargo project with zero config (the nvim/Mason model); a language whose server is absent stays dormant at no cost and — crucially — its root markers never enter workspace detection; `enabled = false` excludes a language even when installed. The pool's active-language set, the daemon startup check (now a non-fatal warning, since a topology-only daemon is legitimate), `plumb doctor` (uninstalled = optional, not an error), and `plumb config show` (a new derived `active` row: `yes (installed)` / `no (… not installed)` / `no (disabled in config)`) all consult the effective state. **(2) Strong vs weak root markers.** Promiscuous markers — `package.json` (typescript), `index.html` (html) — moved to a new `weak_root_markers` config field: a weak marker names the language only of the directory it sits in directly (the resolution dir, or a `.git/`/`.plumb/` boundary), never an ancestor, so a stray tooling `package.json` up the tree (a docs build, a global `~/package.json`) can no longer hijack a Go/Swift/Rust workspace as TypeScript while a real JS/TS project still resolves; strong markers always beat weak ones at the same directory. Together with the `$HOME`-bounded ascent (below) these make the reported misdetection impossible from automatic mode (an uninstalled typescript-language-server is never active, so `package.json` is not even a marker). Guarded by `TestLspInstalled`, `TestLspActive`, `TestNewWorkspacePool_InstallGatesLangs`, and `TestDetect_{WeakMarkerAtStartDir,WeakMarkerAtGitRoot,StrongBeatsWeak,WeakMarkerInAncestorIgnored,PlumbRootWeakMarkerAtRoot,PlumbRootWeakMarkerInSubdirIgnored}`. AGENTS.md § Workspace detection documents both.

- **Topology ↔ memory join: memories now surface where the code is.** The join contract is `memory.CodeRef` (stable fields — file path, symbol name, kind; never topology row IDs, which a reindex invalidates) and the pure resolver `memory.MemoriesForRefs`, matching provenance `source_symbols` (exact identifier), `paths:` globs, and provenance `source_paths` against a ref set, user-authored first — the same slot rule as the hint block. Memory never imports topology and topology never depends on memory; the join happens in Go at the tool layer. Four surfaces light up: **`topology_explore`** and **`topology_affected`** append a budgeted "Related memories" section (≤3 names + descriptions + the match reason, never bodies) for the explored neighbourhood / the changed-and-affected set; **`read_memory`** stale-checks a generated memory's referenced symbols against the live code map and flags the ones that no longer resolve ("may describe code that has moved or been removed"; capped at 8 lookups); and **`session_start`** orders the memories list so those attached to a recently modified file lead. `memory.Memory` now carries `SourcePaths`/`SourceSymbols` parsed from frontmatter. Guarded by `TestMemoriesForRefs{,_CapAndEmpty}`, `TestList_PopulatesSourceRefs`, `TestStaleSymbolsNote`, `TestTopologyExplore_RelatedMemories`, `TestTopologyAffected_KnownContext`, and `TestRecentFirstMemories`.

- **Hint injection: once-per-session suppression + symbol-aware matching on edits.** Each memory now hints at most once per connection (a small seen-set on the session, cleared on re-pin) — after the first pointer, repeating the same hint on every read of a hot path was pure noise (delivers the review plan's B2 W3). And for `edit_file`/`write_file`, hint matching now also consults the topology index: a memory whose provenance references a symbol recorded in the edited file hints even when no paths glob matches (one indexed query per edit; `read_file` stays path-glob-only — it dominates call volume). Guarded by `TestEnrichToolOutput_HintOnceQuiet` and `TestMatchingMemoryNames_SymbolRefs`.

- **`workspace_search` — ranked discovery across code, docs, and memories in one call (51st tool).** The broker over the existing indexed backends: code and doc sections (Markdown/HTML headings) from the topology FTS5 index plus memories (`memory.Index.Search`); each corpus gets its own query budget (docs via dedicated language-filtered queries — see the review fix above). Results are ranked within each corpus and interleaved round-robin by per-corpus rank — raw FTS5 scores are never compared across indexes — and every hit carries the labelling contract: `corpus`, `source`, `field`, `score`, `why`, with per-corpus index freshness (`fresh|stale|building|missing|skipped`) and `exact_match=false` in the header. Degrades honestly: a nil topology store or absent memory index reports `missing` while the other corpora still serve; a stale memory index serves stale-labelled results and kicks the async self-heal reindex (mirroring `search_memories` auto mode); an empty result points at `search_in_files` for the exact lane. The two-lane contract is now stated in all four search tools' descriptions (`search_in_files` exact / `workspace_search` ranked, with `topology_search` and `search_memories` named as its corpus-specific backends) and the discovery ladder documented in `docs/tools.md` + `AGENTS.md`. Guarded by `TestWorkspaceSearch_{AllCorporaLabelled,MemoryOnlyDegradation,NoMemoryIndexReportsMissing,CorporaFilter,EmptyPointsAtExactScan,RejectsBadArgs}` and `TestInterleaveHits`.

- **In-process multi-session coexistence tests (review-plan B4 W1).** `internal/tools/multi_session_test.go` proves the two-agents-one-repo write contract at the unit tier, with each session carrying its own fully-wired per-session deps (`newSessionDeps`: ReadTracker, WriteTracker, rate limiter) over the process-global per-path locks: concurrent edits to one path serialise with both markers landing exactly once; a stale `expected_mtime`/`expected_sha` from before a peer's edit is refused; an unguarded overwrite after a peer's edit trips the session-aware staleness guard (write_file refuses, edit_file warns); a transaction guarded by a pre-conflict sha rejects all-or-nothing with no txlog orphan; and eight racing full-file writers leave exactly one intact payload, never a torn mix. All green under `-race`.

- **Daemon-tier two-session smoke test (review-plan B4 W2).** `cmd/smoke/twosession_test.go` (gated `//go:build integration`) drives two real `plumb serve` proxies against one shared daemon in an isolated HOME/XDG tree, on a marker-only `LanguageNone` workspace so no language server is needed: session A reads and captures the version header, session B edits the same file, A's edit guarded by the now-stale `expected_mtime` is rejected over the wire with the staleness message, B's content survives intact, and `workspace_sessions` shows both sessions to each other. Together with the B4 W1 unit tier this proves the multi-agent write contract end to end.

- **Docker-based Linux testing for a macOS dev machine (two opt-in make targets).** plumb is developed on macOS but ships for Linux; CI already runs the Linux suites on `ubuntu-latest`, but a developer could neither reproduce a red Linux integration run locally nor prove a *fresh* Linux box installs and runs plumb. `make docker-integration` (`build/docker/integration.Dockerfile`) mirrors the CI `integration` job — a `golang:1.26-bookworm` image with real gopls + pyright, the repo bind-mounted so it always reflects the working tree, cached Go build/module volumes for fast reruns — and runs `make integration-test` on Linux. `make docker-cleanroom` (`build/docker/cleanroom.Dockerfile`) is the automatable "clean-VM verification" the launch risk register asks for before tagging: a multi-stage build compiles a pure-Go (`CGO_ENABLED=0`) binary, then a `debian:bookworm-slim` runtime carrying only `bash` + `python3` — no toolchain — copies in just the binary and runs the existing two-agents MCP e2e (`docs/demos/two-agents-one-file.sh`) against it, so the container exit code is the verdict. Both build arm64-native by default (set `DOCKER_PLATFORM=linux/amd64` for emulated amd64 fidelity); neither runs in `make verify`. A new `.dockerignore` keeps the cleanroom build context lean.

- **`server.json` can no longer drift from `VERSION` (review-plan B2 W2).** The MCP registry metadata had sat at `0.9.7` while the repo reached `0.9.17`; `server.json` is bumped and the new `TestServerJSONVersionMatchesVERSION` (`internal/cli/version_meta_test.go`) asserts the pair agree, so a VERSION bump without the matching `server.json` change fails `make test`. Verified red on a deliberate mismatch.

### Documentation

- **`docs/use-cases.md` — measured, reproducible tool comparisons (linked from the README).** A public page with four commit-pinned head-to-head measurements of plumb's tools against the standard native tooling (`grep`/`ripgrep`/whole-file read), with a provenance block (commit, client, model, daemon version, platform) so every number is credible and reproducible. Honest by design — it shows the wins and the washes: `read_symbol` ~8.5× fewer tokens than a whole-file read, `file_outline` ~3.9× fewer, project text search a token *wash* vs `ripgrep` (plumb's value there is symbol annotation + scoping, not size), and `find_references` 9 true call sites / 4 files vs `grep`'s 16 matches / 7 files (~44% noise) — a precision win, not a size one. The reproduce steps pin `git checkout a0885ea` because the doc itself now adds textual matches for the sample symbol — a live demonstration of the Scenario 4 thesis. Methodology + a backlog of further measurements recorded internally.

- **Runnable "two agents, one file" demo (review-plan Positioning W2).** `docs/demos/two-agents-one-file.sh` is a self-contained, reproducible demo: it builds or finds a plumb binary, spins up an isolated HOME with its own daemon, drives two real `plumb serve` sessions over stdio, and shows the guardrail live: Agent B's edit lands, Agent A's stale guarded edit is refused with the "was modified since you read it" message, the final file keeps B's change, and `workspace_sessions` shows both agents. The demo mirrors the B4 test scenarios by design, so the pitch and the test suite prove the same thing; linked from the README's write-safety pillar.

- **Platform and adapter claims now match the retested reality (review-plan B2 W1).** `README.md` no longer claims Linux real-binary validation: macOS only, with Linux integration running in CI and being hardened pre-v1; the experimental tier row now says navigation works against the real servers while diagnostics validation is still in progress. `AGENTS.md`'s adapter-validation intro and the zls / typescript-language-server / kotlin-language-server rows replace the stale "skips until the binary is on PATH" story with the 2026-06-10 retest result: `TestIntegration_DocumentSymbols` passes but `TestIntegration_DidChangeWatchedFiles` fails (zls and typescript-language-server appear to use pull diagnostics; kotlin-language-server needs a real Gradle/Maven project), so the three stay experimental until pull-diagnostics support lands.

## 0.9.16 (unreleased)

Independent dual review of the Advanced Memory Engine (0.9.10) — a §1–7 checklist agent plus a 3-finder `/code-review` pass — surfaced one hot-path perf bug, two real correctness bugs, and a tail of minors a single-author self-review missed. This release fixes **every** finding: the memory hint path no longer re-reads project config on every `read_file`; `search_memories` no longer silently regresses substring search; the index no longer races its own shutdown; episodic summaries are accurate and always fire before eviction; and a round of redaction-coverage and dedup cleanups.

### Changed

- **The optimistic-concurrency guards of `edit_file` and `write_file` now share one implementation.** `edit_file`'s `checkExpectedVersion` delegates to the shared `verifyExpectedVersion` (`write_guards.go`), keeping only its `reconcile` skip and `editLogicErr` wrapping. The ~25-line duplication was deliberate when shipped (0.9.15 kept churn off the then-concurrently-edited `edit_file` files); the 0.9.15 review accepted the guards and folded the siblings now the tree has settled. Behaviour-preserving — wording and semantics were already identical, and the existing guard tests for both tools pin them.

- **Memory hint injection no longer re-reads `.plumb/config.toml` on the `read_file` hot path.** `enrichToolOutput` (run on every `read_file`/`edit_file`/`write_file`/`read_symbol`/`file_outline` success — thousands of `read_file` calls/session) called `memoryConfigFor(ws)` → `config.LoadProject`, doing an `os.ReadFile` + TOML parse + clone + validate of the project config **per call**, in violation of the `EnrichToolOutput` "must be cheap" contract. The resolved `[memory]` config is now snapshotted into the lock-free `sessionView` (seeded from global config at construction, swapped per project on every attach / re-pin / reload, exactly like `[edits]`/`[git]`/`[semantics]`), read via `s.memoryConfig()`. The same per-call load is removed from `memoryIndexLive`, `latestEpisodic`, and `generateEpisodicSummary`; `memoryConfigFor` is deleted. Guarded by `TestApplyProjectConfig_SnapshotsMemory`.

### Fixed

- **`search_memories` no longer silently regresses substring search, honours `case_sensitive`, and self-heals a stale index.** Three bugs in the auto-mode FTS path: (1) on a *fresh* index, a substring FTS5's whole-token `unicode61` tokeniser can't represent (e.g. `essio` inside `UserSession`) returned `No memory matches (source=memory-fts)` and **never fell back to grep** — a real regression vs the pre-0.9.10 grep-only tool; auto mode now greps on zero FTS hits (a literal `mode=fts` keeps the empty FTS result). (2) `case_sensitive: true` was silently ignored on the FTS path (FTS5 is case-insensitive); it now forces the grep path. (3) A stale index in auto mode fell to grep but never reindexed, so FTS stayed cold until the next write/attach; it now kicks a new `Index.ReindexAsync` (single-flight `atomic.Bool` CAS guard) so subsequent queries self-heal back onto ranked FTS. Guarded by `TestSearchMemories_AutoZeroFtsHitFallsToGrep`, `_CaseSensitiveForcesGrep`, `_FtsModeKeepsEmptyResult`, and `TestIndex_ReindexAsync{SelfHeals,Concurrent}` (the latter `-race`-clean).
- **The memory index freshness check now compares content hashes, not `mtime`+`size`.** `Index.Fresh` (run before every `search_memories` to decide FTS-vs-grep) compared each file's modification time and byte count against a stored anchor — so a same-byte-count edit that left the mtime untouched read as "fresh" and served stale FTS results. It now compares the full-content `sha256` the index already stores. This is *cheaper*, not more expensive: `List` already reads every memory's bytes for the frontmatter parse, so hashing is near-free over bytes already in hand, and the change **drops the per-file `os.Stat` syscall** `Fresh` previously made. Guarded by `TestIndex_FreshDetectsSameSizeSameMTimeEdit` (overwrites with an identical byte count under a pinned mtime and asserts staleness).
- **The memory index `Close()` no longer overlaps a concurrent reindex.** `Index.Close()` closed the `*sql.DB` without holding `ix.mu`, so the daemon's shutdown `CloseAll` could close the handle while a just-acquired index was mid background `Reindex` — a mid-transaction close (logged-and-swallowed, but untidy). `Close()` now takes `ix.mu` (which every `Upsert`/`Remove`/`Reindex` already holds during its db work), so the two never overlap; `ix.db` is deliberately left non-nil so a reindex that wins the mutex after a close fails cleanly with "database is closed" rather than nil-dereferencing. Guarded by `TestIndex_CloseRaceWithReindex` (`-race`).
- **Hint and episodic budgets are now enforced in bytes, not rune count.** `[memory] hint_budget_bytes` / `episodic_budget_bytes` are byte caps, but truncation clamped by *rune* count — so a CJK/emoji hint or summary could overrun the declared budget by up to ~4× (and the `…` suffix added bytes on top). Replaced `clampRunes` with `clampBytes`, which truncates to at most `budget` bytes *including* the ellipsis, cut on a UTF-8 rune boundary. Guarded by `TestClampBytes` (ASCII, CJK, emoji, sub-ellipsis budget; asserts `len ≤ budget` and valid UTF-8).
- **Generated memories now carry a `paths:` glob, the match-field label distinguishes provenance columns, and a dir named `..x` still hints.** Three smaller correctness gaps: (1) `WriteGenerated` emitted `source_paths` (the provenance trail) but no `paths:` line, so a machine-generated memory could never hint-match the files it was distilled from once Phase 2 wires the flow; it now also emits a deduped `paths:` glob from `SourcePaths`, round-tripping through `List`/`MatchesPath` like a hand-written memory. (2) `matchMemoryField` scanned `source_paths`/`source_symbols` then discarded them, mislabelling a provenance-column hit as the `"name"` default; it now labels them `source_paths`/`source_symbols` (checked after `path`, before `body`). (3) `hintRelPath` rejected any relative path starting `..`, so an in-workspace directory literally named `..config` was wrongly treated as a workspace escape; the check is now `rel == ".." || HasPrefix(rel, ".."+separator)`, so a genuine `../escape.go` is still refused but `..config/app.go` hints. Guarded by `TestWriteGenerated_{EmitsPathsGlob,NoPathsWhenNoSources,IndexedSourcePathsSearchable}`, `TestDedupeStrings`, `TestMatchMemoryField_SourcePathsLabel`, and the extended `TestHintRelPath`.
- **Hybrid memory v1 review pass: generated memories can no longer crowd user memories out of hint slots, retention ages legacy memories correctly, and a paths glob cannot forge frontmatter.** Three findings from the independent review of the hybrid-memory commit. (1) *Hint crowd-out:* generated `episodic-*` memories carry `paths:` globs and `List` returns memories in name order, so a few episodic memories attached to a hot file could occupy every capped hint slot (`max_hints`, default 3) and displace hand-written notes — search already preferred user-authored memories, hints did not. `Memory` now surfaces `Confidence` from frontmatter (`UserAuthored()`), and `matchingMemoryNames` lets user-authored memories claim slots first. (2) *Dead retention fallback:* `PruneGeneratedEpisodic` checked `CreatedAt.UnixNano() == 0` for the file-mtime fallback, but the zero time's `UnixNano` is a large *negative* number — so a generated memory missing `created_at` was sorted as infinitely old and pruned first; the check is now `IsZero()`. (3) *Frontmatter injection:* a `write_memory` `paths` glob (agent-supplied) containing a newline terminated its frontmatter line, letting a value smuggle in its own key (e.g. forge `confidence: generated`); `writeListLine` now newline-scrubs each value. Also: episodic write/prune failures are now `slog.Warn`'d instead of silently swallowed, and the test-only `buildEpisodic` wrapper was folded into `buildEpisodicDetail`. Guarded by `TestMatchingMemoryNames_UserAuthoredClaimSlotsFirst`, `TestList_PopulatesConfidence`, `TestPruneGeneratedEpisodic_{MissingCreatedAtFallsBackToMtime,ZeroKeepDisables}`, `TestWriteWithOptions_PathsNewlineCannotInjectFrontmatter`, `TestWriteGenerated_PathsNewlineCannotInjectFrontmatter`, `TestEpisodicRelPath`, and the provenance assertions added to `TestGenerateEpisodicSummary_Integration`.
- **Episodic summaries now count writes and touched files accurately, and always fire before eviction.** Four bugs in the rule-based episodic summariser: (1) `transaction_apply`'s file paths live nested in `operations[]`, so a transaction contributed **zero** touched files; `touchedPaths` now descends `operations[]`. (2) `find_replace` defaults to a dry run, but every `find_replace` call was counted as a write; it now counts as a write (and harvests paths) only when `apply == true`, else as a read. (3) The idle reaper gated `summariseIdle` on the **global** `[memory] generated_summaries`, so a project that enabled summaries under a global opt-out never got them; the gate is dropped — the per-session closure re-checks the snapshotted *project* config, so per-project enable **and** disable both work (the *threshold* stays global-resolved from `idle_summary_minutes` → `[session] idle_threshold_minutes`). (4) When `eviction_ttl_minutes` was shorter than the summary threshold, a session was cancelled before it ever summarised; `evictIdle` now summarises (once) before it cancels, under the same lock discipline as `summariseIdle`. The double-walk JSON parse in `buildEpisodic` is also collapsed to a single unmarshal per call. Guarded by `TestBuildEpisodic_TransactionAndFindReplace`, `TestEvictIdle_SummarisesBeforeCancel`, and `TestRunIdleReaper_SummarisesWhenGlobalSummariesOff`.

### Refactored

- **Identifier tokenisation is now one shared `internal/tokenise` leaf, not a copy-pasted pair.** The code-aware splitter (camelCase / PascalCase / snake / kebab / dotted / slashed → space-separated lowercase tokens) backing both FTS indexes was duplicated verbatim in `internal/topology` and `internal/memory`, guarded only by a parity comment. It now lives in a dependency-free `internal/tokenise.SplitIdentifier`, which both packages import (a leaf, so no layering cycle); the canonical table test moved there. Behaviour-identical — the topology/memory FTS tests still pass.
- **The episodic_memories table DDL is a single `episodicMemoriesDDL` const, shared by the baseline schema and the v7→v8 migration**, so a fresh database and a migrated one are byte-identical by construction (previously two hand-maintained copies that could silently drift). Guarded by `TestEpisodicSchemaParity` (PRAGMA `table_info` comparison of a fresh vs a migrated DB).
- **`Relevant` now delegates its per-memory glob test to `MatchesPath`** instead of re-implementing the inner loop, removing a duplicated matcher. Guarded by `TestRelevant_DelegatesToMatchesPath`. `matchGlob`'s basename-first semantics (a slashless glob like `*.go` matches by basename anywhere in the tree; a glob with a slash is path-anchored) are now documented as intended behaviour, not changed.

### Added

- **Hybrid memory v1 now makes generated session memory durable without adding an embedded LLM.** `write_memory` accepts optional `paths` globs and writes them into frontmatter so agent-authored memories can immediately drive `relevant_memories` and path hints. Idle episodic summaries still land in `stats.db` for the `session_start` "Last session" block, and now also write a conservative generated markdown memory when the session touched workspace files: `episodic-*` files are redacted, carry generated provenance (`source_session`, `source_paths`, `source_symbols`, `source_calls`), are indexed for `search_memories`, and are pruned by `[memory] generated_memory_keep` (default 50; `0` disables pruning). Plumb generates only activity summaries; architectural lessons remain agent-authored via `write_memory`. Guarded by `TestWriteMemory_PathsFrontmatterFeedsRelevantMemories`, `TestGenerateEpisodicSummary_Integration`, and `TestPruneGeneratedEpisodic_OnlyDeletesOldGeneratedEpisodic`.

- **The Memory TUI section closed its spec gaps: filter, dates, a frontmatter-free body view, and an enter toggle.** `f` opens an incremental filter over memory names/descriptions while the Memories pane has focus (typing narrows live, enter keeps the query applied, esc clears; header shows `Memories (n/N)` with the query). The detail panel now shows `Created` (from generated-memory `created_at:` frontmatter, hidden when absent) and `Updated` (file mtime) dates — `memory.Memory` carries both. The body view uses the new `memory.ReadBody` so the raw `---` frontmatter block is no longer repeated under the structured header rows, and enter toggles between the list and detail panes. Also fixes a latent cursor clamp that could go negative (and later panic) when a workspace's memory list emptied. Guarded by `TestMemoryFilter{NarrowsList,KeyLifecycle}`, `TestMemoryEnterTogglesListAndDetail`, `TestMemoryDetailShowsDatesAndStrippedBody`, `TestReadBody_StripsFrontmatter`, and `TestList_PopulatesDates`.

- **Redaction now covers Stripe, Google, Slack app-level, and OpenAI-style keys.** Before any generated memory or episodic summary is persisted, `redact.Redact` strips likely secrets — but the rule set missed several common provider shapes a captured tool argument could carry. Added: Stripe secret/restricted keys (`sk_live_…` / `rk_test_…` → `[REDACTED:stripe-key]`), Google API keys (`AIza`+35 → `[REDACTED:google-key]`), Slack app-level tokens (`xapp-…` → `[REDACTED:slack-token]`), and OpenAI-style keys (`sk-…` / `sk-proj-…` → `[REDACTED:api-key]`, with a 20-char lower bound so library names like `sk-learn` are left intact). Each rule is paired with a false-positive guard in the tests (`sk-learn`, a short `AIza…` identifier, and prose mentioning "stripe key"/"google api key" all stay untouched). Guarded by the extended `TestRedact_Secrets` and `TestRedact_FalsePositiveGuards`.
- **Closed memory-index test gaps around timestamp handling.** Added coverage for behaviours the review flagged as untested: `priorTimes` preserves `created_at`/`last_used_at` across a content re-upsert (a re-index is not a "new" memory); `TouchUsed` strictly advances `last_used_at` and is a no-op on a missing memory; and the search recency tiebreak orders two equal-rank, equal-confidence hits by `last_used_at DESC`. Guarded by `TestIndex_PriorTimesPreservedOnReupsert`, `TestIndex_TouchUsedBumpsLastUsed`, and `TestIndex_RecencyTiebreak`.

## 0.9.15 (unreleased)

The **multi-agent coexistence wave** — a concurrency-safety and reconnect-robustness pass distilled from the 0.9.10–0.9.12 review sessions. The single-agent loop was already solid; every fresh friction was about agents and humans coexisting in one repo. This release closes the write-path gaps that let a concurrent peer's or a human's edit be clobbered without warning (optimistic + automatic session-aware guards on both write tools, with a ReadTracker-refresh fix so a session's own edits aren't mis-flagged), points agents at `file_outline` both when a read is truncated *and* proactively when a large under-cap read would trip the client's token budget, makes a daemon restart both self-explaining (errors) and *proactively announced* (a one-shot reconnect note on the next tool result), and closes the 0.9.14 line-number-gutter decision with measured overhead and a cross-client round-trip test.

### Fixed

- **A successful write now refreshes the per-session `ReadTracker`, not just the `WriteTracker` — closing a false-positive in the new staleness guards.** Only `read_file`/`read_symbol` previously recorded into the `ReadTracker`; the write tools recorded into the `WriteTracker` alone. So after `read → edit → edit`, the second edit saw the on-disk mtime advanced past the *recorded read* (its own first edit bumped it) and (a) strict mode demanded a needless re-read, and (b) the just-added `changedSinceSessionRead` guard mis-fired — `edit_file` warned, and `write_file` *refused*, on the session's **own** consecutive writes. A new shared `WriteDeps.recordWritten` seam now records the post-write mtime into **both** trackers on every successful content write (edit/write/find_replace/rename/copy/transaction), so a write counts as authoritative current-state knowledge: own consecutive writes are never flagged, while a genuine external change between two writes still warns/refuses. Guarded by `TestEditFile_StrictMode_ChainedEditsNoReread`, `TestEditFile_OwnConsecutiveEdits_NoStaleWarning`, `TestEditFile_ExternalChange_StillWarns`, and `TestWriteFile_RefreshesReadTracker_NoOverwriteRefusal`.

### Changed

- **The "no workspace / no repository resolved" errors now name the likely cause and the fix.** When a daemon restarts (after a rebuild or upgrade) it clears every connection's in-memory workspace pin, so a previously-working session's next path-bearing or `git` call fails — and the old error gave no hint why (observed live: a `git commit` failing with a bare "no repository resolved" mid-session after a restart). Both `git`'s no-repo error and the shared `noWorkspaceError` now explain that a daemon restart clears the pin and that `session_start` re-attaches, turning a silent state-loss into a self-explaining one. (The proactive complement — a one-shot note on the first tool result after a reconnect — ships as a separate change below; the earlier reservation about it was framed daemon-side, but the *proxy* unambiguously knows when it reconnected, so there is no brand-new-client false-fire.) Guarded by `TestNoWorkspaceError_SelfExplaining` and an extended `TestGit_RefusesWhenNoRepoResolved`.

### Added

- **`plumb serve` now tells the agent when it transparently reconnected to the daemon.** The resilient proxy already survives a daemon crash/restart by re-dialling and replaying the handshake — but the agent was never told, so a mid-session behaviour change (the 2026-06-10 case: read output silently grew a line-number gutter after a rebuild+restart) read as spooky and the cause had to be *inferred*. The proxy now appends a one-shot `# plumb-note: plumb daemon reconnected (now <version>) — your session state … may have changed` as an extra **text content item** on the first content-bearing tool result after a reconnect. It is set only inside `reconnect()` (which fires solely on an *established* connection's failure, never the initial connect — so it cannot false-fire for a brand-new client, the proxy-side advantage the daemon lacks), armed before the new connection is published, and consumed only when injection actually succeeds (so it lands on a real tool result, not a ping/initialize/error frame). `injectReconnectNote` is fully fail-safe and **additive** — it only appends a content item, never edits existing text, and returns any non-`result.content` frame unchanged — so it can never corrupt a tool result; no request-id correlation is used (a fast response can resolve before its request is tracked). Behind the existing `PLUMB_PROXY_RECONNECT` machinery. Guarded by `TestProxyReconnectNote` (one-shot end-to-end through a reconnect) and `TestInjectReconnectNote` (append + four fail-safe shapes).
- **`write_file` now accepts `expected_mtime` / `expected_sha`** (from a prior `read_file` header), the same optimistic-concurrency guard `edit_file` already had. When provided, the write is refused if the file changed since you read it — so a full-content overwrite can no longer silently clobber a concurrent change. Previously `write_file` had **no** way to guard a whole-file replacement, the most destructive write, against an under-the-feet change. Guarded by `TestWriteFile_ExpectedMtimeGuard` and `TestWriteFile_ExpectedShaGuard`.
- **A truncated `read_file` now points at `file_outline`.** When a read is capped at 200 KiB, the truncation note previously offered only `start_line`/`end_line`; an agent capped on a large structured file (e.g. a 105 KiB Markdown doc) would reinvent a section map with a header regex instead of calling `file_outline`, which indexes Markdown sections and code symbols directly. The note now suggests `file_outline` as the one-call structural alternative. Guarded by `TestReadFile_TruncationSuggestsOutline`.
- **A *large but under-cap* whole-file `read_file` now proactively nudges toward `file_outline`.** The truncation note above only fires at plumb's 200 KiB cap — but the real friction (2026-06-10: a 105 KB `todo.md` read) is a file well under that cap whose size trips the *client's own* token budget (which plumb cannot see), spilling the output to a side file with no plumb-side signal. read_file now prepends a one-line `# plumb-note: large file (N KiB) — file_outline returns its structure in ~200 tokens …` when an **unranged, non-truncated** read returns a body over 32 KiB **and** the path has a structural engine (so there is structure worth outlining). Suppressed for ranged reads (already slicing), truncated reads (the truncation note already names it), small files, and structureless paths. The structural gate is injected from the daemon via `langsupport.ByPath` (`hasStructuralEngine`), matching the existing `WithOutsideLabel` pattern — `internal/tools` does not import `langsupport`. Guarded by `TestReadFile_LargeReadNudge` and `TestReadFile_LargeReadNudge_Suppressed` (4 negatives).
- **Automatic session-aware staleness protection on the write tools** (no caller ceremony). When this session has *read* a file and it then changes on disk before a write — a peer agent or a human editing under you, the exact failure that near-lost a doc section during the review session — the write tools now react even without an explicit `expected_mtime`: `write_file` **refuses** (`overwrite_changed: true` overrides), since a whole-file overwrite would discard the change wholesale; `edit_file` **warns** (`# plumb-warn: this file changed on disk since your session last read it …`) but still applies, since its `old_string` anchor already protects the edited region while the surrounding file may have moved. A brand-new or never-read file is never flagged, so blind creation stays frictionless. Shared detector `changedSinceSessionRead` over the per-connection `ReadTracker`. Guarded by `TestWriteFile_RefusesStaleOverwrite`, `TestWriteFile_NewFileNeverFlagged`, `TestEditFile_StaleReadWarning`, `TestEditFile_NoStaleWarningWhenUnchanged`.

### Verification

- **The 0.9.14 line-number-gutter decision is now closed with evidence, not estimate.** (a) **Token overhead measured** (`TestGutterOverhead`): over this package's own 81 Go sources the gutter adds **+11.5%** bytes (typical code +11.4%, prose/markdown +7.0%, pathological short-line worst case +71.4%) — confirming the back-of-envelope "~1 token/line" and well within the universal-keep decision, since Claude clients already pay that via native `cat -n`. (b) **Cross-client round-trip** (`TestClientsAuth_GutterRoundTrip`, `clients_e2e`): a new auth-tier scenario drives a real client to `read_file` a guttered file then `edit_file` one line, asserting on the **on-disk result** — the edit applied and **no `<n>\t` gutter prefix leaked** — which validates the forgiveness path through any client (catches both "client stripped it" and "plumb's forgiveness caught it"); nondeterministic like the rest of the auth tier (a no-op edit is reported inconclusive, not failed). (c) **`find_replace` forgiveness: decided against.** Its patterns originate from search output (un-guttered) or user intent, not `read_file` output, and it is regex-capable, so a literal `\d+\t` in a pattern can be intentional — auto-stripping it there would be a semantic hazard with no observed need. Revisit only if dogfooding shows guttered pastes reaching `find_replace`.

## 0.9.14 (unreleased)

Resolution of the line-number-gutter efficiency concern (raised against 0.9.12): keep the gutter universal, and close its one real failure mode — a client pasting the rendered `<n>\t` prefix into `old_string` — with server-side forgiveness in `edit_file`, mirroring the existing CRLF tolerance. A mis-pasted gutter now costs zero extra round-trips instead of a failed-edit retry.

### Changed

- **Gutter forgiveness in `edit_file` — a guttered `old_string` self-heals instead of failing.** Decision record for the "will the gutter slow agents down?" concern: the gutter is kept **universal** (it removes range-edit re-reads for every client, and Claude clients already pay the `cat -n` token cost natively), and the one real risk — a client pasting the rendered `<n>\t` prefix into `old_string`, burning a failed-edit round-trip — is closed server-side, mirroring the existing CRLF tolerance. The literal match always runs first; only on a miss does `resolveStrMatch` retry with the gutter stripped, and only when the shape is unambiguous (every line prefixed `spaces+digits+tab` AND the numbers consecutive — the shape of a verbatim copy from guttered read output) and the stripped form resolves cleanly (exactly once, or ≥1 under `replace_all`). A guttered `new_string` is stripped alongside, so a verbatim paste can never inject gutter text into the file. Single guttered lines are **never** auto-stripped (a lone `digits+tab` prefix is plausible real content, e.g. a TSV row) — they get an explicit hint appended to the not-found error instead. When forgiveness fires, the response carries a teaching note ("omit the `<n>\t` prefix in future edits"). Wired into both all-or-nothing (`tryEdit`, via the extracted `applyStrEdit`) and `apply_partial` modes. Net effect: the gutter's failure mode costs zero extra round-trips on any client, while genuine tab-separated content is untouched (literal-first + sequence check). Guarded by `TestStripLineGutter`, `TestEditFile_GutterForgiveness_{MultiLine,NewStringAlsoStripped,PartialMode,AmbiguousStrippedFormNotApplied}`, `TestEditFile_SingleLineGutter_HintNotAutoFix`, and `TestEditFile_LiteralTabDigitContentUnaffected`.

## 0.9.13 (unreleased)

On-demand integration harness for the MCP client CLIs (`cmd/clientsmoke`): drive each supported client non-interactively and confirm it actually works *through* plumb, so the `plumb setup <client>` targets are verified rather than hand-checked. Two tiers — a keyless connection check and an opt-in LLM auth check — both asserting on plumb's own session/stats records rather than each CLI's output format.

### Added

- **On-demand MCP client test harness (`cmd/clientsmoke`).** A two-tier integration harness that drives the supported client CLIs non-interactively, so we no longer hand-verify each `plumb setup <client>` target. The **connection tier** (`make clients-test`, `//go:build clients`) runs each client's auth-free connecting probe (e.g. `gemini mcp list`, `hermes mcp test plumb`) and asserts plumb wrote a session file naming the client — proof the CLI completed the MCP `initialize` handshake, deterministic and keyless, asserted on plumb's own signal rather than each CLI's output. The **auth tier** (`make clients-test-auth`, `//go:build clients_e2e`) drives a headless prompt that forces a plumb tool call and asserts a `tool_calls` row landed in the stats DB — running only the clients whose API key is exported (`OPENAI_API_KEY` for most; `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`/`GEMINI_API_KEY`/`CURSOR_API_KEY` for claude/gemini/cursor) and skipping the rest. Each subtest runs in an isolated HOME + XDG tree (like `cmd/smoke`), and an uninstalled client is skipped. Connection-tier coverage (all verified live): gemini, qwen, opencode, hermes, claude-code; cursor-agent (caches MCP tool lists — never reconnects headless) and codex/crush/goose/auggie (no auth-free probe) are connection-tier skips, still auth-tier drivable. `scripts/install-clients.sh` installs the CLIs (idempotent, never keys; hermes needs its `[mcp]` extra); `make build-clients` compiles both tags and is folded into `make verify` so the harness can't bitrot.

## 0.9.12 (unreleased)

Agent-ergonomics fixes from the 2026-06-09 dogfooding sweep: a line-number gutter on file reads so range edits stop drifting by one, and a stale-diagnostics short-circuit so a not-yet-re-analysed snapshot never reads as fresh breakage. Closes items #1 (primary fix) and #2 of the *Agent-ergonomics fixes from dogfooding* entry.

### Changed

- **`read_file`/`read_symbol` now prefix each content line with a 1-based file line-number gutter (`<n>\t`, `cat -n` style).** The output header lines look like content but aren't counted, so hand-computing `start_line`/`end_line` for a range `edit_file` drifted by one or two (2–3 confirmation reads per big-section delete). The gutter is right-aligned, tab-separated, and keyed to the real file position for sliced reads (a read starting at line 100 shows `100\t…`), making range math exact and the metadata header obviously-not-content. It is **display-only** — `str_replace`/`old_string` matching is unaffected (it matches the caller-supplied file content), and the tool descriptions tell agents to strip the leading `<n>\t` before reusing a line as an `edit_file`/`find_replace` `old_string` (the `cat -n` convention Claude Code's native Read already uses). The `lines=`/`chars=`/`indent=` header counts and the 200 KiB truncation still operate on the raw content (computed before the gutter is applied); a trailing newline adds no phantom numbered line; the `(no lines in range …)` placeholder is never guttered. Shared helper `withLineGutter`; `readContentMaybeRanged`/`readLineRange` now also report whether the returned string is real content vs a placeholder. Guarded by `TestReadFile_LineNumberGutter`, `TestReadFile_GutterRangeStartsAtFileLine`, and `TestWithLineGutter`.
- **A stale post-write diagnostics snapshot no longer renders its pre-edit findings.** `formatPostWriteDiagnostics` already knew `fresh=false` means "the LSP had not re-published within the wait window, so this whole snapshot predates the write", but it still rendered the (pre-edit) error/warn groups with a hedge note appended — which read as "I just broke the build" for one beat (e.g. a stale `"io"/"os" imported and not used` right after the imports were fixed). It now short-circuits to a single `diagnostics: pending — LSP not yet re-analysed; call diagnostics() to confirm` line. The fresh path (including the past-EOF `stale?` split) is unchanged; an empty not-fresh snapshot stays silent. Guarded by `TestFormatPostWriteDiagnostics_StaleSnapshotIsPending`.

## 0.9.11 (unreleased)

Java (jdtls) production hardening — transition the daemon from a "static supervisor" to a "dynamic resource manager" for heavyweight language servers, plus multi-OS polish. jdtls reaches ~0.8–1.5 GB RSS with 15–40 s cold starts; the pool previously only reclaimed a server when its last session detached, so an idle-but-connected session kept its JVM resident forever. Closes both jdtls items.

### Added

- **Idle hibernation of heavyweight language servers.** A pool janitor goroutine stops a server's process after `[lsp.<lang>] idle_timeout` without a tool call (default `20m` for java, off for everything else), keeping the `poolEntry` and its warm cache mapped; the next tool call restarts it transparently (`wakeLocked` reuses the `Supervisor` and rebuilds the file watcher). Activity is tracked lock-free by `clientProxy.lastUsed` (an atomic the routing path already holds — no per-call pool-mutex lookup), touched at the routing read sites (`routingProxy.route`/`primaryClient`), not in `clientProxy.get()` which also fires for teardown/probes. The proxy is cleared under `p.mu` before the out-of-lock teardown so a concurrent call sees the server as not-ready and restarts it rather than dialing a dying connection; a wake is pinned only after it succeeds, so a failed restart can't leak a reference. Guarded by `TestClientProxy_TouchUpdatesLastUsed`, `TestPool_HibernateIdle_*`, `TestPool_HibernateAndWakeRestartsServer`, and the gated `TestIntegration_PoolHibernateWake` (real-gopls hibernate→wake).
- **LRU workspace eviction.** `[lsp.<lang>] max_workspaces` (default `2` for java, unlimited otherwise) caps concurrently-running servers of a language; starting one beyond the cap hibernates the least-recently-used running entry first (`overBudgetVictimLocked`). Guarded by `TestPool_OverBudgetVictim`.
- **`plumb debug lsp` + doctor live-server view.** A new `lsp-status` control-socket command lists every pooled server with its lifecycle state, child PID, resident memory, and idle time; `plumb debug lsp` renders it as a table and `plumb doctor` appends a `(live)` row per server. `monitor.ProcessRSS(pid)` samples an arbitrary child process's RSS (macOS via `ps -o rss=`, Linux via `/proc/<pid>/statm`), distinct from the daemon-only `Sampler`; `Supervisor.PID()` exposes the child PID. The four optional control-socket callbacks are collapsed into a `ctrlHandlers` struct. Guarded by `TestRenderLSPStatus`, `TestHandleCtrlConn_LSPStatus*`.
- **`jdtls-data` cache pruning.** The janitor removes Eclipse-workspace storage (~50 MB/project) for projects untouched for 30+ days and not backing a pooled workspace — once at startup and daily thereafter; a live entry's dir is always kept, including while hibernated. Guarded by `TestPool_PruneJdtlsCache`.
- **`[lsp.<language>] idle_timeout` and `max_workspaces` config fields.** Per-language, project-overridable, read at pool construction (restart-needed); surfaced in `plumb config show` and the configuration docs. Guarded by the config defaults tests.

### Docs

- **jdtls binary-naming + resource-budget guidance.** `docs/adding-an-lsp.md` and `docs/configuration.md` document the `command` override for non-Homebrew launchers (`jdtls.sh`/`jdtls.bat`/absolute path) and the hibernation / `max_workspaces` / cache-pruning behaviour.
- **doctor JDK-distro version coverage + CI-tunable cold-start budgets.** `parseJavaMajorVersion` tests now assert the line-1 `java --version` strings of Eclipse Temurin, Amazon Corretto, and Microsoft Build of OpenJDK. The jdtls integration test's ServiceReady/diagnostics deadlines are overridable via `PLUMB_TEST_JDTLS_READY_TIMEOUT` / `PLUMB_TEST_JDTLS_DIAG_TIMEOUT` for slow/cold CI runners, with the warm-cache vs `JDTLS_FRESH_DATA` trade-off documented.

## 0.9.10 (unreleased)

Advanced Memory Engine, Phase 1 — turn the per-workspace memory store from grep-over-markdown into an FTS5-indexed, provenance-aware, self-summarising knowledge layer. Markdown files stay the source of truth; a separate, rebuildable `memory.db` is the derived index (distinct from `topology.db`). Shipped wave by wave.

### Added

- **Proactive memory hints injected into tool responses.** When an agent calls a path-bearing tool (`read_file`, `edit_file`, `write_file`, `read_symbol`, `file_outline`) on a path that matches a memory's `paths:` glob, plumb appends a compact `[Hint: relevant memory 'X' — call read_memory to view.]` block — names only, never bodies. This needed a new seam: `OnAfterTool` is fire-and-forget and cannot enrich, so `mcp.Server` gained an `EnrichToolOutput` hook called on the success path next to the alias-notice. The lookup is cheap (a per-connection `memoryHintCache` over memory frontmatter, refreshed on the memories-dir mtime or a 10 s TTL, never reading bodies on the hot `read_file` path) and bounded by `[memory] max_hints`/`hint_budget_bytes`. Gated on `[memory] inject_hints` (default on). Guarded by `TestServer_EnrichToolOutput`, `TestHintRelPath`, `TestMemoryHintCache_Match`, `TestMatchingMemoryNames_RespectsMax`, and `TestHintBlock`.
- **`internal/redact` — secret scrubber for generated memories.** A dependency-free leaf package (`Redact`/`ContainsSecret`) that strips API keys, tokens (GitHub/Slack/JWT/AWS), PEM private keys, URL-embedded credentials, and `key = value` secret assignments before any generated or episodic memory is persisted, replacing each with a labelled `[REDACTED:<kind>]` placeholder. Conservative-biased to catch secrets while leaving benign prose intact — a summary that merely mentions “token” or a file path like `internal/auth/login.go` is untouched. Table-tested with false-positive guards (`internal/redact/redact_test.go`).
- **`memory.db` FTS5 index over the markdown memory store.** A new per-workspace SQLite/FTS5 index (`internal/memory/index.go`, `index_persist.go`, `index_query.go`) at `<workspace>/.plumb/memory.db`, separate from `topology.db` (durable knowledge vs rebuildable code index). The markdown files stay the source of truth; the index is rebuildable. `Index.Upsert`/`Remove`/`TouchUsed` keep it current; `Reindex` walks the files and repairs drift; `Fresh` (mtime+size anchor, no body reads) gates whether a search can trust the index. `Search` ranks by BM25 with code-aware tokenisation (CamelCase/snake/kebab — `splitIdentifier`, copied from topology to avoid a sibling import), a small bonus for user-authored over generated memories, and a recency tiebreak; it carries `Field`/`Confidence`/snippet metadata. Provenance/lifecycle columns (confidence, source session/paths/symbols, created/updated/last-used, supersedes, stale-after) are in place for later waves. Not yet wired into the tools (next wave). Guarded by `internal/memory/index_test.go` (tokenisation, ranking tie-break, freshness drift/repair, remove). Single-writer discipline: `SetMaxOpenConns(1)` + a per-index mutex; `memory.db` sidecars auto-gitignored.
- **`search_memories` now uses the FTS5 index, with a deterministic grep fallback.** When the per-workspace memory index is available and fresh, `search_memories` returns ranked hits (BM25 + user-authored bonus, annotated `source=memory-fts`, with field/confidence/snippet metadata); otherwise it falls back to the existing grep over the markdown files. A new `mode` arg (`auto`|`fts`|`grep`) overrides the choice; `use_regex` always takes the grep path. `write_memory`/`delete_memory` keep the index current (`memory.WriteIndexed`/`DeleteIndexed`, best-effort — a file write never fails on an index error). The index is owned by a daemon-held `memoryIndexPool` (one handle per workspace, opened lazily with a one-shot background reindex, closed at shutdown) and exposed per-connection via `memoryIndexLive`, gated on `[memory] enabled`. Guarded by `TestSearchMemories_FTSAndGrepFallback` and `TestSearchMemories_NilIndexUsesGrep`.
- **Rule-based episodic summaries (no LLM) surfaced in `session_start`.** When a session goes idle, the daemon's reaper generates a short, deterministic summary of what it did — files modified, read/write tool counts, symbols looked at — from the session's own `tool_calls` rows, passes it through `redact.Redact`, bounds it to `[memory] episodic_budget_bytes`, and persists it to a new `episodic_memories` table (stats schema **v7→v8**; writes funnel through the single stats `Writer` goroutine, reads via the cached read-only handle, always partitioned by workspace). The next `session_start` for that workspace appends a `## Last session` block. Gated on `[memory] generated_summaries` (default on); idle threshold is `[memory] idle_summary_minutes` or falls back to `[session] idle_threshold_minutes`; summarised at most once per idle spell. Guarded by `TestBuildEpisodic*`, `TestEpisodic_RecordAndLatest`, and `TestToolCallsForSession_Partitioned`. (Readers on a pre-v8 stats DB report upgrade-required until the daemon opens it read-write once — pre-existing migration behaviour.)
- **Generated-memory provenance + `read_memory` footer.** `memory.WriteGenerated` writes a machine-generated memory with a provenance frontmatter block (`confidence`, `source_session`, `source_paths`/`symbols`/`calls`, `created_at`, `stale_after`) after passing the body through `redact.Redact` — a secret captured in a tool argument can never reach durable storage. Provenance is mirrored into the index for ranking and parsed back by `ReadMeta`. `read_memory` appends a compact `[provenance] generated — session X · touched a.go · DATE` footer for non-user memories (user memories are unchanged) and bumps the memory's last-used time. Guarded by `TestReadMemory_ProvenanceFooterAndRedaction` and `TestReadMemory_UserMemoryHasNoFooter`.
- **`[memory]` configuration section.** A new project-overridable config block (`internal/config`): `enabled` (FTS index; default on), `generated_summaries` (episodic; default on), `inject_hints` (memory hints in tool responses; default on), `hint_budget_bytes` (512), `episodic_budget_bytes` (1024), `max_hints` (3), `idle_summary_minutes` (0 → falls back to `[session] idle_threshold_minutes`). Surfaced with provenance in `plumb config show`. Guarded by `TestDefaults_Memory`.

## 0.9.9 (unreleased)

Closes out the low-priority *Architecture* residuals: the name-keyed topology traversal imprecision, and the tree-sitter Phase 7 (offline semantic search) decision.

### Changed

- **`topology_explore`/`topology_impact` no longer follow the wrong same-named symbol — disambiguated traversal start.** Both tools resolved their start node by name with a bare `LIMIT 1` (`resolveNode`, `internal/topology/explore.go`), so when two symbols across different files shared a name the BFS could anchor on an arbitrary one and report *its* neighbours — a silent mis-attribution (edge traversal itself was already ID-correct; only the start was ambiguous). Resolution now goes through `ResolveNodes`, which returns every same-name node ordered deterministically (path, then start line) and accepts an optional `NodeHint{PathSubstr, Kind}`; the tools expose two new optional args, **`path`** (case-insensitive file-path substring) and **`kind`** (node kind), to pin the intended symbol. A hint that matches nothing is ignored, so a stale hint never turns a real symbol into a miss. When a name still resolves to several nodes the output appends a one-line `[note: "X" matched N symbols …]` listing the alternatives so the agent can re-query precisely. New package seams `ExploreFrom`/`ImpactFrom` (and the `Store` wrappers) start a traversal from an already-resolved node. Guarded by `TestResolveNodes_*`, `TestExploreFrom_StartsAtChosenNode`, `TestImpactFrom_StartsAtChosenNode`, and `TestTopologyAmbiguityNote`.

### Docs

- **Tree-sitter Phase 7 (offline semantic search) closed — decision: no bundled/offline embedder.** The spike proved a *small local* model loses to FTS5 while only a *strong hosted* model wins; the opt-in hosted / bring-your-own-endpoint re-rank that conclusion implies already shipped in 0.8.47 (`[semantics]` + `topology_search` `mode=fts+semantic`). The Phase 7 *DEFERRED* block and the standalone "Hybrid semantic search" follow-up are closed out; rationale captured internally. Revisit only if a stable, strong, pure-Go local embedder appears.
- **Experimental LSP adapter promotion (zls / typescript / kotlin) attempted, not completed.** Install was authorised, but Homebrew cannot run on this pre-release macOS (`unknown or unsupported macOS version: :dunno`), blocking zls + kotlin-language-server; typescript-language-server 5.3.0 installed via npm passes `TestIntegration_DocumentSymbols` but fails `TestIntegration_DidChangeWatchedFiles` (no diagnostics within deadline). None promoted; all stay *experimental*. Findings + finish steps in `todo-to-review.md`.

## 0.9.8 (unreleased)

Completes the 0.9.7 daemon-memory work: bound the *transient* parse peak that the lazy-grammar + arena-recycling changes left untouched — the actual cause of the daemon's resident footprint.

### Added

- **`plumb debug stacks` — non-destructive goroutine dump over the control socket.** A third `plumb debug` command (alongside `mem`/`heap`): it asks the running daemon to write a full goroutine stack dump — the pprof `goroutine` profile at `debug=2`, i.e. human-readable stacks for *every* goroutine, the `SIGQUIT` equivalent without killing the process — to `plumb.stacks.<ns>.txt` in the cache dir, and prints the path. Built to capture a **live hang**: when a call wedges, the dump shows exactly what each goroutine is blocked on (a held mutex, a stalled `conn.Write`, a lock wait) instead of leaving it to inference. Wired as the `goroutine-stacks` control command (`handleStacksProfile` in `log_level.go`); guarded by `TestHandleCtrlConn_GoroutineStacks`.

### Changed

- **Per-parse memory budget bounds the transient peak — daemon RSS 1.9 GB → ~460 MB.** 0.9.7's lazy-grammar + arena-recycling work cut the steady-state *baseline* but left the cold-start/resync *transient* unbounded — and that transient was the real symptom: a live daemon sat at **1.9 GB RSS** (`HeapSys` high-water 1.9 GB) while its live heap was only ~46 MB. An allocation profile traced 83 % of all bytes to gotreesitter parse arenas under `extractPath`. Root cause: indexing is strictly serial, so a 1.9 GB *live* high-water can only come from a **single pathological parse** — the GLR-heavy Markdown grammar (~200 nodes/byte) blows one parse of a few-hundred-KB file to hundreds of MB to >1 GB (measured: a 300 KB Markdown document → ~1.4 GB of live arena for one parse; the repo's own 353 KB `CHANGELOG.md` → ~715 MB). gotreesitter has a per-parse memory budget (applied to the node arena *and* the GLR scratch independently, doubled again by the recovery parser) but plumb left it at its 512 MB default — too high given the ~4× application. The daemon now sets `GOT_PARSE_MEMORY_BUDGET_MB=128` at startup (before the first parse; honours an operator-set value) and tightens the soft-heap default from 4 GiB to 1 GiB so the GC reclaims each parse's transient before the next, instead of letting consecutive transients stack into the high-water. `debug.FreeOSMemory` (already present) hands the freed pages back. Measured end-to-end after a real restart + full resync of this repo: RSS **1905 MB → 465 MB**, `HeapSys` **1.9 GB → 459 MB** (4.1×). Regression-guarded by `TestParseMemoryBudgetBoundsLargeMarkdown` (a large-Markdown parse must stay materially below its unbudgeted footprint) and `TestApplyParseMemoryBudget`. Note: on macOS the prior 1.9 GB was `MADV_FREE` memory (reclaimed under pressure, not a leak), but the *peak* was real indexing pressure and is what this bounds.
- **Defence-in-depth on the indexing peak: per-grammar parse cap + watch-path reclaim.** Two hardening layers on top of the per-parse budget. (1) A *per-grammar* source-size cap (`langsupport.MaxParseBytes`, 256 KiB) on the GLR-heavy markup grammars — Markdown, HTML, YAML — where one few-hundred-KB file drives a pathological parse for little outline value (Markdown and HTML already prefer the structural Map over their noisy LSP outline; YAML has no LSP at all). A file above the cap is indexed with **zero symbols** rather than parsed; the global `[topology].max_file_size_bytes` (512 KiB) stays the outer bound. (2) `runQueueCycle` now drains the gotreesitter arena pool and calls `debug.FreeOSMemory` after a *coalesced burst* (≥ 64 files, e.g. a `git checkout` or formatter) — previously only the full resync reclaimed, leaving a watch-triggered mass change's transient pinned; a single small edit is deliberately exempt so it never pays a stop-the-world GC. The resync path now also drains the pool before its existing `FreeOSMemory`. Guarded by `TestIndexer_OversizedGrammarSkippedButRecorded`, `TestMarkdownRegistryHasParseCap`, and `TestShouldReclaimAfterBurst`. Operators wanting to bound the GLR scratch further can `export GOT_GLR_MAX_STACKS` — plumb does not override it.

### Fixed

- **A stuck response write can no longer wedge a whole connection — bounded per-connection write deadline.** This closes the open follow-up from the stats-DB and `plumb debug stacks` work below. Mid-session a connection could stop answering: every tool call (including `daemon_info`) hung to the client's request timeout (~4 min for Claude Desktop), cleared only by a daemon restart. Every response on a connection serialises through one per-connection write mutex (`serveState.wrMu`, `internal/mcp/server.go`), and the daemon handed the raw socket to `Serve` with **no write deadline** — so `enc.Encode → conn.Write` could block forever if the `plumb serve` proxy (or the client behind it) stopped draining, and while blocked it held `wrMu`, hanging every later reply (`daemon_info`'s work completes; only its reply can't flush). That `daemon_info` *also* hung is the tell: a stall *inside* `Execute` (a path lock or LSP round-trip) would not hold `wrMu`, so reads would still answer — only a write stuck under `wrMu` explains the total wedge. `serveState` now sets a `SetWriteDeadline` (default **30 s**, `PLUMB_WRITE_TIMEOUT`; `0`/`off` disables) around each `Encode` when the transport supports it (a `net.Conn` does; test pipes don't, and are unaffected). A lapsed deadline fails the write, marks the connection broken, and cancels `Serve` so the connection is torn down with a clear error — the resilient proxy then reconnects and replays the handshake — instead of hanging indefinitely. 30 s is far longer than any healthy local write yet well under the client timeout. Guarded by `TestServer_WriteDeadline_SetThenClearedOnSuccess`, `TestServer_WriteDeadline_TearsDownOnStuckWrite`, and `TestServer_WriteDeadline_NoDeadlineWriterUnaffected`. (Remaining as a smaller follow-up: a lock-free `ping`/`daemon_info` liveness probe so a contended connection is observable *before* the deadline lapses; and the separate hypothesis (b) — a stall *inside* `Execute` — if a future `plumb debug stacks` dump ever shows it.)
- **Stats DB stops flooding the log with `SQLITE_BUSY` and silently dropping rows — batched single-writer.** Under concurrent sessions the global `stats.db` writer hit `database is locked (5)` constantly: every tool call was its own autocommit `INSERT` (one `fsync` + one write-lock acquisition), and `statsStore` spawned a goroutine *per call*, so bursts of writers contended for the single connection and the loser dropped the row after the 5 s busy-timeout. `Open()` also re-stamped `PRAGMA user_version` on **every** open, turning a read-only open into a lock-contending write. Writes now funnel through one `stats.Writer` goroutine that batches inserts into a single transaction (flush at 256 rows or 200 ms) — collapsing hundreds of `fsync`s and lock acquisitions into one — with `synchronous=NORMAL` (corruption-safe under WAL), a periodic `wal_checkpoint(TRUNCATE)` to bound WAL growth, and a non-blocking enqueue that drops-and-counts only on a genuinely full buffer (logged, never silent). `Open()` stamps `user_version` only when it actually changed. Reads stay file-based — WAL readers never block the writer — so `plumb stats` and the TUI keep working with the daemon stopped; the per-call `OpenReadOnly` churn in `daemon_info`/`session_start`/`workspace_sessions` is replaced by a process-cached `stats.SharedReadOnly` handle. `Close` drains and flushes in-flight rows, so a clean shutdown loses nothing. Guarded by `TestWriter_DrainsOnClose`, `TestWriter_DropsOnOverflow`, `TestWriter_RenameAppliesAfterInsert`, and `TestRecordBatch_SkipsInvalid`.

- **OS base directories now resolved via `github.com/adrg/xdg` (new dependency) — no hand-rolled per-OS paths.** plumb's config/data/state/cache locations were hand-rolled across three files (`daemon_paths.go`, `config_load.go`, `session.go`) with inconsistent rules: on macOS config landed in `~/.config` (Linux-style), data in `~/Library/Application Support`, sessions in `~/.local/share`, and the daemon log in `~/Library/Logs` — four different conventions, and the log path had already drifted (a stale `daemon.log` lingered in the cache dir from a prior move). A new `internal/paths` package delegates every plumb-owned directory to the de-facto cross-platform base-directory library, so no OS path literals remain and Windows is handled correctly. On macOS config/data/state now consolidate under `~/Library/Application Support/plumb` and cache under `~/Library/Caches`; the daemon **log** is the one exception — it uses the macOS-native `~/Library/Logs/plumb/daemon.log` (Console.app's location), resolved by `paths.LogDir`, since no base-directory spec models a logs dir. Linux is unchanged. An existing `~/.config/plumb/config.toml` is still read as a fallback so an upgrade is never silently reset.

### Docs

- **`git` `repo` schema corrected.** The `repo` argument description still claimed an omitted repo uses the current working directory; since the 0.9.7 fail-closed fix that is false — an omitted repo uses the connection's pinned workspace, or the call is refused. Description updated to match.

## 0.9.7 (unreleased)

Daemon memory: bound it, explain it, and cut the steady-state baseline. A live heap profile attributed ~307 MB of resident heap to eagerly-decoded tree-sitter grammars (now decoded lazily — gone for languages a workspace doesn't use) and most cold-start allocation churn to never-released parse arenas (now recycled — which *reduces*, but does not eliminate, the transient, since per-parse node allocation is inherent to indexing every file). The daemon can now also profile itself, and a soft ceiling bounds any spike.

### Added

- **Daemon memory introspection + soft ceiling.** The daemon now bounds and explains its own memory. A soft heap limit (`debug.SetMemoryLimit`) is applied at startup — `PLUMB_MEMORY_LIMIT` (e.g. `1500MiB`, or `0`/`off` to disable) with a generous 4 GiB anti-OOM backstop default — so a transient spike can't exhaust the machine. Two new control-socket commands, surfaced as `plumb debug mem` (live `HeapAlloc`/`HeapInuse`/`HeapSys`/`HeapReleased`/`NumGC`/`Goroutines`) and `plumb debug heap` (writes a `runtime/pprof` heap profile to the cache dir for `go tool pprof`), make a spike attributable instead of guessed. A full topology resync now calls `debug.FreeOSMemory()` on completion, handing the large transient working set back to the OS so RSS/`HeapSys` settle to steady state instead of lingering at the walk's peak.

### Security

- **`git` tool now fails closed when `repo` is omitted — closes a cross-session workspace leak.** A `git` call with no `repo` argument could fall through to the daemon's spawn working directory (`os.Getwd()`) when the connection's workspace was transiently unresolved, executing git against an *unrelated* project — observed in the wild resolving a plumb-pinned connection's `git` to a different repo. Because the daemon is a singleton shared across connections, read-tier git (`log`/`diff`/`show`/`blame`) could disclose another project's source and history, and write/destructive tiers could mutate the wrong repo (potentially cross-tenant). The hole was twofold: `Git.checkBoundary` *skipped* the per-connection `PathPolicy` check entirely when the resolved repo was empty, and `findGitRoot("")` fell back to `os.Getwd()`. Both now fail closed: an empty resolved repo is a hard error (`git: no repository resolved — pass an explicit "repo" or attach a workspace with session_start`), and `findGitRoot` refuses an empty path rather than using the daemon cwd. A `git` call can now only ever target an explicit `repo` or this connection's pinned, boundary-checked workspace. The underlying per-connection dep wiring was already correct (both `WorkspaceFn` and the boundary fn read the same live atomic snapshot, rebuilt atomically on every re-pin); the leak was purely the fail-open fall-through. Regression-guarded by `TestGit_RefusesWhenNoRepoResolved`, `TestGit_DefaultRepoBoundaryEnforced`, and `TestFindGitRoot_EmptyPathRefuses`.

### Changed
