New `internal/tools/read_multiple_files_test.go` drives the real `read_multiple_files`→`read_file` path (the tool had no test before, which is why the rename slipped through), and two `TestResolveArgs` cases (`internal/mcp/argguard_test.go`) confirm the alias is bidirectional and schema-aware — `path`→`file_path` for `read_file`-style tools and `file_path`→`path` for `path`-canonical tools like `read_symbol` — each accepted with a warning.

## 0.7.21 (2026-05-24)

### Fixed
- **The dashboard's "uptime" widgets now track the real daemon uptime instead of the oldest live session.** The TUI Dashboard's "Tokens Saved (uptime)", "Top Tools (uptime)", and the activity chart's "↑ N calls (uptime)" were all anchored on `m.sessions[0].StartedAt` — the earliest *currently-connected* session (`session.List()` prunes dead-PID files) — with a `now − 1 minute` fallback. Because conversations start and end while the daemon keeps running, the "uptime" window actually tracked "age of the oldest live conversation", not the daemon: a 6-hour-old daemon whose only live conversation began 3 minutes ago showed a 3-minute uptime and scoped every uptime-labelled stat to those 3 minutes; a conversation ending and a new one starting made the window jump; with no live sessions it fell back to an arbitrary last minute. The fix exposes the daemon's real start time (`daemonStartedAt`, already captured at boot and reported by `daemon_info`) to the TUI by adding `StartedAt` to the metrics snapshot the TUI already polls every 2s (`monitor.DaemonMetrics` + `StartSnapshotWriter`, `internal/monitor/metrics.go`; threaded from `internal/cli/daemon.go`). A single shared anchor — `dashboardUptimeStart` (`internal/tui/dashboard.go`), now also used by `refreshActivity` (`internal/tui/model_refresh.go`) — returns that daemon start time when the snapshot is fresh, falling back to the previous oldest-live-session → `now−1m` logic when it is not (so the TUI degrades gracefully against a stale/absent snapshot or an old daemon build that does not publish the field). No stats-schema change: the daemon-singleton `flock` guarantees every recorded call since `daemonStartedAt` belongs to the current run, so the existing time-windowed queries become exact. Guards: `TestDashboardUptimeStart` (`internal/tui/model_test.go`) and the `StartedAt` round-trip in `TestSnapshotRoundTrip` (`internal/monitor/metrics_test.go`).

## 0.7.20 (2026-05-24)

### Fixed
- **Sessions in a git repo with no language marker no longer hang on "resolving…".** `workspacePool.Detect` (`internal/cli/pool.go`) now recognises a `.git/` directory as a lowest-priority workspace root marker, returning `(root, LanguageNone)`. Previously `Detect` knew only `.plumb/` and language root markers (`go.mod`, `pyproject.toml`, …); a scripts / multi-language repo (e.g. a PowerShell + Python runbook tree under a git root) matched none of them, so `Detect` errored on every path-bearing tool call and — with `auto_attach` off by default — the session never attached. Symptom: the TUI showed `Folder: (resolving workspace…)` indefinitely with `Tools: 0 / Calls: 0` (no workspace root ⇒ `onAfterTool` recorded nothing), even while the client was actively using tools. The `.git/` marker closes the gap in the default config (no `auto_attach` needed); precedence is per-directory nearest-wins, so a `.plumb/` or language marker still beats an ancestor `.git/`, and `$HOME` is excluded so a dotfiles repo there cannot capture the whole home directory. The pre-existing `auto_attach`/`SynthesiseRoot` path still covers the residual case of a seed dir with no `.git/` anywhere above it. Regression guards: `TestDetect_GitDirOnly`, `TestDetect_GitDirInAncestor`, `TestDetect_LanguageMarkerWinsOverGit`, `TestDetect_NearestLanguageMarkerWinsOverAncestorGit`, `TestDetect_GitAtHomeRefused` (`internal/cli/pool_test.go`).
- **TUI now renders an undetectable language as `?` instead of nothing.** A `LanguageNone` session (valid workspace, no LSP language — it still serves language-independent calls) shows a `?` badge in the Sessions list and `Language ?` in the details panel (`sessionLangLabel`, `internal/tui/model_left.go`; details row in `model_right.go`), making clear the session is attached and usable rather than stuck.
- **`session_start` no longer reports a phantom workspace from the daemon's working directory.** Its resolution chain dropped the `os.Getwd()` walk-up fallback (`coldStartWorkspace`): the daemon is a singleton shared across all connections, so its cwd is never a per-session signal — yet for an unresolved session `session_start` would walk up from it and confidently report an unrelated directory (e.g. the plumb checkout the daemon was launched from) that it never actually attached, so the agent saw one workspace while the TUI showed "resolving…". The chain is now: the daemon's **attached root (authoritative)** → explicit `workspace` arg → client `roots/list` → honest "pass `workspace`" error. The attached root is now preferred over the explicit arg too, so the displayed workspace always matches what the TUI, memory, and topology use (previously a `workspace` arg pointing at a subdirectory was shown while the daemon had attached the git root). `internal/tools/session_start.go`; guards `TestSessionStart_WorkspaceResolution`.
- **Claude Desktop now gets its tool guidance (and a workspace-pinning instruction).** `isClaudeDesktop` only matched the client name `claude-desktop`, but Claude Desktop identifies over MCP as **`claude-ai`** — so `writeClaudeDesktopGuidance` was dead code and Desktop users got no guidance. It now matches `claude-ai` too, and the guidance leads with: plumb cannot detect your folder (Desktop does not report it, the daemon is shared) — pass an explicit `workspace` to `session_start` to pin the project. `internal/tools/session_start.go`; guard `TestSessionStart_DesktopGuidance`.

## 0.7.19 (2026-05-24)

### Added
- **TypeScript (`.ts`) topology extraction moved onto tree-sitter — the lex-states gap is closed without a fork.** gotreesitter v0.19.1 ships the TypeScript external *scanner* but not the external *lex-states* table (`ts_external_scanner_states`), so typed arrow params (`(u: User): T => …`) cascaded ERROR nodes. The fix: the missing `typescriptExternalLexStates` table was regenerated from upstream `tree-sitter-typescript`'s `parser.c` at the **exact pinned commit gotreesitter embeds** (`75b3874…`, recorded in `grammars/grammar_updates.json`) via gotreesitter's bundled `ts2go`, and is supplied at runtime through the grammars package's *exported* `RegisterExternalLexStates` — **no vendored fork required** (`internal/topology/extractors/treesitter/ts_lex_states.go`). New `treesitter.NewTypeScript` (`.ts`) replaces the regex extractor for TypeScript: it extracts functions (declarations + arrow/function-expression bindings, incl. `export`ed), classes (incl. `abstract`) with methods, interfaces (→ `KindType`) with their method signatures, type aliases and enums (→ `KindType`) with enum members (→ `KindConstant`), top-level const/let/var, ES/`require` imports, namespace (`internal_module`) members, and describe/it/test blocks (→ `KindTest`); containment 1.0/extractor, intra-file calls 0.8/heuristic. The previously-cascading typed-arrow utility-module layout now parses with **0 ERROR/0 MISSING** (`TestTypeScript_TypedArrowNoCascade` is the regression guard; if a future gotreesitter bump desyncs the table it fails loudly). The `typescript` `langsupport` row flips `EngineRegex → EngineTreeSitter` (extensions narrowed to `.ts`).

- **Tool parameter names now match Claude Code's native tools, and a dispatch-path alias layer accepts other agents' names — so a wrong-but-meaningful parameter no longer costs extra calls.** Two parts. **(1) Canonical rename:** the file-content tools adopt Claude Code's native parameter names — `read_file`/`write_file`/`edit_file`/`delete_file`/`transaction_apply` take `file_path` (was `path`), and `edit_file`/`transaction_apply` edits take `old_string`/`new_string` (was `old_str`/`new_str`). Search/dir tools keep `path`/`pattern` (already matching `Glob`/`Grep`/`LS`). A Claude agent now hits an exact match — no alias, no warning. **(2) Alias engine** (`internal/mcp/argguard.go` + `argalias.go`, wired into `handleToolsCall`): before `Execute`, each `tools/call`'s arguments are validated against the tool's declared schema and recognised aliases are rewritten to the canonical name — recursively, schema-guided, so nested keys like `edits[].old_str` are fixed too. Resolution is a curated table (`path→file_path`, `old_str→old_string`, `filename/file→file_path`, `dir/directory→path`, `regex/query→pattern`, `new_name→name`, …, applied per-tool only where the canonical is a real parameter and isn't already set) plus case/separator normalisation (`startLine→start_line`); each applied alias adds a one-line `note:` to the result nudging toward the canonical name. It **never** guesses by edit distance — a fuzzy near-match is surfaced only as a "did you mean" *suggestion* in the rejection, never silently applied (safe for write/edit/delete tools). A genuinely unknown parameter, or a missing `required` one, is still rejected with the valid-parameter list. Unknown-property rejection is **opt-in per schema** (`additionalProperties: false`, now on every tool schema, drift-guarded by `TestInputSchemasDeclareAdditionalProperties`); the missing-required check applies regardless; odd/unparseable schemas fail open with a WARN. `rename_session` also gained machine-readable `minLength`/`maxLength`/`pattern` on its `name` argument (pattern agreement with `session.NormaliseName` is test-guarded). Previously a wrong key like `{"new_name": …}` (or the native `old_string` on `edit_file`) was silently dropped by lenient JSON decoding, producing a misleading `… is required` and forcing the caller to guess again. `seedPathFromArgs` learned the `file_path` shape so workspace auto-seeding still works.

### Known limitations
- **TSX/JSX (`.tsx`/`.jsx`) stay on the regex extractor.** With the regenerated TSX lex-states attached, JSX itself parses clean, but gotreesitter v0.19.1's **TSX grammar still cascades on typed arrow parameters** (e.g. `const f = (x: number): number => x` → 4 ERROR nodes), which would silently drop trailing symbols from typed-arrow-heavy components — worse than the regex extractor for real-world `.tsx`. This is a residual grammar issue beyond the lex-states gap. A new `tsx` `langsupport` row (`.tsx`/`.jsx`, `EngineRegex`) keeps them on the narrowed regex extractor; closing it needs an upstream TSX-grammar fix or the WASM/wazero path. The correct TSX lex-states table is generated and registered (ready for when the grammar issue is resolved).

## 0.7.18 (2026-05-24)

### Added
- **LSP adapter for Kotlin (kotlin-language-server), unit-tested; integration test ready and gated.** New `internal/lsp/adapters/kotlin` implements the full `lsp.Client` interface, answers `client/registerCapability`/`unregisterCapability`, and bases capabilities on `protocol.DefaultClientCapabilities()`. Wired into the daemon (`newAdapter`/`initParamsFor`) and the default `[lsp]` map as `kotlin` (`Command: kotlin-language-server`, `RootMarkers: [settings.gradle.kts, build.gradle.kts]`, **disabled by default** — opt in with `[lsp.kotlin] enabled = true`); the `kotlin` `langsupport` row now names `kotlin-language-server`, pairing the semantic GPS with the tree-sitter Kotlin Map. (The `build.gradle.kts` marker overlaps Java's; with both enabled, the alphabetical detect order makes Java win — both are opt-in, so this is moot by default.) **Validation status: experimental** — unit-tested with the mock transport; the real-binary integration test (`testdata/kotlin-fixture/` + a `DidChangeWatchedFiles` → diagnostics round-trip, gated `//go:build integration`) is written but **skips until `kotlin-language-server` is installed** (`brew install kotlin-language-server`). Promote to validated once it has run green against the real server.
- **LSP adapter for TypeScript/JavaScript (typescript-language-server), unit-tested; integration test ready and gated.** New `internal/lsp/adapters/typescript` implements the full `lsp.Client` interface, answers `client/registerCapability`/`unregisterCapability`, and bases capabilities on `protocol.DefaultClientCapabilities()`. Wired into the daemon (`newAdapter`/`initParamsFor`, imported aliased as `tsls` to avoid colliding with the topology `typescript` extractor package) and the default `[lsp]` map as `typescript` (`Command: typescript-language-server`, `Args: [--stdio]`, `RootMarkers: [tsconfig.json, jsconfig.json, package.json]`, **disabled by default** — opt in with `[lsp.typescript] enabled = true`). This server serves **both** TypeScript and JavaScript, so both the `typescript` and `javascript` `langsupport` rows now name it — pairing the semantic GPS with the regex TS structural Map and the tree-sitter JS Map respectively. **Validation status: experimental** — unit-tested with the mock transport; the real-binary integration test (`testdata/typescript-fixture/` + a `DidChangeWatchedFiles` → diagnostics round-trip, gated `//go:build integration`) is written but **skips until `typescript-language-server` is installed** (`npm install -g typescript-language-server typescript`). Promote to validated once it has run green against the real server.
- **LSP adapter for Zig (zls), unit-tested; integration test ready and gated.** New `internal/lsp/adapters/zig` implements the full `lsp.Client` interface, answers `client/registerCapability`/`unregisterCapability`, and bases capabilities on `protocol.DefaultClientCapabilities()`. Wired into the daemon (`newAdapter`/`initParamsFor`) and the default `[lsp]` map as `zig` (`Command: zls`, `RootMarkers: [build.zig, build.zig.zon]`, **disabled by default** — opt in with `[lsp.zig] enabled = true`); the `zig` `langsupport` row now names `zls`, pairing the semantic GPS with the tree-sitter Zig Map. **Validation status: experimental** — unit-tested with the mock transport (every interface method); the real-binary integration test (`testdata/zig-fixture/` + a `DidChangeWatchedFiles` → diagnostics round-trip, gated `//go:build integration`) is written but **skips until `zls` is installed on the validation machine** (it was not). Promote to validated once it has run green against a real zls. zls + tree-sitter-zig track the Zig language version (pre-1.0).
- **LSP adapter for Swift (sourcekit-lsp), validated against the real binary.** New `internal/lsp/adapters/swift` implements the full `lsp.Client` interface, answers `client/registerCapability`/`unregisterCapability`, and bases capabilities on `protocol.DefaultClientCapabilities()`. Wired into the daemon (`newAdapter`/`initParamsFor`) and the default `[lsp]` map as `swift` (`Command: sourcekit-lsp`, `RootMarkers: [Package.swift]`, **disabled by default** — opt in with `[lsp.swift] enabled = true`); the `swift` `langsupport` row now names `sourcekit-lsp`, pairing the semantic GPS with the tree-sitter Swift Map. sourcekit-lsp ships with the Swift toolchain (Xcode or swift.org; `/usr/bin/sourcekit-lsp` on macOS) and derives per-file compiler arguments from the SwiftPM build plan. Unit-tested with the mock transport and **integration-tested against a real sourcekit-lsp** (gated `//go:build integration`, `testdata/swift-fixture/` SwiftPM package): document-symbol extraction + a `DidChangeWatchedFiles` + `DidOpen` → diagnostics round-trip, both passing.
- **LSP adapter for Rust (rust-analyzer), validated against the real binary.** New `internal/lsp/adapters/rust` implements the full `lsp.Client` interface (mirroring the pyright worked example), answers `client/registerCapability`/`unregisterCapability` via `SetRequestHandler` so rust-analyzer's dynamic file-watcher registration is honoured, and bases its client capabilities on `protocol.DefaultClientCapabilities()`. Wired into the daemon (`newAdapter`/`initParamsFor` in `internal/cli/pool.go`) and added to the default `[lsp]` map as `rust` (`Command: rust-analyzer`, `RootMarkers: [Cargo.toml]`, **disabled by default** — opt in with `[lsp.rust] enabled = true`); the `rust` `langsupport` row now names `rust-analyzer` as its adapter, pairing the semantic GPS with the existing tree-sitter Rust Map. Unit-tested with the mock transport (every interface method) and **integration-tested against a real rust-analyzer** (gated `//go:build integration`, `testdata/rust-fixture/`): a document-symbol extraction test and a `DidChangeWatchedFiles` + `DidOpen` → diagnostics round-trip, both passing. **Cold-start note:** rust-analyzer loads the sysroot and runs `cargo metadata` on first attach (can take minutes on a large workspace) — the canonical unavailability case the structural layer covers while it warms.

## 0.7.17 (2026-05-24)

### Added
- **Tree-sitter topology extraction for JavaScript (`.js`/`.mjs`/`.cjs`), split off the regex TS/JS extractor.** Plain JavaScript parses cleanly under gotreesitter — it has none of the typed-arrow syntax that trips the missing TypeScript external lex-states table — so it no longer needs the fragile regex scanner. New `treesitter.NewJavaScript`, registered as an `EngineTreeSitter` `javascript` row in `internal/langsupport` (owning `.js`/`.mjs`/`.cjs`) and wired into `buildExtractors`; the `typescript` regex row is narrowed to `.ts`/`.tsx`/`.jsx` only. It extracts top-level **functions** (declarations and arrow/function-expression bindings, including `export`ed ones), **classes** with their **methods** (lexical containment, 1.0/extractor), top-level **constants**/**variables** (`const` → constant, `let`/`var` → variable), ES `import` and CommonJS `require` **imports** (the module path), and `describe`/`it`/`test` blocks at any nesting depth (→ `KindTest`). Intra-file **call edges** are name-resolved heuristics (0.8/heuristic), resolving calls inside functions, arrow bindings and methods. JavaScript probed clean (0 ERROR/0 MISSING) on an idiomatic multi-line sample. This is the cheap interim win of the (still-blocked) Phase 8 TS/TSX flip — only `.ts`/`.tsx`/`.jsx` remain on regex. Tests in `internal/topology/extractors/treesitter/javascript_test.go`.

## 0.7.16 (2026-05-24)

### Added
- **Symbol tools keep working when the language server is cold or cannot parse the file (tree-sitter fallback).** `read_symbol`, `insert_before_symbol`, `insert_after_symbol` and `replace_symbol_body` now fall back to a **fresh tree-sitter parse** of the current file (via the topology index) when the LSP `documentSymbol` call errors or times out — the symbol is located structurally and the operation proceeds, annotated `[topology fallback — LSP unavailable; … range is line-granular]`. The new `Store.ExtractFile` re-parses the file *as it is on disk right now* (not the possibly-stale persisted index), so the resolved ranges are accurate; the edit application path already errors cleanly (never corrupts) on an out-of-range position, the tools remain **dry-run by default**, and the fallback only engages when the LSP path fails — so the LSP-up behaviour is byte-for-byte unchanged. `safe_delete_symbol` deliberately has **no** fallback: its safety guarantee is the LSP reference check, which topology cannot reproduce. Wired via a nil-safe `WithTopologyFallback` setter on each tool (mirrors the existing query-tool fallbacks). Shared helpers in `internal/tools/symbol_topology_fallback.go`; tests in `symbol_topology_fallback_test.go` (read, replace incl. exact-bytes + dry-run, insert, and no-fallback-surfaces-error). This is the resilience half of the Phase 4 "byte-precise surgical edits" item; the char-precise doc-comment/signature/body sub-range separation (which would retire the `include_doc_comment` heuristic) is deferred — it needs character-precise ranges in `topology.Node`, a schema change touching every extractor.

## 0.7.15 (2026-05-24)

### Changed
- **`topology_affected` is now the headline tool: recall-biased, confidence-labelled, and co-location-aware.** Previously it only walked inward dependency edges — but the extractors emit *intra-file* call edges only, so a test in a sibling file (`foo_test.go` beside `foo.go`, `test_foo.py` beside `foo.py`) that exercises a changed symbol was not graph-connected and went unreported. It now adds a **co-location pass**: tests in the same directory as any changed or affected file are flagged too (new `Store.TestsInDirs`, matching on the immediate parent directory). Every affected test now carries a **confidence** and the **reason** it was flagged — `1.0` certain (containment), `0.8` dependency edge, `0.5` co-located (same directory, no edge) — and tests are ordered highest-confidence first. The output leads with an explicit `source=topology — heuristic, biased toward recall (a missed test is worse than an extra)` caveat, and the tool description now frames it as *the* post-change "which tests to run" tool that no language server provides. New `incidentConfidence` confidence derivation; `collectAffected` decomposed into an `affectedGather` (graph pass + co-location pass + sort) to stay within the complexity budget. Tests in `internal/tools/topology_affected_test.go` and `topology_affected_e2e_test.go` (the e2e test proves a sibling test with no call edge is still caught); `docs/topology.md` updated.
- **`session_start` guidance leads with topology when the index is active.** The Claude Code (and Claude Desktop) tool guidance is the surface an agent actually reads every session, so it now frames the two-layer model explicitly: **Topology (the Map)** — `topology_affected`, `topology_search`, `topology_explore`/`impact`, `file_outline`, `topology_routes` — as the primary path for discovery / structure / impact (led by `topology_affected` as *the* post-change "which tests to run" tool), and **LSP (the GPS)** — `get_definition`/`find_references`/`rename_symbol`/hierarchies — for precise, type-aware navigation. When topology is **not** enabled the guidance keeps its prior LSP-led form plus a one-line tip to enable the index. Wired via a nil-safe `SessionStart.WithTopology` setter (mirrors `WithTopologyFallback`); the daemon passes the live store accessor so the guidance reflects whether the index is actually running. Tests `TestSessionStart_TopologyLedGuidance` and `TestSessionStart_LSPLedGuidanceWhenTopologyOff`.

## 0.7.14 (2026-05-24)

### Added
- **Tree-sitter topology extraction for shell scripts (Bash).** `treesitter.NewBash` (`.sh`, `.bash`) joins the gotreesitter family, registered as an `EngineTreeSitter` row in `internal/langsupport` and wired into `buildExtractors`. It extracts shell **functions** (both `name()` and `function name` forms), top-level **variables** and **constants** (`readonly`/`declare -r` → constant, otherwise variable; function-local `local`/`declare` bindings are correctly *not* surfaced as module-level symbols), `source`/`.` **imports** (the sourced path), and intra-file **call edges** between functions (a command whose name matches a defined function). Containment is n/a (shell has no nesting we model); call sites are certain but the callee is name-resolved within the file, so call edges are heuristic (0.8/heuristic). Bash parsed clean (0 ERROR/0 MISSING) on idiomatic multi-line scripts (it is one of the few grammars with its external lex-states wired). First of the *grammar-breadth* phase — a net-new language with no prior extractor and no plumb LSP, so direct moat value for polyglot repos. Tests in `internal/topology/extractors/treesitter/bash_test.go`.
- **Tree-sitter topology extraction for HCL (Terraform/Packer/Nomad).** `treesitter.NewHCL` (`.tf`, `.tfvars`, `.hcl`) joins the gotreesitter family. It extracts the top-level blocks as searchable nodes: `variable` → variable, `output` and `locals` entries → constant, `resource`/`data`/`provider` (and any other labelled block) → type named after its quoted labels (e.g. `aws_instance.web`, `data.aws_ami.ubuntu`), `module` → import. The `terraform { … }` settings block is skipped (no searchable declaration). HCL declarations are flat, so no containment edges are emitted. HCL parsed clean (0 ERROR/0 MISSING) on idiomatic Terraform despite its external scanner lacking a lex-states table (its scanner work does not gate the failing parser states, like Rust/Swift). Net-new language; tests in `internal/topology/extractors/treesitter/hcl_test.go`.
- **Tree-sitter topology extraction for SQL (DDL).** `treesitter.NewSQL` (`.sql`) joins the gotreesitter family, and a new `topology.KindField` node kind is introduced for structured members that are neither methods nor standalone variables. It extracts `CREATE TABLE`/`VIEW`/`INDEX` (and any other `CREATE …`) statement as a **type** named after the created object, and each table column as a contained **field** (`KindField`, qualified `table.column`) linked by a certain (1.0/extractor) containment edge. Data-manipulation statements (`INSERT`/`SELECT`/`UPDATE`/`DELETE`) are operations, not declarations, and are not indexed. SQL parsed clean (0 ERROR/0 MISSING) on idiomatic DDL+DML. Net-new language; tests in `internal/topology/extractors/treesitter/sql_test.go`.
- **Tree-sitter topology extraction for Dockerfiles, plus extensionless-file matching.** `treesitter.NewDockerfile` joins the gotreesitter family. Because Dockerfiles usually have no extension, `findExtractor` (`internal/topology/extractor.go`) and `langsupport.ByPath` now accept **bare filename patterns** (not dot-prefixed): a pattern like `dockerfile` matches the basename exactly or as a dotted prefix/suffix — `Dockerfile`, `Dockerfile.prod`, `prod.dockerfile`, `Containerfile`. The extractor indexes each build stage (`FROM …`, named after its `AS` alias or base image) as a **type**, and the `ENV`/`ARG` declarations that follow it as **variables** contained in that stage (lexical containment, 1.0/extractor). Dockerfile parsed clean (0 ERROR/0 MISSING) on a multi-stage build. `TestRegistryConsistency` is relaxed to allow bare filename patterns (which must not contain a dot); new `TestFindExtractor_ExtensionAndBasename` covers the matcher. Net-new language; tests in `internal/topology/extractors/treesitter/dockerfile_test.go`.
- **Tree-sitter topology extraction for TOML.** `treesitter.NewTOML` (`.toml`) joins the gotreesitter family. It indexes each `[table]` / `[[array.table]]` header as a **type** (named by its dotted key, e.g. `server.tls`, `database.replica`), every top-level `key = value` pair and every pair inside a table as a **field** (`KindField`, qualified `table.key`), with table→field links as certain (1.0/extractor) containment edges. Useful for `Cargo.toml`/`pyproject.toml`/config discovery. TOML parsed clean (0 ERROR/0 MISSING) — it has no external scanner, so no lex-states risk. Net-new language; tests in `internal/topology/extractors/treesitter/toml_test.go`.
- **Tree-sitter topology extraction for YAML.** `treesitter.NewYAML` (`.yaml`, `.yml`) joins the gotreesitter family. It indexes **every block-mapping key** as a field, linked to its enclosing key by a certain (1.0/extractor) containment edge, so the whole config tree is navigable (e.g. `services` → `web` → `image` for docker-compose); keys reached through a block sequence (lists of objects) attach to the nearest enclosing key. Useful for compose files, CI workflows and k8s manifests. YAML parsed clean (0 ERROR/0 MISSING) — it has its external lex-states wired. Net-new language; tests in `internal/topology/extractors/treesitter/yaml_test.go`.
- **Tree-sitter topology extraction for Markdown.** `treesitter.NewMarkdown` (`.md`, `.markdown`) joins the gotreesitter family, and a new `topology.KindSection` node kind is introduced for document headings. The grammar nests a `section` per heading, mirroring the heading hierarchy, so each heading is indexed as a section node with a certain (1.0/extractor) containment edge from a heading to the sub-headings beneath it (`## H2` under `# H1`). Both ATX (`#`) and setext (underline) headings are handled. Gives doc/README discoverability (`topology_search` for a heading, `file_outline`-style navigation). Markdown parsed clean (0 ERROR/0 MISSING). `langsupport.ByPath("README.md")` now resolves to `markdown` (previously unmatched). Net-new language; tests in `internal/topology/extractors/treesitter/markdown_test.go`. **Completes the grammar-breadth phase** — Bash, HCL, SQL, Dockerfile, TOML, YAML and Markdown all probed clean and shipped; none deferred.

## 0.7.13 (2026-05-24)

### Added
- **Tree-sitter topology extraction for Java.** `treesitter.NewJava` (`.java`) joins the gotreesitter family; the `java` `langsupport` row flips `EngineNone → EngineTreeSitter` (keeping its existing `jdtls` LSP adapter — Java now has both the structural Map *and* the semantic GPS). It extracts classes/records/enums (`KindClass`), **interfaces as `KindType`**, methods and constructors, fields (`final` → constant, otherwise variable; multi-declarator fields handled), enum constants (constants), `import` declarations, and `@Test`-annotated tests. Names resolve via the grammar's `name` field; container→member containment is lexical and certain (1.0/extractor); intra-file calls are name-resolved heuristics (0.8/heuristic; same-name methods such as an interface requirement and its implementation share a key, so a call may attribute to either — inherent to the heuristic); locals inside method bodies are not surfaced. Java parsed clean (0 ERROR/0 MISSING) on idiomatic source; tests in `internal/topology/extractors/treesitter/java_test.go`.
- **Tree-sitter topology extraction for Swift (net-new language).** `treesitter.NewSwift` (`.swift`) joins the gotreesitter family, registered as an `EngineTreeSitter` row in `internal/langsupport` and wired into `buildExtractors`. It extracts types (`struct`/`class`/`enum`/`actor` and `extension`, all `KindClass`), **protocols as `KindType`** (a contract, mirroring the Rust trait / Kotlin interface mapping), top-level functions, methods (incl. extension methods and protocol requirements), member and top-level properties (`let` → constant, `var` → variable), enum cases (constants), `import` declarations, and **XCTest tests** (methods named `test…` inside an `XCTestCase` subclass). Container→member containment is lexical and certain (1.0/extractor); intra-file calls are name-resolved heuristics (0.8/heuristic); locals inside function bodies are not surfaced. Swift was re-probed clean (0 ERROR/0 MISSING) on idiomatic multi-line source. Pure addition — Swift had no structural extractor and no plumb LSP, so it is direct moat value; tests in `internal/topology/extractors/treesitter/swift_test.go`.
- **New `file_outline` tool — a token-cheap file skeleton.** `internal/tools/file_outline.go` returns every symbol in a file as its **signature line with the body collapsed**, nested by containment, with byte-precise 1-based line ranges — a 2000-line file's shape in a few hundred tokens, so an agent can decide what to read without reading the file. Symbols come from the language server (`documentSymbol`) when one answers and from the **tree-sitter topology index** when the server is cold or does not cover the file (the output is annotated `source=lsp`/`source=topology`), so the outline still works where no warm LSP serves the file. Multi-line signatures are joined and the body opener stripped; `include_docs` (default true) prepends the first line of each symbol's leading doc comment. It shares the documentSymbol cache with `list_symbols` and reuses the nil-safe `WithTopologyFallback` wiring. Registered in `registerAllTools` (tool count 47 → 48); tests in `internal/tools/file_outline_test.go`; documented in `docs/tools.md`.
- **Tree-sitter topology extraction for Kotlin (net-new language).** `treesitter.NewKotlin` (`.kt`, `.kts`) joins the gotreesitter family, registered as an `EngineTreeSitter` row in `internal/langsupport` and wired into `buildExtractors`. It extracts classes (`class`/`data class`/`sealed class`/`enum class`, `object`, and `companion object` — anonymous companions recorded as `Companion`), **interfaces as `KindType`** (a type contract, mirroring the Rust trait mapping), top-level functions, methods, member and top-level properties (`val`/`const val` → constant, `var` → variable), enum entries (as constants), `import` headers, and `@Test`-annotated tests (including backtick-quoted method names, whose backticks are stripped). Container→member containment (class→method, class→property, class→nested class, enum→entry) is lexical and certain (1.0/extractor); intra-file calls are name-resolved heuristics (0.8/heuristic); local declarations inside function bodies are correctly *not* surfaced as symbols. This is a pure addition — Kotlin previously had no structural extractor and has no LSP, so it is direct moat value (a language native LSP cannot serve). Kotlin was re-verified parseable on idiomatic multi-line files (see the 0.7.13 *Documentation* note); tests in `internal/topology/extractors/treesitter/kotlin_test.go`.

### Changed
- **`topology_explore`/`topology_impact` byte budgeting is now source-aware and AST-boundary-explicit.** `estimateBytes` previously charged every node for its signature even when `include_source=none` and ignored the richer source modes, so the byte budget did not match the rendered output. It now costs a node by what the chosen source mode actually emits — signature only when shown, plus docstring for `snippets`/`full` — so `max_bytes` honestly bounds the result and `none` fits strictly more neighbours under the same budget. Truncation remains on **symbol boundaries**: a neighbour is added only if it fits in full, so a truncated neighbourhood is always a set of whole, coherent symbols (never a fragment of a function). The `snippets`/`full` modes now also surface each symbol's docstring (previously identical to `signatures`). New tests `TestEstimateBytes_SourceModes` and `TestExplore_ByteBudgetWholeSymbols` in `internal/topology/`; `docs/tools.md` updated.

### Documentation
- **Corrected the tree-sitter fidelity record: only TypeScript/TSX is blocked, not Kotlin.** A second, independent re-verification pass (realistic, idiomatic, multi-line `.ts/.tsx/.kt` probe files, counting `ERROR`/`MISSING` nodes) overturned the earlier "Kotlin blocked" conclusion — that was an artefact of single-*line* snippets. Idiomatic multi-line Kotlin (data/sealed/enum/object/companion classes, interfaces, generics, extension funs, `@Test`, backtick-quoted method names) parses with **0 ERROR / 0 MISSING** nodes; gotreesitter v0.19.1 even ships explicit Kotlin recovery tests. The pass also *sharpened* the TypeScript block: typed arrow params (`(u: User) => …`) cascade into ERROR nodes, and the breakage is **context-dependent** (the identical arrow parses clean when preceded by an interface/decorator/class but cascades 7–12 ERRORs in a utility-module layout) — worse than deterministic failure for an extractor, so TS/TSX stays on regex. Plain JavaScript is clean. Mechanism re-confirmed in the module cache (only `bash`/`python`/`yaml` define `*ExternalLexStates` variables; there is no `typescriptExternalLexStates`). Updated the internal tree-sitter design notes, `AGENTS.md`, and the 0.7.12 entry above.

## 0.7.12 (2026-05-22)

### Added
- **Python topology extraction now uses tree-sitter (gotreesitter), replacing the regex scanner.** The new `internal/topology/extractors/treesitter` package parses Python with the pure-Go [gotreesitter](https://github.com/odvcencio/gotreesitter) runtime (no CGo): real class/function nesting, accurate end-lines, certain (1.0) class→method containment edges, and name-resolved intra-file call edges (0.8). The legacy regex Python extractor is removed, and a new `internal/langsupport` registry selects each language's structural engine. gotreesitter embeds all 206 grammar blobs plus its pure-Go runtime, so the binary grows ~26 MB (20→46 MB) — in exchange plumb gains structural awareness of every supported language (the basis for upcoming TS/JS/Rust/Zig and broader-language extractors). Validated at scale in Phase 0 (Python 99.94% clean over the CPython stdlib).
- **Tree-sitter topology extraction for Rust and Zig (net-new languages).** `treesitter.NewRust` (`.rs`) and `treesitter.NewZig` (`.zig`) join the gotreesitter family, registered as `EngineTreeSitter` rows in `internal/langsupport` and wired into `buildExtractors`. Rust extracts functions, methods (incl. trait default/signature methods), types (struct/enum/union/trait/type-alias), constants, statics, `use` imports and `#[test]`-family tests (correctly *not* matching `#[cfg(test)]`); Zig extracts functions, container methods, types bound to `const X = struct/enum/union`, constants, variables, `@import` imports and `test "…"` blocks. Lexical containment edges are certain (1.0/extractor); impl-method→type links and intra-file calls are name-resolved heuristics (0.8/heuristic). These are pure additions — Rust and Zig previously had no structural extractor and have no LSP, so this is direct moat value (languages native LSP cannot serve). Tests in `internal/topology/extractors/treesitter/{rust,zig}_test.go`.
- **Documented a gotreesitter v0.19.1 fidelity limit that defers the TypeScript/TSX flip.** gotreesitter registers external *scanners* for ~100 languages but defines the external **lex-states** tables (`ts_external_scanner_states`, which gate when the GLR parser invokes the scanner) as actual variables for only a few (`bashExternalLexStates`, `pythonExternalLexStates`, `yamlExternalLexStates` — there is no `typescriptExternalLexStates`). Without it, real-world **TypeScript** breaks on typed arrow params (`(u: User) => …` cascades into ERROR nodes that swallow following symbols) — whereas **Rust, Zig, Kotlin and Swift** parse cleanly (their scanners do lexical work that does not depend on the missing per-state gating), and **plain JavaScript** is unaffected (no type syntax). TS/TSX therefore stays on the regex extractor until the lex-states are regenerated from upstream (or a WASM/wazero fallback is added) — tracked as the final phase internally. (An initial pass also flagged **Kotlin** as blocked; re-verification in 0.7.13 found that was a single-line-snippet artefact — idiomatic multi-line Kotlin parses cleanly, and the Kotlin extractor ships in 0.7.13.)
- **The TUI Sessions panel now shows a topology row.** The Details tab gains a `Topology` line for the selected session's workspace — e.g. `1,234 nodes · 56 files · 4.2 MiB · go` — read read-only from `<folder>/.plumb/topology.db` via `topology.StatusForWorkspace` (no daemon round-trip; the row is omitted when the workspace has no index). New `Model.refreshTopology` and `topologyDetailRow` in `internal/tui/`. Together with the 0.7.12 `plumb doctor` check this completes topology visibility. Part of the topology default-enable readiness work.
- **`plumb doctor` now reports topology index health.** A new "Indexing" section (also emitted by `plumb doctor --json`) checks the per-workspace topology index: it passes when topology is disabled (the opt-in default), and when enabled reports indexed file/node/edge counts, DB size, and indexed languages — failing with a fix hint when the index is missing or corrupt (an index that is merely still building is a non-fatal warning — see *Changed*). The check reads the on-disk index read-only via the new `topology.StatusForWorkspace`, without starting an indexer or disturbing a running daemon. New `checkTopology`/`checkTopologyIndex` + `humanBytes` in `internal/cli/doctor.go`; tests in `internal/cli/doctor_topology_test.go` and `internal/topology/status_workspace_test.go`. Part of the topology default-enable readiness work (item 2).
- **The topology index is now kept out of version control automatically.** Whenever the topology database is opened or created, plumb writes (or updates) a `.plumb/.gitignore` that excludes `topology.db` and its SQLite sidecar files (`-wal`/`-shm`). The index is a large, rebuildable, high-churn binary; this stops it being accidentally committed in workspaces that deliberately track `.plumb/` (which also holds `context.md` and `memories/`). The guard runs before the DB file is created, is idempotent (appends only the missing entries and preserves existing `.gitignore` content), and is best-effort (failures are logged, not fatal). New `ensureGitignore` in `internal/topology/db.go`; covered by `internal/topology/gitignore_test.go`. Part of the topology default-enable readiness work tracked internally.
- **Configurable path abbreviation style in the Sessions sidebar.** The folder path shown under each session name is now formatted according to `[ui] path_style` in `config.toml`, with three options: **`compact`** (new default) abbreviates every intermediate directory component to its first letter and keeps the final component in full — e.g. `~/Projects/experiments/others/cve-explorer` → `~/P/e/o/cve-explorer`; **`truncate-middle`** preserves the previous behaviour of keeping the tail of the path after a leading `…`; **`full`** shows the tilde-home path without abbreviation, falling back to `…/<last>` only when the column is too narrow. The setting is also editable live in the TUI Settings screen (Appearance group, `←→` to cycle) and takes effect immediately without a daemon restart. New helper functions `contractPathCompact`, `contractPathFull`, and `contractPathTruncateLeft` in `internal/tui/model_utils.go` back the three strategies.

### Changed
- **`plumb doctor`'s topology check distinguishes a pending index from a broken one, the index is read strictly read-only, and the TUI debounces its reads.** Three review follow-ups to the 0.7.12 "Indexing" check (resolving three open review questions): (1) an enabled index that *exists* but has not finished its first pass is now a non-fatal **warning** (`!`), not a failure — `plumb doctor` no longer emits a false negative or a non-zero exit during the cold-start indexing window. The new `topologyIndexHealth` helper classifies four states — empty (initial indexing in progress), all files skipped, files indexed but no symbols (legitimate for a docs/config-only tree, and also the signature of a broken extractor, so it is surfaced), and healthy — while only a *missing* or *corrupt* DB stays a hard failure. `checkResult` gains a `warn` field (rendered `!`, styled like a failure but never counted toward the exit code), the run summary reports the warning count, and `plumb doctor --json` gains a matching `warn` field. (2) `topology.StatusForWorkspace` now opens the index with `mode=ro` (mirroring `stats.OpenReadOnly`) so an inspection while the daemon is down never writes the main DB or creates `-wal`/`-shm` sidecars. (3) The TUI debounces the per-tick topology read to at most once per 5 s (and immediately when the selected session's workspace changes) instead of opening the DB on every 2 s poll. New `topologyIndexHealth`/`printCheck` in `internal/cli/doctor.go`; `Model.topoStatusAt` debounce in `internal/tui/`; tests in `internal/cli/doctor_topology_test.go`, `internal/topology/status_workspace_test.go`, and `internal/tui/model_topology_test.go`.
- **Topology resync is now throttled, and periodic resync is on by default.** The full index resync (`processResync`) pauses for `[topology] resync_pause_ms` (default 25 ms) after every `[topology] resync_batch` files (default 100), so a large workspace's index build yields CPU to live tool calls rather than saturating a core — write-triggered upserts are never paced, and the pause is interruptible so shutdown stays fast. `[topology] resync_interval_minutes` now defaults to **60** (was effectively 0/disabled), so an enabled index recovers from external changes (`git pull`, a branch switch, edits by other tools) without waiting for the next attach. All three knobs are configurable and validated as non-negative (0 disables). New `Indexer.pace`; `validate` split into `validateQuality`/`validateTopology` to stay within the complexity budget. Tests in `internal/topology/pace_test.go`. Part of the topology default-enable readiness work (items 1 and 2).

### Fixed
- **Topology indexer no longer silently drops file updates when its queue is full.** `Indexer.Enqueue` writes to a 256-deep buffered queue and previously dropped any operation that arrived while the buffer was full, which could leave the index permanently stale until the next attach-time resync. A queue overflow now sets a pending-resync flag (`resyncPending`); the worker reconciles the whole tree at the end of its current cycle (`runQueueCycle`) so dropped per-file updates self-heal rather than being lost. Tests `TestIndexer_EnqueueOverflowFlagsResync` and `TestIndexer_RunQueueCycle_HonoursPendingResync` in `internal/topology/`. Part of the topology default-enable readiness work (item 4).
- **Sessions sidebar no longer appends a trailing `…` to abbreviated paths.** The cell renderer in `model_render.go` clips every left-panel line to `m.leftWidth-1` characters. The available-width budget passed to `contractPath` was off by one, so the path line was always exactly one character over the limit and the renderer silently replaced the last character with `…`. The budget is now `m.leftWidth - 8` (prefix width + 1 guard) so the formatted line fits within the renderer threshold.
- **CI: the `integration` job no longer fails decoding the pyright `initialize` result.** The LSP spec types `ServerCapabilities.textDocumentSync` as `TextDocumentSyncOptions | TextDocumentSyncKind`, but the struct only accepted the object form; recent pyright returns the bare `TextDocumentSyncKind` number, so the result decode failed with `cannot unmarshal number into Go struct field … of type protocol.TextDocumentSyncOptions`. `TextDocumentSyncOptions` now has an `UnmarshalJSON` that accepts both the object and the bare-number forms. New `internal/lsp/protocol/types_test.go` covers both wire shapes.
- **CI: the `ci` lint job no longer trips gosec G115 on `internal/monitor/process_linux.go`.** Two integer conversions on the Linux-only `/proc` reader (`uint64(os.Getpagesize())` and `time.Duration(ticks)`) are provably in range — page size is a small positive power of two, and the CPU clock-tick count cannot approach `math.MaxInt64` — and are now annotated with justified `//nolint:gosec // G115:` directives, matching the existing suppression convention.
- **CI: the `integration` job's pyright watched-files test now passes against a real pyright.** `TestIntegration_DidChangeWatchedFiles` wrote a broken `.py` file, announced it via `didChangeWatchedFiles`, and waited for error diagnostics — but pyright runs in its default `openFilesOnly` diagnostic mode and only publishes diagnostics for *open* documents, so a watched-file notification for an unopened file never produced any and the step timed out. (The test had only just begun reaching this point on CI, after the earlier jdtls-download and `initialize`-decode fixes unblocked the job.) It now opens the file with `didOpen` after the watched-files notification — exactly what plumb's `diagnostics` tool does in production (`internal/tools/diagnostics.go`) — so it exercises the real external-write → notify → open → diagnostics pipeline end to end against a live server. Confirmed locally against pyright: diagnostics arrive in under a second once the file is opened. `internal/lsp/adapters/pyright/integration_test.go`.

### Documentation
- **Rewrote the Topology guide for newcomers and refreshed the config docs.** `docs/topology.md` now opens with a plain-language "what is it / why it exists / benefits" introduction and a "how it works" architecture section aimed at readers new to the concept, and `docs/architecture.md` links to it. `docs/configuration.md` is updated to match the new resync settings (`resync_batch`, `resync_pause_ms`, and `resync_interval_minutes` now defaulting to 60).
- **Documented the `plumb doctor` topology check and the topology LSP fallback.** `docs/cli-reference.md` now lists the new "Indexing" section under `plumb doctor`; `docs/tools.md` notes the topology fallback (shipped in 0.7.8) on `find_symbol`, `workspace_symbols`, and `list_symbols`.

## 0.7.11 (2026-05-22)

### Fixed
- **Sessions stuck on "resolving…" when the language server is unavailable.** When `gopls` or `pyright` is not on the daemon's `$PATH`, `attachWorkspace` previously returned early — before calling `session.Patch` to set `info.Folder` — leaving every session with an empty workspace in the TUI and preventing stats attribution. The workspace is now always recorded; if LSP acquisition fails the session degrades to filesystem-only mode (`LanguageNone`) so the TUI, stats, and all non-LSP tools continue to work.

## 0.7.10 (2026-05-22)

### Fixed
- **CI: the `integration` job no longer 404s installing jdtls.** The step resolved the jdtls tarball from `api.github.com/repos/eclipse-jdtls/eclipse.jdt.ls/releases/latest`, but that repository publishes no language-server releases — its only release is an unrelated pre-release VSIX, so `releases/latest` returned 404, `ASSET_URL` resolved to empty, and `curl` then failed with "Malformed input to a URL function". jdtls is distributed via `download.eclipse.org`, not GitHub Releases. The step now resolves the newest stable milestone (and its timestamped tarball) from `download.eclipse.org/jdtls/milestones/`, falls back to the rolling `snapshots/jdt-language-server-latest.tar.gz` if the listing cannot be parsed, and no longer needs `GH_TOKEN`. `docs/adding-an-lsp.md` updated to point at the Eclipse download server for the same reason.

### Documentation
- **Documented the unified `git` tool's full behavioural contract.** The safe-biased tier classification of ambiguous subcommands (`checkout -b` is a write but any other `checkout` is destructive; `restore --staged` vs `restore --worktree`; `switch --force`; bare `git stash` is a write; `branch`/`tag` create vs delete vs list), the typed `add`/`commit` footgun protection (only `commit -m <message>` / `add -- <files>` ever run, so `--amend`/`--no-verify`/`-F`/editor/globs are unreachable, and pre-commit hooks always run), the write-rate-limit slot consumed by every non-read tier, and the output caps (200 lines for `log`/`blame`, 100 KiB overall) were all implemented but undocumented. Now recorded in `docs/tools.md` (full contract), the `AGENTS.md` `[git]` section, and `docs/configuration.md` (classification note + cross-link).

## 0.7.9 (2026-05-22)

### Changed
- **Automatic session names are now lowercase.** Newly generated session names now use `adjective-noun` form such as `swift-falcon`, while user-provided names through `rename_session` still preserve the entered case.
- **TUI Settings is now a real settings screen, and the theme picker is a popup.** The Settings section (index 4) was previously *just* the theme picker filling a two-panel layout. It is now a full-width, grouped settings screen (rendered like the Dashboard/Logs sections) listing the editable global settings, grouped Appearance / Logging / Editing / Indexing / Git / Others: **Theme** (opens the popup), **Log level**, **Log format**, **Strict edits**, **Show write diff**, **Rate limit / min**, **Topology**, **Quality analysis**, and — all editable — git **allow_writes** / **allow_destructive** / **allow_push**, **cache TTL** (duration presets), **cache max_size**, **lsp_query timeout** (duration presets), and **workspace auto_attach**. `↑↓`/`jk` move between rows, `←→`/`-`/`+` change the focused row (toggle / cycle / number / duration-preset), `enter`/`space` toggles or opens the theme popup. Because the TUI is a separate process from the daemon, only **Theme** (TUI-local, applied via `RebuildStyles()`) and **Log level** (pushed live to the running daemon over the existing control socket, mirroring `plumb log-level`) take effect immediately; every other row persists to the global config via the new `config.Save` and is marked `*` ("applies on next daemon start"). The theme picker is now a centred popup overlay that dims the whole screen behind it (`renderThemePicker` + `spliceOverlay`), split into **Dark** and **Light** sections with side/top/bottom padding; cursor navigation follows the grouped dark-then-light order and each move applies **and** saves the theme live (no revert), so the dimmed background re-renders in the highlighted theme as a live preview, and `esc`/`enter` closes. New generic writer `config.Save(apply func(*Config)) error` in `internal/config/config.go` (load → mutate → re-encode, refusing to clobber an unreadable file); `SaveTheme` is now a thin wrapper over it. New `internal/tui/model_settings_keys.go` holds the settings/theme-picker key handling; the old two-panel theme-picker code in `model_settings.go` is replaced. The screen is **scrollable** (keyboard `pgup`/`pgdown` and mouse wheel) with **mouse click-to-select**; rows are organised into aligned label/value/control columns under faded dotted group rules (Appearance / Logging / Editing / Indexing / Git / Others). The pinned footer is a two-line background bar: line 1 puts the `*` restart legend on the left and the navigation shortcuts (with brighter keys) on the right; line 2 always shows the status message (seeded to the active theme when Settings opens). A global **`ctrl+t`** shortcut opens the same theme picker from any section (documented in the help overlay, not the status bar). The theme picker gained faded dotted **Dark**/**Light** section rules, a `✓` after the active theme's name, and a matching background footer bar. Tests: `internal/config` `TestSave_PersistsFieldAndPreservesRest`; `internal/tui/model_settings_test.go` covers item building, navigation/clamping, toggle/cycle/number/duration edits with persistence, the dark/light grouping, logical-line structure, click-to-row mapping, and theme-picker apply-and-save.

## 0.7.8 (2026-05-21)

### Added
- **Topology fallback for `find_symbol`, `workspace_symbols`, and `list_symbols`.** When the language server errors or times out (e.g. it hit `[lsp_query].timeout` while still indexing), these three name-lookup tools now fall back to the topology index — when topology is enabled — instead of failing, turning an LSP stall into a fast, approximate answer. Fallback results are clearly annotated: `[topology fallback — LSP unavailable; results are approximate and may be stale. source=topology, mode=indexed-approximate]`. `find_symbol` and `list_symbols` use a new path-scoped `Store.SymbolsInFile` query; `workspace_symbols` uses the existing FTS5 `Search`. Wiring is via a nil-safe `WithTopologyFallback` setter (no constructor-signature change, so existing callers/tests are untouched); the fallback runs under the *original* request context rather than the expired LSP deadline, and is a deliberate no-op when topology is disabled or returns nothing — so the authoritative LSP error still surfaces in that case. The position/semantic tools (`get_definition`, `find_references`, `explain_symbol`, hierarchies, `rename_symbol`) are intentionally excluded: they need the type-checker and have no topology equivalent. Tests in `internal/tools/topology_fallback_test.go` index a temp workspace via the real pure-Go store and assert each tool falls back.

### Fixed
- **`config.SaveTheme` no longer clobbers an unreadable config file.** The TUI theme picker's save path called `Load()` and discarded its error, so a global `config.toml` with a syntax error was silently overwritten with defaults plus the new theme — destroying the user's recoverable settings. `SaveTheme` now aborts with a clear error when the existing file cannot be parsed; a *missing* file is still fine (first-save creates it). Added `TestSaveTheme_RefusesBrokenConfig`. Also dropped two stale doc comments in `internal/tui/theme.go` that referenced a `--theme` flag which was never implemented. Closes the 0.7.7 theme-system review; two non-blocking follow-ups (decouple `plumb config show` from the TUI package; `SaveTheme` re-encodes the full resolved config) recorded in `docs/todo.md`.
- **Cancelled LSP queries are now cancelled in the server, not just abandoned locally.** When an LSP call hits its `[lsp_query].timeout` (or is otherwise cancelled), `jsonrpc.Conn.Call` sends an LSP `$/cancelRequest` for that request id so the language server stops computing a result that would be discarded. Without it, a timed-out query kept running inside gopls; repeated retries could stack overlapping abandoned computations and inflate the server's CPU and memory. Adds `TestConn_ContextCancel_SendsCancelRequest`.

## 0.7.7 (2026-05-21)

### Added
- **Full theme system — 6 built-in themes, live picker, and config persistence.** The TUI now ships five additional built-in themes alongside the existing Nordico: `darcula` (JetBrains Darcula, warm oranges), `dracula` (dracula.github.io, purple accent), `gruvbox` (earthy browns and yellows), `github-light` (GitHub's clean light UI), `solarized-light` (Solarized classic). Navigate to Settings (`/` → Settings or `ctrl+5`/`alt+5`) to open the live theme picker: left panel lists all themes with cursor (`❯`) and saved (`✓`) markers; right panel shows colour swatches (`██` per semantic token) and a mini preview. Navigating the list applies the theme immediately; `esc` reverts to the theme active when Settings was entered; `enter`/`space` saves to `~/.config/plumb/config.toml`. The saved theme is applied automatically on the next `plumb` launch. `plumb config show` now uses the active theme's chroma style for TOML syntax highlighting instead of hardcoded `"nord"`. Foundation changes: `ContrastText color.Color` and `ChromaStyle string` added to `Theme` struct; hardcoded `lipgloss.Color("0")` replaced with `ActiveTheme.ContrastText` so light themes render legibly; four inline styles in `rightTabBar()` moved into `RebuildStyles()` exported vars. New `[ui]` config section (`theme`, default `"nordico"`). Tests: `TestTheme_AllFieldsSet` (reflect-based nil/empty check for every theme field), `TestTheme_AllSixThemesRegistered`, `TestIsLightTheme_Classification`, `TestSaveTheme_RoundTrip`.
- **Interactive session renaming via TUI.** Press `r` on a selected session in the Sessions panel to open a rename modal with real-time validation. Allowed character set: letters (any case), digits, and hyphens; max 25 characters. User input case is preserved. Modal shows validation feedback (✓ valid or ⚠ error reason), closes on Enter to save or Esc to cancel. Session name is immediately persisted to stats DB. Changes: `MaxNameLength` 16→25 in `internal/session/names.go`; `NormaliseName` accepts `[A-Za-z0-9-]` and preserves case; new `renameSessionModal` component in `internal/tui/model_rename_modal.go`; 'r' key handler in `model_keys.go`; modal integration in `model_update.go` and `model_render.go`. Validation rules: not empty, max 25 chars, start/end with letter or digit (no leading/trailing hyphens), no consecutive hyphens.

### Fixed
- **`git` denylist now includes `-c` and `-C`.** Both flags were listed in the original design spec but were absent from the implementation. `-c <key>=<val>` is a live config-injection vector on subcommands that pass unknown flags up to git's global parser; `-C <path>` changes the working directory and would bypass `findGitRoot`'s pinning.
- **`git stash <unknown>` now gives a helpful error.** Previously `git stash branch` reported `subcommand "stash" is not permitted`, which is wrong because `stash` itself is allowed. It now names the rejected sub-subcommand and lists the valid ones.
- **Project-config git changes are now logged.** `applyProjectConfig` was already logging edits and walk config changes via `slog.Info`; git config changes (`allow_writes`, `allow_destructive`, `allow_push`) are now included in the same log entry.
- **`read_file` / `read_symbol` no longer silently discard `fileSHA256` errors.** The error is now logged at warn level and the `sha256=` field is omitted from the header rather than emitted as an empty value. Clients that parse the header by key are unaffected; clients that passed an empty sha back as `expected_sha` now get a consistent "no field" experience.
- **`transaction_apply` `expected_sha` test coverage added.** `TestTransaction_RespectsExpectedSha` covers both the correct-hash-passes and wrong-hash-rejected paths; only `edit_file` had this coverage before.
- **`make integration-test` timeout raised from 2 m to 10 m.** The 2-minute limit was too tight when jdtls is installed locally; CI already used 10 minutes.
- **LSP tool calls can no longer hang the MCP client.** Every LSP-backed tool (`workspace_symbols`, `find_symbol`, `get_definition`, `explain_symbol`, `list_symbols`, `find_references`, `read_symbol`, `call_hierarchy`, `type_hierarchy`, `rename_symbol`, and the four symbol-edit tools) now runs under a configurable deadline. Previously these tools passed the daemon-lifetime context (cancelled only on SIGTERM) straight through to `jsonrpc.Conn.Call`, which blocks on the response channel — so a still-indexing or wedged language server made the call wait indefinitely until the *client* gave up (e.g. Claude Desktop's 4-minute timeout, surfaced as an opaque "MCP server unresponsive" error). Now a slow server fails fast with an actionable message (`… language server did not respond within 30s (it may still be indexing the workspace — retry shortly)`). New global `[lsp_query]` config section with `timeout` (default `30s`, `0` disables), overridable via `PLUMB_LSP_QUERY_TIMEOUT`, shown with provenance in `plumb config show`. The deadline is applied at the tool layer (`withLSPDeadline` / `lspTimeoutErr` in `internal/tools/lsp_deadline.go`, mirroring `applySearchDeadline`) and is a no-op when the caller's context already carries a deadline, so it never shortens the cold-start `initialize`/`initialized` handshake (which runs on the adapter before the proxy is live). Separately, `jsonrpc.Conn.Call` now logs any request whose round-trip exceeds 2 s at WARN (`jsonrpc: slow call method=… elapsed=…`) so a slow server is visible in `daemon.log` instead of failing silently. Tests: helper unit tests (`lsp_deadline_test.go`), tool-level timeout tests against a blocking mock (`lsp_timeout_test.go`), and config resolution/validation tests (`internal/config/lsp_query_test.go`).

### Changed
- **Unified git tool — `git_add` and `git_commit` folded into a single tiered `git` tool.** The git surface is no longer split across a read-only `git` plus separate write tools; one `git` tool now covers the full status→add→commit→branch→push flow, gated by a tiered allowlist so flexibility does not compromise safety. Tiers: **read** (status, log, diff, show, blame, shortlog, plus branch/tag/stash listing) always run; **write** (add via typed `files`, commit via typed `message` → `-m`, switch, mv, branch/tag create, stash push/pop) require `[git] allow_writes` (default on); **destructive** (reset, clean, checkout, restore, rebase, revert, branch/tag delete, stash drop) require `allow_destructive` + `confirm:true`; **network** (push, fetch, pull) require `allow_push` + `confirm:true`. Tier classification is arg-aware and safe-biased (e.g. `restore --staged` is a write, but `restore <path>` is destructive; `checkout -b` is a write, any other checkout is destructive). New `[git]` config section (`allow_writes`, `allow_destructive`, `allow_push`, `protected_branches`) resolvable globally, per-project, and via `PLUMB_GIT_ALLOW_WRITES`/`_DESTRUCTIVE`/`_PUSH` env vars. Security invariants: the subcommand always leads the argv so global flags in `args` cannot reconfigure git, a denylist rejects `--git-dir`/`--work-tree`/`--namespace`/`--upload-pack`/`--receive-pack`/`--exec-path`, force-pushing a `protected_branches` entry (default `main`/`master`) and pushing to an ad-hoc URL are always refused, and unknown subcommands (`merge`, `rm`, `config`, `filter-branch`, `clone`, `submodule`, …) are rejected. No shell is ever invoked. **Breaking:** the `git_add` and `git_commit` MCP tools are removed — call `git` with `subcommand:"add"` (typed `files`) or `subcommand:"commit"` (typed `message`) instead. Tool count 49 → 47.

## 0.7.6 (2026-05-21)

### Added
- **Plumb Topology: Phase 2 — call edges, new tools, TypeScript extractor, and indexer hardening.** Completes the original topology vision across five work tiers:
  - *Tier 0 — Definition of Done benchmarks.* Two new `//go:build integration` tests in `internal/topology/benchmark_test.go`: `TestDoD6_TopologyQueryLatency` (warms both gopls and topology, then compares per-query `workspace/symbol` lookup latency; logs the numbers and asserts an absolute latency bound — the original DoD-6 "≥5× faster than LSP" target is **not** met, measured ~1.2× warm and slower cold, and is tracked in `docs/todo.md` → "Topology — remaining Phase 2 gaps") and `TestDoD7_ConcurrentSearchNoBusy` (100 concurrent `Search` goroutines while the indexer writes, asserts zero errors and zero races under `-race`). Also note: Phase 2 items 5 (LSP fallback) and 6 (TUI/doctor topology visibility) were deferred, not shipped.
  - *Tier 1 — Call-edge emission.* Go AST extractor now emits `EdgeCalls` for intra-file function calls (`ast.CallExpr` walk, confidence 1.0, no self-loops, cross-file calls excluded). Python extractor emits `EdgeCalls` via a second-pass line scanner tracking current-function indent (confidence 0.6, source `"heuristic"`). Three new tests for Go (`TestExtract_CallEdges_IntraFile`, `TestExtract_CallEdges_NoSelfLoop`, `TestExtract_CallEdges_CrossFileNotEmitted`); Python test gaps filled: `TestExtract_AsyncDefIsFunction`, `TestExtract_ContainmentEdgeConfidence` (asserts 0.8), `TestExtract_CommentOnlyFile`, `TestExtract_CallEdges_IntraFile` (asserts confidence=0.6, source="heuristic").
  - *Tier 2 — Three new MCP tools.* `topology_impact`: bidirectional BFS blast-radius analysis — two sub-graphs (outward: what a symbol depends on; inward: what depends on it), inputs `name`/`depth`/`max_nodes`/`max_bytes`/`edge_kinds`, hard caps and budget truncation same as `topology_explore`. `topology_affected`: given `files` or `symbols`, traverses inward edges to collect dependents then separates `KindTest` nodes into a "likely affected tests" section — use after writing to suggest which tests to run. `topology_routes`: framework-aware entry-point scanner matching Go `http.HandleFunc`/mux patterns, Cobra `Run`/`RunE`, Python `@app.route`/`@router.get`; confidence 0.65–0.75; mandatory confidence annotation in every result. `Direction` enum (`DirectionBoth`/`DirectionOutward`/`DirectionInward`) added to `ExploreOpts` and threaded through BFS `expandFrontier`/`collectNeighbours`. All three tools registered in `handleConn`; unit tests cover nil-store degradation, defaults, and format helpers.
  - *Tier 3 — TypeScript/JavaScript extractor.* New `internal/topology/extractors/typescript` package; line-by-line regex scanner for `.ts`/`.tsx`/`.js`/`.jsx`/`.mjs`/`.cjs`. Extracts: `function`/`async function`, arrow functions (`const foo = () =>`), `class`/`interface`/`type alias`, ES `import`/CommonJS `require`, Express `app.get/post/put/delete/patch/use` (synthesised route nodes), Jest/Mocha/Vitest `describe`/`it`/`test` blocks (`KindTest`), class method containment edges (confidence 0.7). Brace-depth class tracking uses strict `<` (not `<=`) to keep class context active across multi-method bodies. Minified files (`.min.`/`.bundle.`) skipped. Registered in `buildExtractors()`. Tests cover class methods with imports, empty file, minified skip, test blocks, ES/CJS import, Express route, containment-edge confidence, extension list, language/path round-trip.
  - *Tier 4 — Indexer hardening.* Three improvements: (a) `drain` now returns `[]indexOp` using a per-path coalescing map (last op per unique path wins — fixes multi-file write drops where only the last file was processed); (b) `isStale` now checks both `mtime_ns` and `content_hash` (was mtime-only — fixes backup-restore edge case where mtime regresses); (c) periodic resync wired via nil-channel ticker pattern: when `ResyncIntervalMinutes > 0` a ticker fires and enqueues `opResync` only when the indexer is idle (avoids stacking resyncs). Tests updated: `TestIndexer_Drain_PerPathCoalescing` replaces `TestIndexer_Drain_ReturnsLast` and asserts correct per-path coalescing; `TestIndexer_IsStale_*` updated for new hash parameter.
- **Plumb Topology: Phase 1 persistent semantic index.** New `internal/topology` package implements a SQLite/FTS5 semantic graph at `<workspace>/.plumb/topology.db`. Go AST extractor (`go/parser`+`go/ast`, no CGo) and Python regex extractor (line-by-line `bufio.Scanner`) produce `Node` and `Edge` records that a daemon-owned background `Indexer` persists with mtime-based staleness detection. The indexer coalesces rapid writes via a bounded queue (cap 256) and skips vendor, node_modules, `.git`, testdata, `.plumb`, dist, build, and `__pycache__` directories. FTS5 full-text table (`topology_fts`) stores name, name_tokens (split from camelCase/snake_case/kebab-case), qualified name, signature, docstring, path, and kind for BM25-ranked search. BFS neighbourhood traversal (`topology_explore`) supports configurable depth, node, and byte budgets with hard caps (depth ≤ 4, nodes ≤ 200, bytes ≤ 100 000) and reports truncation. Three new MCP tools: `topology_status` (index health), `topology_search` (FTS5 ranked query with kind/language filters and snippet extraction), `topology_explore` (bounded BFS neighbourhood). All three degrade gracefully when topology is disabled or the workspace is not yet attached. New `[topology]` config section with `enabled` (default false), `resync_on_attach`, `exclude_patterns`, `max_file_size_bytes` (default 512 KiB), and `resync_interval_minutes`. `write_file`, `edit_file`, and `transaction_apply` enqueue written paths for re-indexing via `WriteDeps.TopologyNotify`. WAL mode with `busy_timeout=5000` and short per-file transactions ensures MCP read queries never block on indexing writes. Unit tests cover schema/WAL/FTS5, search ranking, BFS truncation, and nil-store graceful degradation.
- **Client-aware token-savings model.** `internal/stats/savings.go` now uses per-client profiles (`claude-desktop`, `claude-code`, `codex`, `gemini`, `unknown`) instead of a single static `altCost` table. Each profile assigns conservative per-tool fallback estimates based on the client's native capabilities (e.g. Claude Code can run `rg` directly, so `search_in_files` is near-zero savings; Claude Desktop has no filesystem access, so the same tool scores higher). A single `normaliseClient(name)` function canonicalises all aliases. `TokensSavedForClient(tool, clientName, outputBytes)` selects the matching profile; the old `TokensSaved` wrapper routes to `unknown` for backward compatibility. Schema migrated v5→6→7 to add `client_name` and `client_version` columns to `tool_calls`; both `Record()` and the aggregation queries are client-aware. 7 new unit tests in `internal/stats/savings_test.go`.
- **Code-quality differential after writes.** `write_file`, `edit_file`, and `transaction_apply` now append a compact "code quality" section to their response when golangci-lint finds issues in the written file. Plumb runs golangci-lint asynchronously by default (background mode) so writes never block; sync mode is opt-in via `[quality] mode = "sync"`. Results are cached per file and invalidated on mtime change. New packages: `internal/quality` (language-agnostic `Analyser` interface + `Runner`), `internal/quality/golangcilint` (subprocess analyser). New config block `[quality]` with `enabled` (default false), `mode`, `analysers`, `timeout_ms`, `max_findings_per_file`. Wired into `WriteDeps` as a nil-safe `QualityReportFn`. The runner is per-MCP-connection to match the existing session model. Disabled by default until proven on diverse repos. Tests cover parser, queue coalescing, cache invalidation, sync/background dispatch, and overflow formatting.
- **Memory TUI section.** Press `/` → Memory (or `ctrl+3`/`alt+3`) to open the new Memory section. Left panel lists all workspace memories with name and description; right panel shows metadata (name, description, size, paths) and the full scrollable body. `j/k`, `pgup/pgdn`, and `tab` navigate; mouse clicks select. Memories refresh on the standard 2-second poll cycle.
- **Project-config hot-reload.** The daemon watches `<workspace>/.plumb/config.toml` per session and reapplies it within ~30 s of an mtime change — strict mode, write rate limit, and walk config take effect without reconnecting. A background goroutine (one per session, guarded by `sync.Once`) polls every 30 s; reloads are deduplicated against the last-applied mtime (seeded at attach by `applyProjectConfig`), and the watcher exits on session close via the per-session context. Topology/quality enablement and workspace auto-attach are resolved at attach and are not part of the hot-reload set. Tests in `internal/cli/config_watcher_test.go` cover dedup, reload-on-change, unresolved-workspace skip, single-start, mtime seeding, and `-race` thread-safety.

### Changed
- **`SavingsLabel` — client-aware savings framing in `session_start`.** `stats.SavingsLabel(clientName string) string` is a new exported function that returns `"capabilities enabled"` for Claude Desktop clients and `"tokens saved"` for all others. `session_start`'s "Most-used tools" section now appends a savings summary line (`~4.5k capabilities enabled` / `~4.5k tokens saved`) when accumulated savings for the top-5 tools are non-zero. This surfaces the value of plumb to the AI agent at session start, with the correct framing for clients that have no native filesystem fallback.
- **`docs/mcp-tools.md` — client capabilities and fallback behaviour table.** Added a "Client capabilities and fallback behaviour" section at the top of the tool catalogue with a four-client comparison table (Claude Desktop / Claude Code / Codex / Gemini CLI) and two implication notes: one on error messages (do not suggest native alternatives to Claude Desktop users) and one on savings framing (`capabilities enabled` vs `tokens saved`).
- **File line-length guideline raised from ~400 to ~600 lines.** The previous limit was too tight for self-contained TUI sections and complex tool files. The gocyclo-15 and ~600 limits are now the enforced quality gates.

### Fixed
- `refreshDashboard` cyclomatic complexity (was 16, above the gocyclo-15 limit). Decomposed into `refreshDashboardBuckets`, `refreshDaemBuckets`, and `refreshDashboardProject`.

## 0.7.4 (2026-05-21)

### Added
- **`git_add` tool — stage explicit file paths.** `files` (required list of absolute paths), `repo` (optional, derived from first file if omitted). Runs `git add -- <files>`; no glob expansion. Returns a staged-file summary (`git diff --cached --name-status`). Counts against the session write rate limit. 5 unit tests.
- **`git_commit` tool — commit whatever is currently staged.** `message` (required), `repo` (optional). Commits the current index as-is — call `git_add` first to stage. Pre-commit hooks always run; no `--no-verify` escape hatch. Returns short hash + subject. Counts against the session write rate limit. 5 unit tests.
- **`git_init` tool — initialise a git repository.** `path` (required, created if absent), `init_plumb` (optional bool). When `init_plumb: true`, also creates `.plumb/context.md` so plumb attaches on the next session; existing `context.md` is never overwritten. 5 unit tests.

## 0.7.3

### Changed
- **`diagnostics` tool — accept multiple URIs in a single call.** The tool now accepts `uris: []string` alongside the old scalar `uri` (kept for backward compatibility — treated as `uris:[uri]`). Three call modes: omit `uris` or pass `[]` for all files; one URI for a single-file query; multiple URIs to fan out and merge results in one response. Description updated. `docs/mcp-tools.md` updated. 5 new unit tests cover: single via `uris`, multi-file, multi-file with one untracked, all-clean multi-file, and scalar `uri` backward-compat.

### Fixed
- **TUI Dashboard activity chart refreshes every 30 s to track growing time window.** Bucket boundaries are now re-queried when a new tool call is recorded, the terminal is resized, or 30 seconds have elapsed — whichever comes first. This keeps the chart current as the uptime/lifetime windows grow, while avoiding the per-2-second-tick jitter caused by bucket-boundary drift.
- **TUI Dashboard activity chart shape changes with no new data.** `refreshDashboard` re-queried `Activity()` every 2 s using the live `time.Since(firstCallAt)` window. As the window grew, `bucketMs` grew with it, causing calls near bucket boundaries to hop between buckets and the chart to visibly "breathe" even with no new tool calls. Bucket arrays are now cached by call count and chart width; they are only re-queried when `dashLifetimeCalls` or `activity.Calls` actually increases, or when the terminal is resized. The chart is stable between tool calls.
- **TUI Dashboard activity chart — outlier session compresses all other activity to 1 pixel.** `dashBuildGrid` scaled the y-axis against the absolute bucket maximum. One busy session (e.g. 300 calls in a single bucket) set `maxV = 300`, compressing every other bucket to 1 pixel and making the chart look flat with a single spike. `maxV` is now computed as the P90 of non-zero bucket values (floor 3): the top 10 % of buckets clip at full height, while the remaining 90 % are properly distributed across the pixel range.
- **TUI Dashboard activity chart — sparse data invisible at default scale.** `dashBuildGrid` used a `maxV` floor of 10, meaning a 1-call bucket rendered as just 1 pixel out of 8 — effectively invisible for short uptime sessions with low call density. Lowered the floor to 3: a 1-call bucket now renders at 2 pixels (25 % height); a 2-call bucket at 5 pixels (62 %); ≥ 3 calls reaches full height. Data-rich charts (actual peak >> 3) are unaffected — the actual max still dominates `maxV`.
- **TUI Dashboard Activity Graph Height and Resolution.** The dashboard activity graph height is now capped at 8 pixels instead of 7, making full use of the braille character set. The horizontal resolution has also been doubled to utilize both dots in a braille character independently, providing a more detailed view of activity spikes.

## 0.7.2

### Fixed
- **gopls PATH augmentation for GUI-launched daemons.** When plumb is launched by a GUI application (Claude Desktop, Cursor) on macOS, it inherits launchd's stripped `PATH` (`/usr/bin:/bin:/usr/sbin:/sbin`), which omits `/usr/local/bin` and `/opt/homebrew/bin` — the typical Homebrew installation prefix for `go`, `gopls`, and other tools. Without `go` on PATH, gopls cannot locate the module cache and reports every import — including stdlib packages like `context` and `fmt` — as "could not import". The `envFor` helper in `internal/cli/pool.go` now always augments PATH before spawning the LSP subprocess: existing PATH entries are preserved first, then `/etc/paths` and all `/etc/paths.d/*` files are read (the same sources `path_helper(8)` uses), then `/usr/local/bin`, `/opt/homebrew/bin`, and `/opt/homebrew/sbin` are appended, deduplicating throughout. Per-language `[lsp.go] env` config overrides still apply on top, so explicit config wins.

### Changed
- **`copy_file` tool + `rename_file` move clarity.** New `copy_file(from, to, overwrite, dirty_ok)` tool: preserves source permissions, cross-device safe (safeWrite), two-path deadlock-safe locks, `FileCreated` LSP notification. `rename_file` description updated to say it is the primary move tool and points to `copy_file` for duplication. Docs updated: `mcp-tools.md`, `AGENTS.md` (count 34→35). 8 unit tests.
